601 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Hunt v. Daley


No. 1-95-1779


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


286 Ill. App. 3d 766; 677 N.E.2d 456; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 66; 222 Ill. Dec. 253



February 19, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE ELLIS REID, JUDGE PRESIDING.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of December 30, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 996.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of Circuit Court of Cook County reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and city officials, sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held that Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 8-20-200(c) was unconstitutional. Under § 8-20-200(c) the city prohibited appellee gun owner from registering his handguns for failure to re-register the guns every two years prior thereto, causing him to forfeit his right to possess the guns within the city.


OVERVIEW: The gun owner attempted to re-register his handguns. The city denied his applications on the ground that he failed to renew previous registrations upon their expiration in violation of Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 8-20-200(a) (1990). The gun owner appealed the decision to the city license commission, which also denied re-registration. The gun owner filed an action for administrative review. The trial court reversed the city's denial of the gun owner's applications, holding that § 8-20-200(a) was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's decision. The court held that: (1) the trial court was acting within its discretionary powers in deciding to hear the constitutional issue although it was not raised in the administrative proceedings; (2) the re-registration provision of the ordinance met the rational basis test where the court could conceive of several purposes for the ordinance such as to more readily associate a handgun with its owner's current address; and (3) the existence of less onerous alternative means of securing those interests was not by itself sufficient to render the ordinance unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision, which found the city's re-registration requirement under its gun ban ordinance to be unconstitutional. The gun owner could be denied the right to re-register his handguns where the court could conceive of a rational basis for the re-registration requirement.

 

602 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Collins v. Chicago Transit Auth.


No. 1-96-2442


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


286 Ill. App. 3d 737; 677 N.E.2d 449; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 59; 222 Ill. Dec. 246



February 18, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 96 L 01217. The Honorable Robert J. Quinn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant passenger sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motion of appellee Chicago Transit Authority (CTA) to dismiss the passenger's complaint against the CTA and another passenger who assaulted her while she was on one of the CTA's trains. The trial court dismissed the action based on the immunity granted CTA under the Metropolitan Transit Authority Act, 70 Ill. Comp. Stat. 3605/27.


OVERVIEW: After a fellow passenger assaulted the passenger on a CTA train, the passenger filed a complaint against the assailant and the CTA. Pursuant to the CTA's motion, the trial court dismissed it from the action based on its immunity under the Metropolitan Transit Authority Act. The passenger argued on appeal that, notwithstanding any immunity it may have, the CTA was liable for her injuries because it owed her a special duty. The passenger claimed that the CTA breached its duty of care by failing to provide security guards, by failing to institute appropriate security measures to protect her and other female passengers, by failing to properly train personnel regarding procedures following an attack on a passenger, by failing to implement proper procedures to notify police and security personnel when passengers were in danger, and by failing to stop assaults. The court held that the passenger's allegations were insufficient to create an issue of whether a special duty existed because they failed to establish that the CTA had direct and immediate control over her and did not allege that a public employee created a position of peril for her.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the passenger's case against the CTA on the grounds of immunity.

 

603 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Human Rights Comm'n


No. 1-96-0317


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


286 Ill. App. 3d 508; 676 N.E.2d 315; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 46; 221 Ill. Dec. 794



February 7, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Review of Order of The Illinois Human Rights Commission. Honorable Helen W. Gunnarsson, Administrative Law Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee filed an administrative sexual harassment and unequal pay complaint against respondent employer. Respondent Illinois Human Rights Commission (commission) dismissed the employee's complaint because it was filed prior to the expiration of the Illinois Department of Human Rights (department) 300-day investigation period as provided by 775 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7A-102(G)(1). The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: An employee filed an administrative complaint with the department, alleging that the employer harassed her and gave her unequal pay on the basis of her sex. The commission granted the employer's motion to dismiss the complaint because it was filed prior to the expiration of the 300-day investigation period as provided by 775 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7A-102(G)(1). The employee appealed, contending that she relied on information provided by the department to file the complaint and that the 30-day post-investigation appeal window period of 775 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7A-102(G)(2) should have been tolled. On appeal, the court held that the commission's determination that the employee's complaint was untimely was correct and that equitable principles did not toll the 30-day appeal window period. The commission's interpretation, that 775 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7A-102(G)(1) required the employee to sign and notarize her charge under oath or affirmation pursuant to Ill. Admin. Code tit. 56, § 2520.330, and that the investigation period ran from the date that the employee filed a charge containing her notarized signature under oath or affirmation, was logical and correct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the employee's sexual harassment complaint and remanded the case to the department for further proceedings.

 

604 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Rosewell v. J.C. Penney Co. (In re Rosewell)


No. 1-95-0917


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


286 Ill. App. 3d 814; 677 N.E.2d 443; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 49; 222 Ill. Dec. 240



February 7, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 18, 1997. Released for Publication March 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Misc. No. 86-34. 1985 Objection No. 721. The Honorable Michael J. Murphy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order entered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied its request for a reduction in the assessed valuation of certain real property and partial refund of taxes paid in full under protest to appellee collector.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied the taxpayer's objection to the application of the collector for judgment and order of sale, finding that the taxpayer had failed to demonstrate actual or constructive fraud by the taxing authority and denied the objection. On appeal, the taxpayer argued that a 1995 amendment to the Property Tax Code, 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 200/23-15 applied to the case and eliminated the burden of proving constructive fraud. In the alternative, it argued that the 1994 amendment controlled and similarly removed the requirement of demonstrating fraud. Finally, it contended that even if the statutory amendments were inapplicable, it made an adequate showing of fraud. The court held that: 1) because the amendments interfered with vested rights, the controversy had to be decided under the Act as it existed at the time of trial; 2) in light of the presumptive validity of the assessment and the taxpayer's heavy burden, the trial court did not err by failing to shift the burden to the taxing authority to come forward with evidence in support of the assessment; and 3) there existed insufficient evidence to support an inference of fraud.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court in favor of the collector.

 

605 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Moran v. City of Chicago


No. 1-94-3662


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


286 Ill. App. 3d 746; 676 N.E.2d 1316; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 42; 222 Ill. Dec. 112



February 5, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 26, 1997. Released for Publication March 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE KENNETH L. GILLIS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff detainee appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed counts alleging that defendant City of Chicago and police officers owed plaintiff a special duty and that they acted willful and wantonly in failing to protect plaintiff, and that defendants had deprived him of his civil rights guaranteed under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, in his action to recover for injuries he sustained while being questioned by defendants.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff detainee brought an action against defendant City of Chicago and police officers for injuries he sustained while being questioned by defendants. Upon defendants' motions, the trial court dismissed plaintiff's tort claims based upon the immunity provisions of the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act (Act), 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 10/4-102, 2-204, 2-202, and 2-109, and his claims of deprivation of his civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court affirmed the trial court's order. Plaintiff did not establish that defendants owed him a special duty under the Act, and failed to show that their conduct was willful and wanton, that they were indifferent to, or disregarded his safety. The court also held that plaintiff failed to allege deliberate or reckless indifference to his liberty and personal security interests sufficient to sustain his § 1983 claim. Finally, the court held that plaintiff failed to state a cause of action for denial or impairment of his right of access to the courts, because he failed to show that he suffered a significant detriment as a result of defendants' objectionable conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which dismissed plaintiff detainee's causes of action against defendant City of Chicago and police officers, alleging that they owed him a special duty, and deprived him of his civil rights guaranteed under the Fourteenth Amendment, holding that defendants were protected by the immunity provisions of the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act.

Calamari v. Drammis


No. 1-96-1102


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


286 Ill. App. 3d 420; 676 N.E.2d 281; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 35; 221 Ill. Dec. 760



February 4, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 95 L 10609. The Honorable Paddy H. McNamara, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed her amended complaint with prejudice and denied her motion to reconsider. The patient filed an action against defendant doctor alleging that he was negligent in performing plastic surgery on her.


OVERVIEW: The patient voluntarily dismissed her initial complaint because of her failure to file the attorney's affidavit of merit and physician's report required by 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-622 (1992). After the amendment of § 2-622 in 1995, the patient filed an amended complaint. The trial court dismissed the complaint with prejudice for failure to comply with the amended § 2-622. On appeal, the patient contended that the old version of § 2-622 should have been applied to her complaint, rather than the amended version. The court found that because the patient's refiled complaint was filed after the effective date of the amendment and was not pending at the time it became effective, the amended version of § 2-622 was properly applied. The court determined that the patient had not shown good cause for her failure to provide the necessary documents under § 2-622 and that the trial court properly considered the patient's delays and lack of any good cause for them in dismissing the complaint. The court concluded that under the amended § 2-622, the patient could not obtain an extension to provide an affidavit of merit and physician's report, which she failed to attach to her amended complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court dismissing the patient's negligence claim against the doctor with prejudice.

People v. Cully


No. 2-95-1381


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


286 Ill. App. 3d 155; 675 N.E.2d 1017; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 14; 221 Ill. Dec. 593


August 27, 1996, SUBMITTED  
January 17, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rule 23 Order Redesignated Opinion and Ordered Published January 17, 1997. Released for Publication February 20, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 95--CF--261. Honorable Conrad F. Floeter, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of practicing medicine without a license.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was self-employed as a licensed physician. The Illinois Department of Professional Regulation informed defendant that it would not renew his license because of defendant's failure to make timely payments on his student loan. Defendant continued to practice medicine. Defendant was convicted of practicing medicine without a license. On appeal, defendant claimed that it was unconstitutional for the state to use an underlying statute that allowed the nonrenewal of a medical license when the licensee has defaulted on an educational loan in conjunction with Medical Practice Act of 1987 § 50, 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 60/50, that the trial court erred when it refused to give certain jury instructions, and that prosecutorial misconduct denied defendant a fair trial. The court held that (1) 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 60/50 and § 60(5) of Act 2105 of the Civil Administrative Code, 20 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 2105/60(5), bore a rational relationship to the purpose of the Medical Practice Act; (2) the trial court erred when it refused to give the jury instruction on mental state; and (3) the prosecutor's comments were improper, but they were not substantially prejudicial to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant.

Texaco-Cities Serv. Pipeline Co. v. McGaw


No. 1-95-1022


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


286 Ill. App. 3d 529; 675 N.E.2d 1004; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 20; 221 Ill. Dec. 580



January 17, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 20, 1997. Released for Publication February 28, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 93-L-50312. Honorable Alexander P. White, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) affirming a determination of defendant, director of the Illinois Department of Revenue (department), that the taxpayer's proceeds from the sale of a pipeline and associated realty were business income. The department appealed from the trial court's apportionment determination.


OVERVIEW: After the taxpayer sold a portion of its pipeline, the department determined that the proceeds from the sale constituted business income and issued a notice of deficiency. The taxpayer filed a protest to the notice, and a hearing was held before an administrative law judge (ALJ), which concluded that the income was business income subject to apportionment under the special one-factor formula under 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/304(d)(2) (1994). The taxpayer sought administrative review, and the trial court upheld the determination of the ALJ. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the proceeds from the sale of the pipeline constituted business income under the functional test because the pipeline was used in the taxpayer's business operations. Further, the taxpayer failed to introduce any evidence that the sale of the pipeline did not contribute to the taxpayer's continuing business operations as a whole. With regard to the department's appeal, the court found that the plain language of § 304(d) did not clearly provide for an activity analysis and found that the proceeds should not have been apportioned under the one-factor formula.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the order holding that the proceeds from the sale of the taxpayer's property were business income. The court reversed the portion of the order apportioning the proceeds under the one-factor formula.

Downey v. Wood Dale Park Dist.


No. 2-96-0287


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


286 Ill. App. 3d 194; 675 N.E.2d 973; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 3; 221 Ill. Dec. 549


September 20, 1996, SUBMITTED  
January 8, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 20, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. Nos. 95--L--0080, 95--L--1382. Honorable Paul Noland, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff independent administrator of the estate of deceased autistic minor appealed from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which granted defendant park district's motion to dismiss and found that § 3--108(a) immunity, 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/3--108(a) (1994), applied to defendant park district and that no special duty existed.


OVERVIEW: The court upheld the trial court's finding that the park district was entitled to immunity. The court determined that the park district's mere knowledge of the deceased child's disability of autism did not constitute "unique awareness of a particular danger" sufficient to impose a special duty exception to the immunity statute. The court determined that plaintiff did not allege sufficient facts to satisfy the first element of the special duty doctrine. The element of direct and immediate control was lacking. The court relied on the fact that the legislature had provided municipalities with immunity for an injury caused by a failure to supervise on public property, 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/3--108(a) (1994).


OUTCOME: Judgment dismissing the suit against the park district was affirmed.

People v. Walensky


No. 1-95-1533


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


286 Ill. App. 3d 82; 675 N.E.2d 952; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 997; 221 Ill. Dec. 528



December 31, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 14, 1997. Released for Publication February 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Dennis J. Porter, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County is affirmed. Granted state's motion and assess defendant $ 150 as costs for this appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant on an amended charge of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, and denied his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. Defendant contended that the trial court did not have jurisdiction to entertain the state's motion to reconsider its order suppressing the evidence seized pursuant to the search warrant, since that motion was filed more than 30 days after the entry of the June 29 order. Defendant further contended that the trial court erred in granting the motion to reconsider under the "good faith" exception to the exclusionary rule. Defendant challenged his conviction on the grounds that the evidence presented was insufficient to support his conviction. The court disagreed with defendant's contention that the trial court erred in denying him an evidentiary hearing regarding the alleged bad faith of the police officers. The court believed that it was not against the manifest weight of the evidence for a trier of fact to have found that defendant possessed the narcotics in question beyond a reasonable doubt. Finally, the court concluded that a rational trier of fact could well have found the presence of the element of intent to deliver beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: Judgment of conviction was affirmed.

People v. Orsby


No. 2-95-1286


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


286 Ill. App. 3d 142; 675 N.E.2d 237; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 968; 221 Ill. Dec. 330


September 23, 1996, SUBMITTED  
December 30, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 95-CF-167. Honorable Henry C. Tonigan III, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance, unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, and armed violence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawful possession of a controlled substance, unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, and armed violence. Defendant raised several arguments on review. The court found that the police officers had probable cause to stop the defendant in his car because they observed the defendant's vehicle swerve, that he failed to signal for a turn, and that his vehicle had only one headlight. The court also found that the defendant was not entitled to a disclosure of the state's informant because the defendant failed to offer any explanation as to how production of the confidential informant would allow him to rebut the testimony about prior drug transactions. Finally, the court found that the defendant's conviction for armed violence was proper because the handgun that was recovered from the defendant was next to his thigh and the ammunition was in his coat pocket, thereby giving him immediate access to a weapon. The trial court's decision was affirmed in all regards except for sentencing, which was remanded for a new sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: Trial court's decision was affirmed in all regards except for sentencing. Defendant's conviction of armed violence was proper because gun was found in his vehicle next to his thigh and the ammunition was in his coat pocket.

 

612 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Grano


No. 2-96-0249


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


286 Ill. App. 3d 278; 676 N.E.2d 248; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 969; 221 Ill. Dec. 727



December 30, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 4, 1997. Released for Publication March 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 94--CF--644. Honorable Thomas E. Callum, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the owner and head instructor of a karate school, was accused by one of his teenage students of having a sexual relationship with her. He appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which found him guilty of criminal sexual assault under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12--13(a)(4) (1994) and sentenced him to four years in prison.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found that the trial court improperly barred evidence under the rape shield statute, and reversed for a new trial. The defense counsel wished to impeach the victim with the testimony of three witnesses who would testify that the victim told them that she had sex with three other adult men and three witnesses (the other adult men) who would testify that they never had sex with the victim. The victim's prior sexual activity or reputation is generally inadmissible under § 115--7 of Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115--7(a) (1995). The trial court interpreted "sexual activity or the reputation" of the alleged victim to include her prior accusations of sexual misconduct. The court found, however, that the defense sought only to introduce evidence of the prior allegedly false statements for impeachment purposes. The statute was not designed to preclude the admission of all evidence relating to sex. The legislature intended to exclude the actual sexual history of the victim, not her prior accusations. Because there was no contention that the complainant ever engaged in sexual activity, there was no need to invoke the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new trial. The court found that the trial court's erroneously applied the rape shield statute to the facts of the case, but found in favor of the state on all other issues raised by the defendant.

Allen v. Board of Trustees of Community College Dist. No. 508


1-93-3108


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


285 Ill. App. 3d 1031; 675 N.E.2d 187; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 983; 221 Ill. Dec. 280



December 26, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Edward C. Hofert, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants teachers sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment to appellees, a board of trustees, the chairman of the board, the chancellor of the City Colleges of Chicago, and the county, in appellants' wrongful discharge action.


OVERVIEW: Appellants resigned after appellees served them with a notice of hearing and written notice that appellees were considering a recommendation that appellants be dismissed for cause. The charge was that appellants awarded grades to phantom students registered for their classes but who never attended in an effort to keep their classes from being closed. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that because appellees had a prima facie basis to discharge appellants, appellants' resignations, which were given to avoid dismissal, could not be considered to been given under duress. The court held that even if appellees' belief that appellants had committed a federal crime by falsely certifying the number of students in their class to receive payment was incorrect, appellants were not coerced into resigning. Appellees had an indisputable basis for bringing dismissal proceedings, and appellants had the choice to contest those charges or resign. The court found that appellants failed to allege or show proof of the existence of any custom or college policy or of any causal connection between such a policy or custom and their alleged constitutional injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's grant of summary judgment to appellees in appellants' wrongful discharge action.

Timothy Christian Sch. v. Village of W. Springs


No. 1-95-3475


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


285 Ill. App. 3d 949; 675 N.E.2d 168; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 977; 221 Ill. Dec. 261



December 24, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 16, 1997. Released for Publication February 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Thomas Durkin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developer sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) in favor of appellee village.


OVERVIEW: In 1982, as part of an earlier litigation settlement, the developer gave the village approximately one acre of property and agreed with the village to make improvements on the property and flood control. In 1994, the village entered into a contract to sell the one-acre parcel to another company for a townhome development. The developer filed a petition for contempt and sought to enjoin the sale. It argued that the intent of the 1982 agreement was that the land would be used as a drainage and flood control area in perpetuity. The developer appealed the trial court's denial of its requested relief. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment from the trial court. The court held that although drainage was clearly the parties' intent in 1982, there was no evidence whatsoever of an intent that the one-acre parcel would remain open space in perpetuity. The court further held that there was nothing in the record stating that drainage was currently a problem or that the townhome development would create a drainage problem.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court in favor of the village.

 

615 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


BRANNING v. BRANNING


NO. 4-96-0144


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


285 Ill. App. 3d 405; 674 N.E.2d 463; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 948; 220 Ill. Dec. 920


October 16, 1996, Oral Argument Held  
December 18, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 19, 1996. Released for Publication January 17, 1997. As Corrected February 24, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 96MH37. Honorable Theodis P. Lewis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a court-appointed guardian of a ward of the state, challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which granted a petition brought by appellee state requesting approval to subject the ward to electroconvulsive therapy.


OVERVIEW: When appellee state sought approval to subject a ward of the state to electroconvulsive therapy (ECT), appellant guardian for the ward requested and was denied an examination by an independent psychiatrist prior to the treatment. Although the trial court approved the treatment, rendering the issue moot, the court reviewed and vacated the order because it found that 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-110 (1994), which authorized involuntary medical treatment of state wards, violated due process protections. The objective of providing for persons without the capacity to make reasoned decisions about their need for treatment due to a serious mental illness or disability was a sufficiently compelling state interest to overcome an individual's liberty interest in refusing unwanted medical treatments, but for that interest to be served, the state was required to show that the individual was unable to make a rational decision for himself regarding treatment. Because the statute did not require this, it violated substantive due process. Also, the simple requirement of court "approval" of a guardian's informed consent was held insufficient to satisfy procedural due process.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of the trial court authorizing electroconvulsive therapy of a ward of the state because the statute under which the approval was sought violated the ward's due process protections by permitting an invasion of the ward's liberty interests.

Pincham v. Cunningham


No. 1-93-3252


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


285 Ill. App. 3d 780; 674 N.E.2d 898; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 949; 221 Ill. Dec. 105



December 16, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 22, 1997. Released for Publication January 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Mary Jane Theis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff judge appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his claim for declaratory relief on the ground that the claim presented no controversy that was ripe for adjudication.


OVERVIEW: The judge made comments about a political candidate during a speech while he was a sitting appellate court justice. The judicial inquiry board sought to determine whether there was a reasonable basis to bring charges against the judge for a violation of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 67(A)(2), 134 Ill. 2d R. 67(A)(2) and Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 67(A)(4), 134 Ill. 2d R. 67(A)(4). The judge subsequently retired from the bench and he filed an action seeking a declaration that the rules under which he was investigated were unconstitutional. The court held that the case did not present an actual controversy and that it was premature because he sought to adjudicate rights that were dependent on future events: (1) he would have had to become a sitting judge again because the challenged rule related to the conduct of sitting judges and (2) the board had to decide to reinstate its past complaint against the judge. Further, declaratory relief was not available to adjudicate nonliability for past acts. The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the judge's complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the judge's complaint.

People v. Peck


NOS. 4-94-1009, 4-94-1010 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


285 Ill. App. 3d 14; 674 N.E.2d 440; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 922; 220 Ill. Dec. 897


August 22, 1996, Oral Argument Held, SUBMITTED  
December 9, 1996, FILED


NOTICE:   [***1] UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23 ORDER.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 9, 1996. As Corrected February 24, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. Nos. 94CF95, 93CF1106. Honorable Ronald C. Dozier, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) for aggravated criminal sexual assault, committed upon his two daughters under 13 years of age in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-14(b) (1992).


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of four counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault, committed upon his two daughters under 13 years of age in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-14(b) (1992). Defendant appealed, arguing, among other things, that the trial court had erroneously admitted hearsay testimony in violation of 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115-10 (1992) and an audiotape of an interview with one victim. The court agreed that the trial court had erroneously admitted several hearsay statements that either did not involve a detail pertaining to an act committed against the declarant victim or was unclear whether it constituted such a matter, and so required reversal of the conviction. The court also held that the state did not meet its burden of establishing that statements made in a audiotaped interview of one of the victims while in the sheriff's office were sufficiently reliable in light of the frequent leading and suggestive questions to the victim and, thus, that the trial court abused its discretion by admitting the audiotape. The conviction was reversed and the case remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case for a new trial because the trial court had abused its discretion in admitting hearsay statements that did not come under a hearsay exception or did not have a sufficient indicia of reliability.

Oregon Community Unit Sch. Dist. No. 220 v. Property Tax Appeal Bd.


No. 2-96-0105


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


285 Ill. App. 3d 170; 674 N.E.2d 129; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 919; 220 Ill. Dec. 858


October 22, 1996, SUBMITTED  
December 5, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 6, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Review of Order of Property Tax Appeal Board. PTAB Docket Nos. 89--1163--I--3, 89--1164--I--3, 89--1165--I--3, 90--0968--I--3, 91--1583--I--3, 92--1069--I--3.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent taxpayer challenged the county's ad valorem real property tax assessments of its machinery and equipment. Petitioners, county and fire, school, and park districts (county), sought review of the order of the Property Tax Appeal Board (Illinois), which reversed the county and assessed the taxpayer's machinery and equipment as personal property, exempt from real property taxation.


OVERVIEW: Taxpayer was a nuclear power plant. Its steam generators were assessed for ad valorem real property tax purposes as real property by the county. The taxpayer appealed the assessments to the board. The county claimed that the board erroneously reclassified the property as personal property. The court held that: 1) 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 200/24-5 (1994) froze the classification of property made prior to January 1, 1979; 2) prior to January 1, 1979, the county classified the taxpayer's land, building structures, and building-related property as real property and machinery and equipment as personal property; 3) the county's classification of the taxpayer's steam generators as real property in 1978 was not lawful and was not frozen; 4) the board's reclassification of the steam generators as personal property did not violate § 200/24-5; 5) the board's interpretation of § 200/24-5 was reasonable and was supported by the uniformity clause of Ill. Const. art IX, § 4(a); and 6) the taxpayer's machinery and equipment installed after January 1, 1979 were frozen as personal property and exempt from real property taxation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the board reclassifying the taxpayer's machinery and equipment as personal property, exempt from real property assessments.

 

619 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Disabato v. Board of Trustees of the State Emples. Retirement Sys.


1-94-3649


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


285 Ill. App. 3d 827; 674 N.E.2d 852; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 911; 221 Ill. Dec. 59



December 4, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court, Cook County. The Honorable Edwin M. Berman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retired secretary of state investigators sought to have their benefits recalculated. Defendant board of trustee of the state employees' retirement system (SERS) denied their claims. The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois) affirmed the board's decision. The retirees appealed.


OVERVIEW: The retirees believed that the statutory scheme by which their retirement benefits were calculated was discriminatory, and they sought to have their benefits recalculated. The circuit court denied the recalculation. On appeal, the court affirmed. The retirees' primary contention was that the more favorable benefit calculation accorded state police under 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/14-103.12(c) denied them equal protection. They argued that because there was essentially no difference in the their job duties and those of state police officers, § 14-103.12(c) created an unreasonable and arbitrary classification. The court believed that the legislature had implicitly expressed the basis for the classification at issue within the provisions of § 14-103.12(c). The statutory duties of the state police were substantially broader than those of the retirees, and the legislature could have rationally sought to reward those who took on those additional duties and who continued to perform them over a long period of time. Therefore, the classification established by § 14-103.12(c) of SERS did not deny the retirees equal protection of the laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's decision that denied recalculation of the retirees' benefits.

DeLuna v. Treister


1-94-1397, 1-94-2719 Consolidated


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


286 Ill. App. 3d 25; 676 N.E.2d 973; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 886; 222 Ill. Dec. 9



November 27, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 7, 1997. Released for Publication February 13, 1997.
Rehearing denied by, 02/07/1997
Appeal granted by DeLuna v. Treister, 174 Ill. 2d 558, 1997 Ill. LEXIS 1395 (1997)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by DeLuna v. Treister, 185 Ill. 2d 565, 708 N.E.2d 340, 1999 Ill. LEXIS 16, 236 Ill. Dec. 754 (1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS. THE HONORABLE JENNIFER DUNCAN-BRICE, JUDGE, PRESIDING.
DeLuna v. St. Elizabeth's Hosp., 147 Ill. 2d 57, 588 N.E.2d 1139, 1992 Ill. LEXIS 27, 167 Ill. Dec. 1009 (1992)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff survivors of the deceased patient sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the survivors' medical malpractice action against defendant hospital and doctor on the grounds that the action was barred by the dismissal with prejudice of a prior action against the doctor for failure to comply with the procedural requirements of Ill. Code Civ. P. § 2-622, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-622.


OVERVIEW: The court determined that the survivors could not attack the "with prejudice" language in the order dismissing the first action against the doctor. The court found that the issue was raised throughout the appellate process in the first case, the issue was definitively resolved, the court did not have jurisdiction to alter the order, and the survivors were judicially estopped from even advancing such a claim. The court concluded, however, that the survivors' failure to comply with § 2-622 in the first action did not bar their refiling. The court determined that the prior dismissals resulted from procedural infirmities and the prior action did not result in an evidentiary evaluation of the merits of their medical malpractice claim. The court determined that dismissal for failure to comply with the precondition set out in § 2-622 by failing to attach the required certification was akin to dismissal for lack of jurisdiction, which was a listed exception that did not bar refiling under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 273, 134 Ill. 2d R. 273. The court found that the survivors could also proceed against the hospital that derived its liability from the doctor.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's dismissal of the actions and remanded for further proceedings.

Village of Schaumburg v. Jeep Eagle Sales Corp.


No. 1-95-0608


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


285 Ill. App. 3d 481; 676 N.E.2d 200; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 902; 221 Ill. Dec. 679



November 26, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 15, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 93 MC 006408. The Honorable Arthur Janura, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed its action seeking fines and an injunction against defendant car dealership for an alleged violation of the city's sign ordinance, Village of Schaumburg, Ill., Municipal Code tit. XV, §§ 155.11.02(4)(A)(2), 155.11.03(5)(A)(2) (1993). The circuit court held that the ordinance violated the First Amendment to the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted an ordinance establishing a maximum number of corporate or official flags that could be displayed by car dealerships. The dealership violated the ordinance. Another section of the ordinance regulated the display of banners. After the city brought an action alleging that the dealership violated the ordinance, the dealership contended that the provision of the ordinance regulating banners was unconstitutionally overbroad and restrained free speech. The circuit court agreed, and it entered an order dismissing the city's action. On appeal, the court affirmed the order. The court held that: (1) although the dealership was not charged with violating the banner regulation, the existence of a broadly written statute could have a deterrent effect on free expression, and the ordinance was subject to challenge by the dealership; (2) the ordinance imposed a content-based regulation on noncommercial expression, and the city 's justification that the ordinance promoted traffic safety and aesthetics was insufficient to meet its obligation of showing that the ordinance was necessary to serve a compelling state interest; (3) the invalid parts of the ordinance were not severable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the city's action against the dealership for an alleged violation of the city's sign ordinance.

O'Hare Truck Serv. v. Illinois State Police


No. 2-95-1603


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


284 Ill. App. 3d 941; 673 N.E.2d 731; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 871; 220 Ill. Dec. 587


September 4, 1996, SUBMITTED  
November 22, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 31, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 95--L--1155. Honorable Edward R. Duncan, Jr., Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant towing service sought review of the decision by the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) in favor of appellees state police and officer in appellant's action seeking monetary damages and injunctive relief from appellant's removal from the district tow list. Appellant argued that it was removed from the list without due process of law in violation of the Illinois Constitution and U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Appellant towing company challenged the trial court's decision in favor of appellees state police and officer in appellant's action stemming from appellant's removal from the district's tow list. The court held that appellant's action against appellees was not barred by U.S. Const. amend. XI because appellant challenged the constitutionality of appellees' action in removing it from the towing list. In addition, appellant was only seeking injunctive relief from the state and only seeking monetary damages from appellee officer in his individual capacity. However, the court held that appellant failed to allege a property interest protected by the Due Process Clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and the Illinois Constitution. Because each district was allowed to form its own tow list and adopt its own procedures, appellant failed to allege that its purported property interest was based on an Illinois state law or regulation. Accordingly, the court affirmed the trial court's decision in favor of appellees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision in favor of appellees state police and officer. Appellant's action was not barred by the Eleventh Amendment because appellant was challenging the constitutionality of appellees' action in removing appellant from the district's tow list. However, appellant failed to establish a property interest protected by the Due Process Clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment and the Illinois Constitution.

People v. Nitz


No. 3-96-0276


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


285 Ill. App. 3d 364; 674 N.E.2d 802; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 841; 221 Ill. Dec. 9


October 1, 1996, SUBMITTED  
November 15, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 23, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit, Rock Island County, Illinois. No. 95--CF--838. Honorable Larry Vandersnick, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court convicted defendant on two counts of the offense of hate crime in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-7.1 (1994), based on his racially motivated harassment of his neighbor. The trial court fined defendant and placed him on 30 months' probation, including a term of six months in the county jail.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of a hate crime for his disorderly conduct in harassing a neighbor. He claimed that § 5/12-7.1 was an unconstitutional infringement on free speech, was unconstitutionally vague, and was unconstitutionally overbroad. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that § 5/12-7 was constitutional in all respects. The state proved, beyond a reasonable doubt, that defendant knowingly acted in an unreasonable manner in order to alarm or disturb his neighbor and to provoke a breach of the peace, pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/26-1 (1994). Thus, because defendant's disorderly conduct conviction was based on racially motivated conduct, rather than solely on unpopular or bigoted speech, there was no infringement on the constitutionally protected right of free speech. Also, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-7.1 (1994) was not unconstitutionally vague because § 5/12-7.1 clearly stated, in terms commonly used and understood, the nature of the offense and the guidelines for its proper application. Further, § 5/12-7.1 was not overbroad because it clearly did not punish people for the mere use of words.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of the hate crime offense.

People v. Parsons


No. 1-94-4175


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


284 Ill. App. 3d 1049; 673 N.E.2d 347; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 855; 220 Ill. Dec. 435



November 1, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 10, 1996. Released for Publication December 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Francis J. Mahon, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: State's motion granted. Judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated arson based on evidence that he set off a bomb in the bathroom of a bar he frequented. On appeal, defendant argued that the indictment was insufficient, and that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury on the lesser-included offense of criminal damage to property.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction arguing that the indictment was insufficient in that it did not specify that the property was damaged by means of fire or explosive. The court affirmed the conviction, finding that when such a charge was raised for the first time on appeal, the standard by which the indictment was tested was less stringent than when the sufficiency was challenged before trial. The court found that the indictment specified the date and place at which defendant was said to have violated the arson statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/20-1.1(a) (1994), which referred to arson as damage to real property by means of fire or explosive. The court held that the indictment sufficiently apprised defendant of the precise offense charged with enough specificity to allow him to prepare a defense and to allow his conviction to act as a bar to future prosecution. The court found that although criminal damage to property was a lesser-included offense of aggravated arson, defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on the lesser offense as the evidence was no extensive that a jury could not rationally have acquitted defendant of the larger offense and convicted of the lesser one.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, finding that the indictment was sufficient to apprise him of the precise offense charged with the requisite specificity. The court held that defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on the lesser-included offense of criminal damage to property because, on the evidence adduced, a jury could not rationally have acquitted him of aggravated arson and convicted him of the lesser offense.

Anderson v. Chicago Bd. of Election Comm'rs


1-96-0628


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


284 Ill. App. 3d 832; 672 N.E.2d 1259; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 835; 220 Ill. Dec. 247



October 30, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 10, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS, COUNTY DEPARTMENT, COUNTY DIVISION. THE HONORABLE MICHAEL J. MURPHY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff challenger appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), affirming the decision of defendants, Chicago Board of Election Commissioners (Board) and others, approving the nominating petition of a candidate for ward committeeman. The challenger argued that the nominating petition lacked the requisite number of signatures to be placed on the ballot.


OVERVIEW: A registered voter who was confined to a wheelchair and communicated with his eyes and nodding his head up and down executed a nominating petition by nodding assent when asked by his wife and legal guardian if he wished to execute the petition. The voter's wife signed the voter's name for the voter in the presence of proper authority. The challenger claimed that the signature did not comply with § 7-10 of the Election Code, 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-10, and that, therefore, the petition did not contain enough signatures to elect the candidate for ward committeeman. The Board approved the nominating petition, and the circuit court affirmed the Board's decision. The challenger appealed, and the court affirmed. The court held that the Board's construction of the Election Code honored its letter and its spirit. The Election Code evinced a strong public policy protecting the rights of those unable to physically participate due to some disability. Reading § 7-10 in pari materia with 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-1.2, the court held that the voter was permitted to execute the petition as he did.


OUTCOME: Over the challenger's appeal that the nominating petition lacked the requisite number of signatures to place the candidate for ward committeeman on the ballot, the court affirmed the circuit court's affirmance of the Board's approval of the nominating petition.

People v. Bennett


Nos. 2-95-0231, 2-94-1411 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


284 Ill. App. 3d 276; 672 N.E.2d 799; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 773; 219 Ill. Dec. 946


July 24, 1996, SUBMITTED  
October 16, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 5, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lee County. Nos. 93--TR--5588, 94--CF--0077. Honorable Thomas E. Hornsby, Judge, Presiding.

This Opinion Substituted for Withdrawn Rule 23 Order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Lee County (Illinois) denying his petitions for habeas corpus and mandamus. Defendant argued that a sentencing provision, § 5-8-4(d) of the Unified Code of Corrections, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4(d) (1994), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to 364 days' imprisonment on a misdemeanor conviction and to 18 months' imprisonment on a felony conviction, the sentences to be served concurrently. Defendant's felony sentence, after the appropriate credits were applied, was completed three months prior to the misdemeanor sentence. Defendant filed petitions for habeas corpus and mandamus, seeking an immediate release because of the completion of his felony sentence. The trial court denied the petitions, as well as defendant's motions for diminution of sentence and reconsideration. Defendant appealed, arguing that he was denied equal protection and due process because he was required to serve more prison time than someone who had received the same sentences for the same conduct, but who already happened to be serving the misdemeanor sentence, under the merger provision of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5-8-4(d). The court affirmed, finding that the merger provision did not mandate that an offender with nonmerged concurrent misdemeanor and felony sentences would automatically serve more time than an offender with merged sentences. Further, the provision was reasonably designed to accomplish a legitimate state goal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying defendant's petitions for habeas corpus and mandamus in connection with his confinement pursuant to a misdemeanor sentence.

Serafin v. Seith


No. 1-95-1135


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


284 Ill. App. 3d 577; 672 N.E.2d 302; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 753; 219 Ill. Dec. 794



October 4, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. No. 91 CH 07485. THE HONORABLE DOROTHY KINNAIRD, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff stockholder appealed the decision of the Circuit Court Of Cook County (Illinois), which held that the stockholder's claims against defendant law firm were barred by the statute of repose contained in 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-214.3 (1992)


OVERVIEW: The stockholder owned shares in a corporation that was formed by a lawyer who worked for the law firm. The stockholder's ownership percentage was less than the one third required to prevent the dilution of the stockholder's ownership share. More than six years after the corporation was formed the stockholder filed an action against the law firm alleging fraud, fraudulent concealment, and legal malpractice. The lower court dismissed the stockholder's action pursuant to § 5/13-214.3, holding that the six year statute of repose barred the stockholder's action, and the court affirmed. The court held that the six year statute of repose began running with the formation of the corporation because the other stockholders' ability to dilute the shares sprang from the formation of the corporation and not any later acts. The stockholder's equal protection rights were not violated because the statute of repose applied to other professionals. The court ruled that the law firm was not equitably estopped from asserting that the stockholder's claim was time barred because the stockholder had ample time to comply with § 5/13-214.3 after the alleged misrepresentations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the stockholder's complaint against the law firm.

Palmros v. Barcelona


No. 2-95-1340


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


284 Ill. App. 3d 642; 672 N.E.2d 1245; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 758; 220 Ill. Dec. 233


August 15, 1996, SUBMITTED  
October 4, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 12, 1996. Rehearing Denied December 12, 1996. Released for Publication December 12, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kendall County. No. 94--L--46. Honorable Grant S. Wegner, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant decedent's widow sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Kendall County (Illinois), which dismissed as time-barred her complaint against appellee attorney alleging malpractice in the drafting and execution of decedent's will.


OVERVIEW: Appellee attorney drafted and executed decedent's will. Appellant decedent's widow initiated action alleging malpractice against appellee after the will was contested in probate. The trial court dismissed appellant's complaint as time-barred, pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-619(a)(5) (1994) and 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-214.3(d) (1994), and appellant sought review. The court held that there can be no injury for which damages were sought until appellant suffered a loss. The injury was not the negligent act itself; it was something caused by the negligent act or omission. The injury that triggered the statute of limitations was appellee's breach of his duty of due care. The court found that her injury did not occur until the death of her spouse for whom appellee rendered service, and the shortened limitation period of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-214.3(d) (1994) applied. The court held that appellant failed to file the action within the requisite time, and it affirmed an order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the trial court, which dismissed appellant decedent's widow's malpractice action against appellee attorney. The court held that appellant's complaint was time-barred because the statute of limitations was triggered at the point where appellant first suffered damages, the point where her spouse died and not at the time of the will contest, and thus, appellant failed to file the action within the requisite time.

Klomann v. Illinois Mun. Retirement Fund


No. 1-95-0368


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


284 Ill. App. 3d 224; 674 N.E.2d 38; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 745; 220 Ill. Dec. 767



September 30, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 90-CH-9372. Honorable John N. Hourihane, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former village attorney appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County(Illinois), which found that the record supported the determination by defendants, village and municipal retirement fund, that the attorney was not entitled to pension benefits under the Illinois Pension Code.


OVERVIEW: Prior to his retirement, the village trustees passed a resolution declaring the attorney eligible for participation in the retirement fund. The attorney enrolled as a participant and, after his retirement, the fund awarded him benefits. The village and the fund later reversed their positions and declared the attorney ineligible. The attorney argued that Ill. Const. 1970, art. XIII, § 5 barred the fund from changing its position once it had accepted the village's resolution. The court disagreed and held that it was the Illinois Pension Code that determined whether the attorney was eligible for benefits, not the resolution. The court also rejected the attorney's argument that this reversal was barred by the 35-day limitations period applicable to final administrative decisions under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-103 (1992). The court held that the fund's final administrative determination was not the initial acceptance of the resolution but the later termination of benefits. The court further held that the attorney had failed to show any bias or prejudice resulting from the trial court's alleged error at an earlier stage in remanding the case to the fund and not to the village.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court in favor of the village and the municipal retirement fund.

Stern v. Norwest Mortg.


No. 1-95-1627


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


284 Ill. App. 3d 506; 672 N.E.2d 296; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 748; 219 Ill. Dec. 788



September 30, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Albert Green, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff borrowers appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their claims against defendant mortgage company for violation of the Illinois Mortgage Escrow Account Act, 765 Ill. Comp. Stat. 910/1 et seq. (1992), and for violation of the Illinois Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Business Practices Act, 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. 505/2 (1992), after they were charged an escrow waiver fee on their home loan.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff borrowers obtained a loan from defendant mortgage company to purchase a home, and chose the option of pledging a certificate of deposit sufficient to cover anticipated taxes. Defendant informed plaintiffs that they a one-time service fee applied if they exercised that option. Plaintiffs paid the charge, but then filed a class action against defendant, alleging that it violated the Illinois Mortgage Escrow Account Act (Act), 765 Ill. Comp. Stat. 910/1 et seq. (1992), by charging them and others similarly situated an escrow waiver fee, and that it violated the Illinois Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Business Practices Act (Consumer Fraud Act), 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. 505/2 (1992). Defendant filed a motion to dismiss, which was granted, and plaintiffs appealed. The court affirmed the dismissal of the complaint under the Consumer Fraud Act because the parties had a legitimate disagreement over the implications of the Act, and the Consumer Fraud Act prohibited deception, not error. The court reversed the judgment as to defendant's right to impose an escrow waiver fee because by its action, defendant fee appropriated for itself the very benefit conferred upon plaintiff by the Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of plaintiff borrowers' claim against defendant mortgage company for charging them an escrow waiver fee because defendant, through the fee, appropriated the benefit that was to be conferred on plaintiff through the statute. The court affirmed the dismissal of the consumer fraud claim because there was a legitimate disagreement over the fee, and only deception was prohibited, not error.

 

631 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Orr v. Edgar


Nos. 1-96-1613, 1-96-2178, 1-96-3050, Consolidated


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


283 Ill. App. 3d 1088; 670 N.E.2d 1243; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 734; 219 Ill. Dec. 355



September 26, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 22, 1996. Released for Publication October 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Nos. 95 CO 0246, 95 CO 0268, Consolidated. The Honorable Francis Barth, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state and officials appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiff citizens in an action challenging the state's two-tier system of voter registration. The state contended the court erred in holding that the two-tier system, which implemented the National Voter Registration Act, violated certain provisions of both the Illinois Vehicle Code and the State Mandates Act.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff citizens filed suit against defendant state and officials challenging its two-tier system of voter registration, on the grounds that it violated the notice requirements of the Illinois Vehicle Code, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-105, the equal protection clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, and the guarantee of free and equal elections, Ill. Const. art. III, § 3. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the citizens, holding that the two-tier system violated both the Vehicle Code and the State Mandates Act, 30 Ill. Comp. Stat. 805/3(b). On review, the state argued that the trial court's findings were erroneous. The appeals court agreed that the two-tier system violated the notice requirements of the Vehicle Code. The court rejected the state's position that posting a sign at each licensing facility was sufficient to satisfy the requirements of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-105, since the statute specified that each applicant must be notified. The court also ruled that because no funds were appropriated by the state for the two-tier system of registration, the local election authorities were relieved of the obligation to implement the mandate.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment in favor of the citizens because the two-tier system of voter registration violated the voter-registration notice provisions contained in the Illinois Vehicle Code. The court ruled that the statute required that notice be given to each applicant of their right to vote in state and local elections.

 

632 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Vladimir P. (In re Vladimir P.)


No. 1-95-2141


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


283 Ill. App. 3d 1068; 670 N.E.2d 839; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 702; 219 Ill. Dec. 161



September 20, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE CATHERINE HABERKORN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After an adjudicatory hearing, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found respondent, a 15-year-old Jewish boy, to be delinquent and adjudicated him as a ward of the court. The delinquency findings were based on an aggravated assault, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-2 (1994), and a hate crime, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-7.1 (1994), against another Jewish boy.


OVERVIEW: Respondent and other boys were playing with a broken knife when a 13-year old Jewish boy walked by them wearing a head covering and prayer tassels symbolizing his religious beliefs. The other boys shouted religious slurs against the Jewish boy and then one of them threw the knife handle at the boy. Respondent threw the knife blade at the boy. The court upheld the delinquency findings. First, the court held that Illinois' hate crime statute was constitutional. The court rejected respondent's argument that the statute violated his rights to free speech and thought, due process, and equal protection under the law guaranteed by the state and federal Constitutions. In particular, the statute did not impermissibly criminalize thought. Instead, the statute punished an offender's criminal conduct in choosing a victim by reason of his beliefs or hatred, and then committing one of the criminal acts included in 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-7.1 (1994). Finally, respondent could be guilty of a hate crime even though both he and the victim were Jewish.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

People v. Bofman

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual assault and sentenced him to nine years of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant first claimed that the aggravated criminal sexual assault statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-14 (1994) was unconstitutional. The court disagreed and determined that the statute was constitutional even though it did not specify a mental state. Defendant also argued that the indictment was insufficient. The court determined that the indictment was not defective for failing to allege a mental state because the statute defining the charge did not include a mental state. Defendant further contended that the trial court erred when it concluded that there was no lesser-included offense of which he could have been convicted. The court stated that the trial court had recognized that aggravated criminal sexual abuse was a lesser-included offense and the evidence supported defendant's conviction. Defendant argued that the trial court had decided, prior to the conclusion of the trial, the credibility of the witnesses and defendant's guilt. The court held that the trial court had properly weighed the credibility of the witnesses and had drawn reasonable inferences. Defendant's conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that had convicted defendant of the offense of aggravated criminal sexual assault.

People v. Cortez


No. 1-95-1158


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


286 Ill. App. 3d 478; 676 N.E.2d 195; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 676; 221 Ill. Dec. 674



September 12, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 94-CR-13410. Honorable Edward M. Fiala, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of conviction from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of stalking and sentenced him to probation alleging that the stalking statute was unconstitutional on its face and its application to him violated ex post facto constitutional guarantees.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of stalking and sentenced him to probation. On appeal, defendant argued that the stalking statute was unconstitutional on its face and its application to him violated ex post facto constitutional guarantees. The court held that defendant had not satisfied his burden of establishing the constitutional violations and the judgment of conviction was affirmed. The statute did not encompass innocent conduct and bore a reasonable relationship to the interest it sought to protect and the 1993 stalking statute was not void for overbreadth. Further, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague as it applied to defendant. The statute clearly warned defendant that his conduct would subject him to penalty under the statute. In addition, the 1993 stalking statute was sufficiently narrow as to avoid arbitrary enforcement by the police. The statute did not violate defendant's ex post facto constitutional guarantees because defendant's conduct was unlawful under both the 1992 and 1993 versions of the stalking statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction against defendant for stalking.

Sprague v. City of Marion

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Williamson County (Illinois) that vacated appellee officer's three-day suspension in the officer's declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: The officer was suspended for three days without pay by the chief of police for the city. The officer then sent a letter to a merit commission stating that he contested the suspension. No action was taken on the officer's letter even though the officer considered the letter sufficient notice that he was appealing the suspension and requesting a hearing. The officer then filed a declaratory judgment action arguing that the suspension was null and void under 65 Ill. Comp. In reversing that judgment, the court ruled that § 5/10-2.1-17 did not entitle the officer to a hearing for a three-day suspension. The court noted that the opportunity of a hearing was only discussed in the first paragraph of the statute dealing with the removal or discharge of an officer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment vacating the officer's suspension, and it remanded to the trial court with directions to reinstate the suspension.

People v. Munetsi

The trial court sentenced defendant to 11 years imprisonment for armed robbery and 3 years imprisonment on each of the 3 counts of aggravated unlawful restraint. M.E.H. v. L.H.


No. 2-95-1188


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


283 Ill. App. 3d 241; 669 N.E.2d 1228; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 641; 218 Ill. Dec. 702


June 11, 1996, SUBMITTED  
August 28, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 1, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ogle County. No. 94--L--67. Honorable Stephen C. Pemberton, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff children appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Ogle County (Illinois), which dismissed their action against defendant father. The complaint alleged childhood sexual abuse, unlawful sexual relations in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 5/11--11 (1992), and false imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: When the children filed their claims in 1994, they were 45 and 44 years old. The trial court concluded that the statute of repose contained in the childhood sexual abuse section of the 1991 Limitations Act, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 5/13--202.2(b) (1992), barred their claims against their father. That statute of repose barred complaints alleging childhood sexual abuse by persons 30 years of age or older. The court affirmed. The court rejected the children's argument that the 1994 amendment to the Act, which eliminated the statute of repose, applied to their claims. The court held that the father had obtained a vested right in the statute of repose contained in the original 1991 Act and that, therefore, the amended 1994 Act, which repealed the statute of repose, could not revive the children's causes of action. The court further held that the children's causes of action against their father had accrued when they reached 18 years of age and ruled that the discovery rule did not apply to cases in which plaintiffs claimed that they had repressed childhood sexual abuse from their memories.


OUTCOME: The court held that the trial court had properly dismissed the children's complaint against their father and affirmed the trial court judgment.
