People v. Shapiro


NO. 4-95-0584


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


283 Ill. App. 3d 343; 669 N.E.2d 1200; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 633; 218 Ill. Dec. 674


February 9, 1996, SUBMITTED  
August 23, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 2, 1996. As Corrected October 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 95CF100. Honorable John R. DeLaMar, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(a)(1), 145 Ill. 2d R. 604(a)(1), the state sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) that granted defendants' motions to suppress evidence and to quash their arrest. Defendants were charged with possession and intent to deliver a controlled substance in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/401(a)(11) (1994).


OVERVIEW: The state argued that the initial seizure of the package was proper. The court affirmed the granting of the motions. The court found that the proper standard to be applied in seizing a package from the Postal Service was whether authorities had a reasonable suspicion, based upon articulable facts, that the package might have contained illicit narcotics. In this case, the express mail package met four of the drug package profile characteristics of the Postal Service, and although there were no additional factors to indicate the package was suspicious, the court concluded that the characteristics of the package provided reasonable suspicion to remove it from the mail stream for the limited purpose of further investigation. The court found, however, that the detention of the package was unreasonable and a violation of the Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The court considered three factors in reaching this decision: the investigatory diligence, the length of the detention, and the information conveyed to defendants and concluded that the process of the investigation was not conducted diligently and the length of the detention, more than three days, was unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the granting of defendants' motions to suppress evidence and quash their arrest.

People v. Fornear


No. 2-94-0471


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


283 Ill. App. 3d 171; 669 N.E.2d 939; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 627; 218 Ill. Dec. 618

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 93--CF--2446. Honorable John R. Goshgarian, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a review of an order of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated discharge of a firearm under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24-1.2(a)(2) (1992), of reckless conduct, and of unlawful use of a weapon under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24-1(a)(7) (1992).


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of aggravated discharge of a firearm in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24-1.2(a)(2) (1992), of reckless conduct, and of violating 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24-1(a)(7) (1992) by unlawful use of a weapon, and denied defendant's motion for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict. The court affirmed that judgment on appeal. The court also held that there was no need to sever the unlawful use of a weapon charge because there was no reasonable likelihood that testimony as to the presence of a shotgun would have been a material factor in affecting the jury's resolution of the shooting related charges, and that the evidence that defendant possessed the shotgun was clear and uncontradicted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's legally consistent convictions for aggravated discharge of a firearm, for reckless conduct, and for unlawful use of a weapon, and a denial of his motion for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict.

In re C.M.


Nos. 3-95-0651 & 3-95-0694


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


282 Ill. App. 3d 990; 669 N.E.2d 707; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 624; 218 Ill. Dec. 564


June 11, 1996, SUBMITTED  
August 14, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County, Illinois. No. 93-J-10. Honorable John F. Michela, Judge, Presiding.

Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. No. 95-J-7455. Honorable Vincent J. Cerri, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Department of Children and Family Services (DCFS) appealed judgments from the Circuit Courts of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, and the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County (Illinois) that determined the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 4/2-10, 2-27, 5-10, and 5-23 (Supp. 1995) as amended by Public Act 89-21 did not limit the trial court's power to place delinquent minors in the custody of the DCFS.


OVERVIEW: Minors who had placed in the custody of the DCFS had been adjudicated as delinquent for criminal activities. The court reversed the judgments that placed custody of the minors in the DCFS. The court observed the specific language of article II of the Public Act 89-21 that amended the Juvenile Court Act of 1987 (Act), 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/2-10(2) and 2-27(1)(d), which provided that minors charged with criminal offenses or adjudicated delinquent could not have been placed with the DCFS. The court held that the amendments were constitutional because the best interests of the child standard was maintained, and it was within the legislature's power to redefine the trial courts' ability to place minors with the DCFS within that modified contour. The court rejected an equal protection claim because juveniles were not a suspect class, and the amendment was rationally related to the Act's purpose of protecting abused, neglected, or dependent minors that had not been adjudicated delinquent. Finally, the court held that the amendments altered the DCFS's mandate under the Child and Family Services Act and did not allow for an independent basis determination for a custody petition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments and remanded for further proceedings consistent with its opinion.

People ex rel. Sklodowski v. State


Nos. 1-93-2951, 1-93-3171, 1-93-3172, 1-93-3173, (Cons.)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


284 Ill. App. 3d 809; 674 N.E.2d 81; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 613; 220 Ill. Dec. 810

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing November 26, 1996. Rehearing Denied November 22, 1996. Released for Publication November 27, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Lester D. Foreman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, public educators' retirement systems, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), dismissing their action against appellees, state and state officials, for a writ of mandamus, declaratory judgment, and an enforcement order based on appellees' failure to contribute retirement pension benefits in violation of 1989 Ill. Pub. Act 86-273 and Ill. Const. art. XIII, § 5 (1970).


OVERVIEW: In 1989, the Illinois legislature enacted 1989 Ill. Pub. Act 86-273 and amended the state pension law to require a specified level of funding for public educators' retirement systems over a seven-year period. After the legislature failed to provide the funding, appellants, public educators' retirement systems, brought an action against appellees, state and state officials, for a writ of mandamus, declaratory judgment, and an enforcement order compelling appellees to make the specified contributions to the retirement systems. The court reversed dismissal of appellants' claim against state officials, who were properly directed to comply with state law establishing appellants' right to the contributions.

People v. Felix


NOS. 4-95-0607, 4-95-0608 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


282 Ill. App. 3d 621; 668 N.E.2d 644; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 574; 218 Ill. Dec. 160


January 26, 1996, SUBMITTED  
July 26, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 27, 1996. As Corrected August 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Vermilion County. Nos. 94CF348, 94CF455. Honorable Thomas J. Fahey, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois), which dismissed unrelated felony drug charges against defendant because the state had successfully sought forfeiture of defendant's cash and other property, which were allegedly connected to the drug charges.


OVERVIEW: The state filed felony drug charges against defendant. The state then filed complaints, which sought forfeiture of certain possessions of defendant and the drugs, which the trial court granted. Thereafter, defendant filed motions to dismiss the felony charges and alleged that the asset forfeitures constituted punishment for double jeopardy purposes and any subsequent prosecutions violated the double jeopardy clause. The trial court granted defendant's motions, and the state appealed. On appeal, the court reversed the decision of the trial court. The court held that the double jeopardy clause protected against three abuses. The present cases addressed the third of these protections, multiple punishments for the same offense. However, the court ruled that in rem civil forfeitures did not constitute punishment for the purpose of the double jeopardy clause. The court reversed the dismissals because they were based upon in rem civil forfeitures.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which had dismissed the state's felony drug charges against defendant.

 

643 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ratliff


No. 2-95-0282


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


282 Ill. App. 3d 707; 669 N.E.2d 122; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 575; 218 Ill. Dec. 391


January 25, 1996, SUBMITTED  
July 26, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 3, 1996. Released for Publication September 3, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, No. 94--CF--171. Honorable Melvin E. Dunn, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People of the State of Illinois appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss two counts against him on the basis of double jeopardy. Defendant paid a penalty and fees under a city ordinance after the seizure and impoundment of his car by the police. The criminal counts arose from the same factual transaction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested because of his actions in a domestic argument. The police found bullets on his person and a revolver in his car. The city held that defendant violated § 29--48 of the Code of Ordinances of the City of Aurora for the use of a car in committing certain offenses. On appeal, the court held that charging defendant a $ 500 fine and towing and storage fees was neither "so extreme" nor "so divorced" from the ordinance's nonpunitive purpose of compensating the city for the damages done by defendant. Five hundred dollars was a reasonable proxy for the likely actual administrative costs incurred by the city in preparing, prosecuting, hearing, and disposing of § 29--48 complaints. The court found that the sanctions the city charged under § 29--48 and the fees for towing and storage expenses incurred by the city were solely remedial in nature. Thus, the fine and fees under § 29--48 did not constitute punishment for double jeopardy purposes under the federal or the Illinois constitution. The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded for further proceedings. The court found that a city ordinance that subjected defendant to a penalty and fees did not impose punishment for double jeopardy purposes.

People v. Falconer


No. 1-95-0828


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


282 Ill. App. 3d 785; 668 N.E.2d 1095; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 560; 218 Ill. Dec. 263



July 22, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 29, 1996. Certiorari Denied April 28, 1997, Reported at 1997 U.S. LEXIS 2748.
Appeal denied by People v. Falconer, 169 Ill. 2d 576, 675 N.E.2d 636, 1996 Ill. LEXIS 381, 221 Ill. Dec. 441 (1996)
Writ of certiorari denied Falconer v. Illinois, 520 U.S. 1201, 117 S. Ct. 1562, 137 L. Ed. 2d 709, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 2748 (1997)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Falconer, 2013 IL App (1st) 112809-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1586 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE MICHAEL TOOMIN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted him of first degree murder and sentenced him to 50 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for first degree murder and his 50 year sentence. He claimed that plaintiff state's comments during closing and rebuttal argument denied him a fair trial. He also contended that the state improperly attempted to shift the burden of proof to defendant by making rebuttal arguments that defendant failed to produce witnesses. The court affirmed. It noted that argument that asked the jury to consider a defendant's interest in the outcome of the case in evaluating his credibility was proper. The state's comments were not improper, as they were framed as comparing defendant's credibility with the credibility of the testifying witness. The state did not urge the jury to completely disregard defendant's testimony. Where the defendant testified and asserted an affirmative defense, the state's prosecutor's passing comments about that defense were not reversible error. Insofar as the defendant bore the burden of production on the issue of imperfect self-defense where second degree murder was a possible verdict, it was questionable whether comments on whether defendant met that burden could be said to impermissibly shift the burden of proof to the defense.


OUTCOME: Defendant's first degree murder conviction and 50 year prison sentence were affirmed.

Illinois Bell Tel. Co. v. Illinois Commerce Comm'n


Nos. 2-94-1272, 2-94-1440, 2-94-1443, 2-94-1464, 2-94-1468 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


283 Ill. App. 3d 188; 669 N.E.2d 919; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 552; 218 Ill. Dec. 598


February 21, 1996, SUBMITTED  
July 17, 1996, FILED


NOTICE:  [***1] UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23 ORDER.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 25, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for review of the order of the Illinois Commerce Commission. Appeal No. 2--94--1272. Petition for review of the order of the Illinois Commerce Commission. Appeal No. 2--94--1440. Petition for review of the order of the Illinois Commerce Commission. Appeal No. 2--94--1443. Petition for review of the order of the Illinois Commerce Commission. Appeal No. 2--94--1464. Petition for review of the order of the Illinois Commerce Commission. Appeal No. 2--94--1468.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, competitors and utility board, challenged an order of the Illinois Commerce Commission (Commission), which regulated rates and charges for noncompetitive services provided by appellee telephone company. The competitors and the utility board had filed a complaint before the Commission seeking an investigation and reduction of the rates charged by the telephone company.


OVERVIEW: The competitors challenged the rates set by the Commission. The court examined the statutes addressing regulation and held that 220 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13--506.1 was a permissible use of the police power. The court held that the standards set forth in § 13--506.1 were sufficiently precise to pass constitutional muster. The court held that the Commission did not ignore substantial evidence in finding the use of the telephone company's actual capital structure reasonable and that the Commission's finding that the telephone company's actual capital structure was reasonable was supported by substantial evidence. The court held, however, that the Commission applied an incorrect construction of 220 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9--230 and, in so doing, failed to apply the section at all. Rather than determining whether the telephone company's risk or capital costs were greater because of its affiliation with another company, the Commission merely determined that the telephone company's capital structure was reasonable. As a result, the Commission also failed to make a finding of fact upon a principal issue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the Commission's order.

 

646 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Communications & Cable v. City of Chicago


No. 1-95-4358


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


282 Ill. App. 3d 1038; 668 N.E.2d 1032; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 544; 218 Ill. Dec. 200



July 12, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 29, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 95 CH 11919. The Honorable Alexander P. White, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff cable companies appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied their motion for injunctive relief in an action challenging the validity of a municipal amusement tax, Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 4-156-010 et seq., as applied to cable television services.


OVERVIEW: The cable companies were required to collect and remit an amusement tax from their subscribers. They contended that the tax was an unauthorized occupational tax prohibited by Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(e)(2). The court affirmed the trial court's denial of injunctive relief, holding that the imposition of an amusement tax was authorized by 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-42-5 and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in ruling that the activity of viewing cable television was subject to taxation as an amusement. The court further held that the tax did not violate the Uniformity Clause, Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2, merely because providers of broadcast television, movie rentals, and other services were not subject to the tax. The court held that because the tax ordinance applied to businesses other than cable service providers, it was not a "franchise fee" as defined in 47 U.S.C.S. § 542(g)(1)(A). The tax was not imposed solely because of status as a cable provider but was a tax of general applicability that was not unduly discriminatory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of injunctive relief to the cable companies.

Rodgers v. Whitley


No. 1-93-4338


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


282 Ill. App. 3d 741; 668 N.E.2d 1023; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 531; 218 Ill. Dec. 191



July 8, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 29, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Alexander P. White, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant residents sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissing appellants' amended complaint challenging the constitutionality of certain provisions of the Property Tax Extension Limitation Act, 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 200/18-185 et seq. (1996), and denying a permanent injunction to enjoin appellees, Governor and Director of the Illinois Department of Revenue, from enforcing the act.


OVERVIEW: Appellant residents filed suit against appellees, Governor and Director of the Illinois Department of Revenue, challenging the constitutionality of the Property Tax Extension Limitation Act (Act), 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 200/18-185 et seq. (1996), and seeking a permanent injunction to enjoin appellees from further enforcing the Act. The court reversed the circuit court's judgment except insofar as it determined that appellants failed to state a claim under the uniformity of taxation clause, Ill. Const. art. IX, § 4(a), and the cause was remanded for further proceedings. The court concluded that appellants had alleged an injury to a legally cognizable interest and held they had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the Act. The court concluded that appellant's amended complaint sufficiently stated a claim that the Act violated the special legislation clause, Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13, and the due process and equal protection clauses because classifications based on county population were not rationally related to the stated purpose of providing property tax relief for people residing in districts which had experienced excessive tax extension increases.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment except insofar as it determined that appellant residents failed to state a claim under the uniformity of taxation clause and the cause was remanded for further proceedings. The court concluded that appellants' amended complaint sufficiently stated claims that a property tax extension statute violated the state's special legislation clause and the due process and equal protection clauses.

Zamarron v. Pucinski


No. 1-94-1685


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


282 Ill. App. 3d 354; 668 N.E.2d 186; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 503; 218 Ill. Dec. 23



June 28, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 13, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 89-CH-01. Honorable Edwin M. Berman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, representing a class required to pay court fees, sought relief from appellees, clerk of court, chief deputy of court, and treasurer of court (court employees) for violation of state and federal constitutions based on increased court filing fees. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered a directed finding for the court employees, as the class representatives failed to present a prima facie case. The representatives appealed.


OVERVIEW: Class representatives alleged that the General Assembly enacted Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 25, para. 27.2, 27.3a (1989) to revise the law in relation to clerks of courts in order to abate general property taxes and for other nonjudicial purposes, in violation of the Free Access Clause of the Illinois Constitution and the Due Process Clauses of the Illinois and the United States Constitutions. The representatives argued that the lower court erred when it entered a directed finding in favor of the court employees, committed reversible error when it refused to admit a certified copy of the legislative debates into evidence, and abused its discretion when it refused to compel the court employees to produce documents requested under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 237(b). 134 Ill. 2d R. 237(b). The court held that the representatives failed to establish a prima facie case that §§ 27.2, 27.3a were constitutionally infirm. Although the lower court should have considered the legislative debates, its refusal to admit them into evidence was not reversible error. The court held that the lower court did not abuse its discretion when it declined to compel production of records sought by the representatives.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the court employees was affirmed.

Village of Cary v. Trout Valley Ass'n


No. 2--95--1470


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


282 Ill. App. 3d 165; 667 N.E.2d 1082; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 506; 217 Ill. Dec. 689


June 4, 1996, SUBMITTED  
June 28, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 9, 1996. Released for Publication August 9, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 94--ED--8. Honorable James C. Franz and Michael J. Sullivan, Judges, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant association sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois), which granted judgment in favor of plaintiff village on its condemnation complaint.


OVERVIEW: The village filed a condemnation complaint seeking to acquire an easement for the construction and installation of an underground sewer pipe on the association's land. The trial court granted judgment for the village, which the court vacated and remanded. The association's traverse and motion to dismiss should have resulted in dismissal because the village could not demonstrate its right to condemn by proper proof. A municipality could only exercise the power of eminent domain if it was specifically conferred by legislative enactment. The village's condemnation complaint alleged that it was condemning the property pursuant to 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-139-1 et seq. (1994). Once the association contested the village's right to condemn by filing a traverse and motion to dismiss, the village had the burden of establishing that it had the authority to exercise its right of eminent domain. The ordinance cited by the city was invalid because the village failed to comply with the requirements of 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-139-5 (1994). The ordinance did not set out the estimated cost of the contemplated project, the period of usefulness, or the method of defraying the cost of the project.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and remanded the trial court's decision for entry of an order dismissing the village's petition for condemnation.

Town of Cicero v. LaFrancis


No. 1-95-2791


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


282 Ill. App. 3d 556; 668 N.E.2d 164; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 514; 218 Ill. Dec. 1



June 28, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 13, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Joan Pucillo, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) judgment dismissing its citations to defendant vehicle owners on the basis that the city ordinance was unconstitutional and exceeded the home rule power to enforce a vehicle tax against commercial vehicles under § 2-121 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-121.


OVERVIEW: The town issued citations to commercial vehicle owners for violating a local ordinance requiring the purchase and display of a town vehicle sticker on vehicles registered in the town. After a hearing, the trial court dismissed the complaints on the basis that the town ordinance was unconstitutional and exceeded the town's home rule powers to enforce a vehicle tax against commercial vehicles. The court reversed, agreeing with the town that the tax was authorized by its home rule powers. At issue was whether the phrase "except commercial motor vehicles" in the state statute applied to home rule units, rendering the ordinance unconstitutional. The court found it did not. The legislature was well aware that the statute was deemed not to limit home rule powers absent specific language. Having failed to enact specific language, the amended statute had no restrictive effect on home rule units.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the town's citations to vehicle owners was reversed and the case was remanded because the legislature did not intend to deprive home rule units of the power to tax commercial motor vehicles when it amended the vehicle code.

Village of Glenview v. Ramaker


No. 1-94-1935


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


282 Ill. App. 3d 368; 668 N.E.2d 106; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 492; 217 Ill. Dec. 921



June 27, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 13, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. P 1660486. Honorable George Zimmerman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant resident sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted judgment for plaintiff village and found the resident guilty of violating Glenview, Ill. Municipal Code § 4.7 (1959) by keeping a pot-bellied pig as a pet.


OVERVIEW: The resident obtained a pot-bellied pig as a household pet. She wrote to the village asking that § 4.7 be amended to exclude pot-bellied pigs. The village served her with a complaint alleging violation of § 4.7. The village informed her that before it would reconsider its position she would be required to submit a citizens' petition in support of revising the ordinance. The resident submitted the petition. The resident appeared in the trial court for a hearing on the violation. The trial court granted her a continuance on the condition that she remove the pet from the village. The resident complied with the trial court's ruling. The court reversed, in part, the trial court's decision. The court held that the fine imposed was excessive because she removed her pet from the village to prepare for trial and imposition of the fine did not aid enforcement. The court affirmed, in part, the trial court's decision. The ordinance was a legitimate exercise of the village's police power with a reasonable relationship to government interest and a rational basis for pet classification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision granting judgment for the village and finding the resident guilty of violating the village ordinance by keeping a pot-bellied pig as a pet. The court reversed the trial court's decision which imposed the fine.

Kemp-Golden v. Department of Children & Family Servs.


NO. 4-95-0452


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


281 Ill. App. 3d 869; 667 N.E.2d 688; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 485; 217 Ill. Dec. 599


February 21, 1996, ORAL ARGUMENT HELD  
June 26, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 29, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 94MR34. Honorable Luther H. Dearborn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother filed a complaint for declaratory relief and administrative review of a decision made by defendant Department of Children and Family Services (DCFS). The Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) granted the DFCS' motion to dismiss because the mother lacked standing. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother filed a report of possible abuse of her son by his father in accordance with the Abused and Neglected Child Reporting Act (Act), 325 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7 (1992). The mother sought administrative review of the DCFS' decision to expunge the report and a declaration that the regulatory scheme which denied her standing was unconstitutional. The court held that the complaint was properly dismissed because the mother did not have standing to seek administrative review or to raise a constitutional challenge to the administrative standing provisions. The mother was not a subject of the report entitled to seek judicial review because the Act's language indicated that a person who made a report was not considered a subject and her participation in the proceeding did not vest her with party or intervenor status. Under both the Act and the Illinois Administrative Code, only decisions that denied requests for expungement were subject to judicial review. The mother also lacked standing because she had no personal claim, status, or right which would be affected by a declaratory judgment that the standing provisions were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Watts


No. 2-95-0762


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


281 Ill. App. 3d 434; 667 N.E.2d 150; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 476; 217 Ill. Dec. 357


May 7, 1996, SUBMITTED  
June 24, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 23, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 94-CF-1754. Honorable John R. Goshgarian, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted of him of violating the Home Repair Fraud Act (Act),815 Ill. Comp. Stat. 515/1 et seq. (1994).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was acquitted of a theft charge because there was insufficient evidence to establish that he had no intention of performing his promised construction duties, but was found guilty of home repair fraud because he did not rebut the state's evidence that he had failed to employ qualified personnel. The court held that the mandatory presumption of criminal intent created by § 3 of the Act was invalid as violative of due process because it relieved the state of the affirmative burden of persuasion on the presumed element of intent or knowledge by providing that the trial court had to find the presumed element unless defendant persuaded it not to make such a finding. Defendant was prejudiced by the statutory presumption because the predicate facts offered by the state were insufficient to prove criminal intent beyond a reasonable doubt. The doctrine of collateral estoppel precluded relitigation because the controlling issue of criminal intent had been adjudicated by the acquittal on the theft charge, which was based on the finding that defendant had not accepted money for work that he had not intended to perform.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's judgment of conviction.

COUNTY COLLECTOR FOR JUDGMENT & ORDER OF SALE v. Johnson


No. 2-95-1026


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


281 Ill. App. 3d 467; 667 N.E.2d 109; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 461; 217 Ill. Dec. 316


May 7, 1996, SUBMITTED  
June 19, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 23, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 94-TX-26. Honorable R. Peter Grometer, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent property owner filed an amended motion pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1203 (1994) to vacate an order from the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) directing the county clerk to issue a tax deed to petitioner tax purchaser. The tax purchaser moved to dismiss the owner's amended motion. The trial court entered an order dismissing the amended motion. The owner appealed that order.


OVERVIEW: The tax purchaser successfully argued that tax deeds were incontestable under the Property Tax Code, specifically 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 200/22-45 (1994), except by filing an appeal or a petition under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1401 (1994). The owner did not contest the issuance of the tax deed by either of these methods. The court overturned the trial court's judgment. First, it was true that 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 200/22-45 did not permit a party to contest the issuance of a tax deed by filing a motion under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1203. For all practical purposes, 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 200/22-45 divested the trial court of jurisdiction over the matter once it entered its order, in apparent conflict with the general rule that the trial court retains jurisdiction to vacate or modify its own orders for 30 days after entry. The court ultimately concluded that § 22-45 both conflicted with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 303, 155 Ill. 2d R. 303, and unduly infringed on the inherent power of the judiciary. Thus, § 22-45 violated the separation of powers doctrine and was unconstitutional. The trial court erred in granting the tax purchaser's motion to dismiss the owner's amended motion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant estate administrator sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted appellees, doctors and hospital's, motion to dismiss with prejudice and later denied the estate administrator's motion to reconsider, which included an amended affidavit and medical report.


OVERVIEW: The estate administrator brought a malpractice complaint against the doctors and hospital. On review, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by dismissing the complaint with prejudice. The court held that the estate administrator could not amend the complaint because the error involved was not minor or technical. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by not granting leave to file the second amended affidavit and medical report because they failed to satisfy 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 2-622(a)(1)(ii).

Blue Cat Lounge v. License Appeal Comm'n


1-95-0811


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


281 Ill. App. 3d 643; 667 N.E.2d 554; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 437; 217 Ill. Dec. 465



June 11, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 94 CH 4681. The Honorable Thomas P. Durkin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowner appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed the revocation of the tavern's liquor license.


OVERVIEW: After the liquor control commission revoked a tavern's license, the owner of the land on which the tavern sat appealed. Under the terms of 235 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-13 (1992) the landowner could not operate a tavern on the property for one year following the revocation. The lower court affirmed the revocation. On appeal, the landowner claimed that the circuit court erred in striking its memorandum of law, in denying the owner's motion to realign, and in affirming the revocation of the liquor license. The court held that the legislature did not intend for the scienter requirement of 235 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/10-2 (1992) to be implied in 235 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-13 (1992). The court also held that 5/7-13 did not violate the Fourteenth Amendment of the U.S. Constitution because the liquor license was a privilege, not a property right. Further, the court held that 5/7-13 did not constitute a taking of private property in violation of the Fifth Amendment because there was no permanent deprivation of property and the landowner could use the property for other purposes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against the landowner.

People v. Morales


No. 1-94-2892


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


281 Ill. App. 3d 695; 666 N.E.2d 839; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 405; 217 Ill. Dec. 170



June 6, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 93-CR-5971. Honorable Thomas F. Dwyer, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the jury at the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) after defendant shot and killed the victim. Defendant was sentenced to a 45 year term. Defendant appealed, challenging his conviction and his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction was based on eyewitness testimony of two witnesses. He claimed that the state's use of another witness' prior inconsistent statements denied him a fair trial; that the state failed to prove that he was guilty beyond a reasonable doubt; that the jury verdict was coerced by the conditions of their deliberations in that the trial court refused to declare a hung jury after they could not initially reach a verdict. Also, the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing defendant to a 45 year term. The court found that defendant was properly convicted and sentenced, holding that: (1) while the admission some of the witness' prior statement was not proper, it was harmless error and did not violate the right to due process. (2) The evidence was not so incredible so as to raise a reasonable doubt as to defendant's guilt. (3) There was no proof that the trial court abused its discretion in requiring the jury to deliberate further. (4) The trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant because the trial court considered both the serious nature of the crime, defendant's rehabilitative potentials, and other mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Barry v. Owens-Corning Fiberglass Corp.


No. 1-94-2193


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


282 Ill. App. 3d 199; 668 N.E.2d 8; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 398; 217 Ill. Dec. 823



June 3, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 30, 1996. Released for Publication August 13, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE DEAN M. TRAFELET, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Decedent sued appellant manufacturer after he was diagnosed with mesothelioma resulting from exposure to asbestos products. He died prior to trial and appellee widow amended the complaint to assert wrongful death and survival claims pursuant to the Wrongful Death Act, 740 Ill. Comp. Stat. 180/2 (1992). After a jury in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) returned a verdict for more than 12 million dollars, the manufacturer appealed.


OVERVIEW: A manufacturer claimed various errors after a jury awarded a verdict in excess of 12 million dollars to the widow and surviving children of a worker who died from asbestos-induced mesothelioma. The court affirmed. It rejected a claim of error in the admission of a 90-second videotape of a medical procedure because it accurately depicted decedent's diseased lungs. It also declined to reverse based on the use of a mortality table showing life expectancies of surviving family members because there was no reason to believe that its use, albeit erroneous, either misled the jury or prejudiced the manufacturer. The court also found that other claimed errors, including errors relating to the language of a jury instruction and to the reading of certain expert testimony, were waived. While the verdict form that was used was incorrect, the court had no reason to conclude that its use inflated the total award. The court also declined to overturn the verdict based on amount alone. While refusing to set out a litmus test for generally determining when an award was unreasonable, the court found that, based on the evidence and the applicable law, the manufacturer was not entitled to relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered on the jury's verdict, awarding more than 12 million dollars to the widow and children of a decedent who died from asbestos-related mesothelioma.

Gollub v. Cook County (In re Estate of Janussek)


1-95-2503


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


281 Ill. App. 3d 233; 666 N.E.2d 774; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 379; 217 Ill. Dec. 105



May 28, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Frank M. Siracusa, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, children born during an intestate decedent's father's marriages in Germany (heirs), sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied the heirs' claim to establish their right as heirs of decedent's estate.


OVERVIEW: Decedent was born illegitimate in Berlin, German but was granted legitimacy based upon a petition filed by decedent's father. Decedent received his father's name pursuant to German law. Decedent's father married two times and had three more children (heirs). Decedent immigrated to the United States and died intestate in Chicago, Illinois. Respondent administrator filed a petition to probate decedent's estate. The circuit court entered an order of unknown heirs. The heirs filed petitions for heirship, which was denied by the circuit court. The heirs claimed on appeal that they could inherit from the decedent's estate because they were descendants of the decedent's father. The administrator claimed that the heirs could not inherit under the Probate Act because they would not have inherited decedent's estate under German law. The court agreed with the heirs' claims. The court ruled that heirs were entitled to their share of the decedent's estate under 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1(d), (h), because the decedent's legitimacy under German law was recognized in Illinois.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment that denied the heirs' petition for heirship and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

662 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Nordstrom v. Wauconda Nat'l Bank


No. 2-95-1221


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


282 Ill. App. 3d 142; 668 N.E.2d 586; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 532; 218 Ill. Dec. 102



May 24, 1996, SUBMITTED  
July 9, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 26, 1996. Released for Publication August 26, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 94--L--980. Honorable Bernard E. Drew, Jr., Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff debtors challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which dismissed two of the debtors' claims against defendant creditor bank as barred by the Illinois Credit Agreements Act (act), 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. 160/1 et seq. (1994).


OVERVIEW: The debtors argued that the act did not preclude a claim of promissory estoppel and that the act was unconstitutional because it violated equal protection and due process. On appeal, the court held that the act required every credit agreement or modification thereof to be in writing. The court found that the alleged modification of the agreement, which provided that the creditor bank would procure insurance, was not in writing. The court held that the statement by the creditor bank's agent that she would take care of the insurance was an unenforceable oral modification of the original written contractual agreement. The court held that the act prohibited the debtors from asserting promissory estoppel or breach of contract claims based on the alleged oral modification. The court held that the act did not affect a fundamental right or involve a suspect classification, and therefore the act was constitutional because it was is rationally related to a legitimate state interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the trial court, which dismissed the debtors' promissory estoppel and breach of contract claims against the creditor bank.

 

663 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Lou Owen, Inc. v. Village of Schaumburg


No. 1-95-0157


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


279 Ill. App. 3d 976; 665 N.E.2d 456; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 292; 216 Ill. Dec. 396



April 26, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Lester Foreman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant village appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which issued a preliminarily injunction that enjoined the enforcement of a municipal ordinance banning commercial teen dances such as those conducted by plaintiff license holder. The trial court held that the ordinance did not satisfy the strictures of equal protection and did not bear a reasonable relationship to its intended purpose.


OVERVIEW: The license holder obtained a license to conduct commercial teen dances and operate a teen nightclub. The village passed an ordinance that limited teen dances to those held in hotels and sponsored by non-profit groups. Because the effect of the ordinance was that the license holder could no longer conduct his business, he sought to enjoin enforcement of the ordinance. The court affirmed the circuit court's holding that the ordinance was facially unconstitutional as violative of equal protection. The court examined the evidence and held that the circuit judge's implicit finding that the restraints imposed by the ordinance were not necessary to secure the common welfare was not against the manifest weight of the evidence and that he did not abuse his discretion when he granted the preliminary injunction to prevent enforcement of the ordinance. The evidence established teen dances held in hotels or sponsored by non-profit groups were no safer than teen dances that were held elsewhere or sponsored by for-profit enterprises. Therefore, the ordinance did not bear a reasonable relationship to its stated purpose, which was to make teen dances safer.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, which enjoined the enforcement of a village ordinance, was affirmed and the case was remanded to the circuit court.

 

664 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Secor


No. 3-95-0571


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


279 Ill. App. 3d 389; 664 N.E.2d 1054; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 289; 216 Ill. Dec. 126


February 14, 1996, SUBMITTED  
April 23, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 28, 1996. Released for Publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois, No. 95-CF-405. Honorable Amy Bertani, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit (Illinois) of one count of criminal sexual assault in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-13(a)(4) (1994), and one count of aggravated criminal sexual abuse in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-16(d) (1994). He was sentenced to concurrent terms of six and three years imprisonment. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of molesting his son's friend when the friend was spending the night at his house with his son. Defendant's family and the victim's family had a history of allowing the children to sleep over at the other family's house. On appeal defendant contended in part that the state failed to prove him guilty of criminal sexual assault beyond a reasonable doubt and that § 12-13(a)(4) of the Criminal Code of 1961 was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed. First, the court held that the state produced sufficient evidence that defendant occupied a position of trust or supervision in relation to the victim. Second, the court rejected defendant's argument that the phrase "held a position of trust, authority or supervision" in § 12-13(a)(4) was so vague and undefined that it left enforcement of the law to the whim of the arresting officer, judge or jury. The terms "trust," "authority," and "supervision" were sufficiently definite to warn potential defendants of the type of conduct that was prohibited and to channel the discretion of police, judges, and juries. Finally, the court held that § 12-13(a)(4) was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for criminal sexual assault and aggravated criminal sexual abuse.

Granberg v. Didrickson


No. 1-96-0443


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


279 Ill. App. 3d 886; 665 N.E.2d 398; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 267; 216 Ill. Dec. 338



April 16, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Aaron Jaffe, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state officials appealed the order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granting plaintiff state representatives' request for a preliminary injunction.


OVERVIEW: The representatives voted against an appropriation of $ 15,792,000 to the Department of Transportation Road Fund for use by the Department of State Police. The representatives sought injunctive relief prohibiting vouchers or warrants authorizing expenditure of the appropriated funds arguing that under § 8.3 of the State Finance Act, 30 Ill. Comp. Stat. 105/8.3 (1994), monies in the Road Fund may be appropriated to the Department of State Police only under certain conditions which were not met in this case. The officials sought review of the trial court decision granting the preliminary injunction on the basis that the legislature could not amend a substantive bill with an appropriation bill. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment from the trial court. The court held that the General Assembly attempted with the appropriation to allocate monies from the Road Fund to the State Police in violation of the State Finance Act. The court further held that if the additional $ 15,792,000 were needed for police services, all that would be required is for the General Assembly and the governor to enact into law either a supplemental appropriations bill or amend the State Finance Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the trial court and converted the preliminary injunction order into a permanent injunction.

Tucker v. St. James Hosp.


No. 1-93-2371


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


279 Ill. App. 3d 696; 665 N.E.2d 392; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 256; 216 Ill. Dec. 332



April 15, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Sidney A. Jones, III, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient brought a medical malpractice action against defendant physician and codefendant hospitals. The patient failed to attach to his complaint an attorney's affidavit or a health professional's report, as required by Ill. Code Civ. P. 735, Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-622. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the physician's and the hospitals' motions, and dismissed the case with prejudice. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient claimed the trial court abused its discretion in refusing to allow the case to be tried on the merits. The patient filed an unsworn, undated affidavit declaring that his witness was knowledgeable in the relevant issues and had determined in a written report that there was a meritorious cause of action. The affidavit stated that it was made under oath, however, spaces for the date and signature of a notary public were left blank. There was no indication that an oath was actually administered. The witness states in his report that he was not a surgeon and that he was unable to assess whether the doctor was negligent. The court held the patient did not submit an adequate health professional's report or attorney affidavit, and the trial court acted well within its discretion in dismissing the action after providing plaintiff with numerous opportunities to comply with Ill. Code Civ. P. 735, Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-622. The trial court made every reasonable effort to afford the patient extra time to comply. Even if the patient's affidavit and health professional's report were sufficient, the documents were filed long after the statutory period had expired.


OUTCOME: The trial court's dismissal of the patient's action and denial of his motion to vacate were affirmed.

PEOPLE v. ONE SINGLE FAMILY RESIDENCE


NO. 5-94-0682


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


278 Ill. App. 3d 1097; 663 N.E.2d 1104; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 187; 215 Ill. Dec. 590



April 3, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Franklin County. No. 93-MR-18. Honorable Terrence J. Hopkins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Franklin County (Illinois), which granted defendants' and intervenor purchaser's motion for summary judgment in the state's forfeiture action of a residence that had drugs in it.


OVERVIEW: The state filed a complaint for forfeiture seeking the forfeiture of a residence alleging that pursuant to a search warrant, police had found drugs in the residence. The purchaser filed a motion to intervene. Defendants and the purchaser filed a joint motion for summary judgment arguing that because defendant had been convicted of possession but acquitted of possession with intent to deliver, forfeiture constituted multiple prosecution and punishment for the same offense in violation of the double jeopardy clause. The trial court granted the motion for summary judgment, and the state appealed. The court affirmed, concluding that although defendant was not convicted of a violation of § 401 of the Controlled Substances Act, the violation upon which the forfeiture was based, she was prosecuted for it, and the double jeopardy clause prohibited multiple prosecutions for the same offense. The court held that forfeiture of the defendant's residence constituted punishment for double jeopardy purposes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant and intervenor in the state's forfeiture action of defendant's residence.

People v. Tooles


No. 3-94-0627


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


278 Ill. App. 3d 756; 663 N.E.2d 1085; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 185; 215 Ill. Dec. 571


June 7, 1995, SUBMITTED  
April 1, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 9, 1996. As Corrected July 1, 1996. As Corrected July 17, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County, Illinois. No. 92-CF-831. Honorable John Michela, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court for the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County, Illinois, which convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual assault and one count of criminal sexual assault. Defendant argued that the absence of a written jury waiver pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115-1 (1992) required a reversal of his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of criminal sexual assault and one count of aggravated criminal sexual assault. Defendant pleaded not guilty and demanded a jury trial. Defendant then orally waived his right to a jury trial, but no written waiver was executed. Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted of criminal sexual assault. Defendant appealed, claiming that the absence of a written jury waiver required a reversal of his conviction. The court reversed the judgment and held that, pursuant to § 5/115-1, defendant could not have waived his right to a jury trial without the waiver having been in writing. The purpose of the statute effectuated the constitutional right to a jury trial. No court rules conflicted with the written waiver requirement, so the statute did not violate the separation of powers clause of the state constitution. After reviewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the prosecution, the court concluded that the state had presented sufficient evidence to have permitted defendant to have been retried.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for sexual assault and remanded for a new trial.

People v. Farmer


No. 3-94-0163 (Cons. with Nos. 3-94-0164 & 3-94-0165)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 186; 233 Ill. Dec. 722



April 1, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23 ORDER.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 9, 1996. The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Published to Unpublished (May 1, 1996).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County, Illinois. Nos. 91-CF-625, 91-CF-798 & 93-CF-29.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from the judgment of the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County (Illinois), which convicted him in a bench trial of unlawful possession of cannabis and unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. His probation from his convictions for two counts of unlawful possession of a controlled substance was revoked and he was sentenced to terms of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his convictions for all counts had to be reversed because he did not make a written waiver of a jury trial as required under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115-1 (1994). The State contended that defendant failed to preserve the issue for appeal, that a written jury waiver was not required, that the statute requiring written waivers was unconstitutional, and that any error was harmless. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, holding that defendant was entitled to a new trial on his convictions for unlawful possession of cannabis and unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver because 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115 (1994), requiring all criminal trials to be tried before a jury unless defendant waived the jury trial in writing, was constitutional and mandatory. The failure to hold the jury trial absent defendant's written waiver constituted plain error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for two counts of unlawful possession of a controlled substance, reversed his convictions for unlawful possession of cannabis and unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, and remanded the matter for a new trial.

People v. Williams


No. 1-95-1399


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


279 Ill. App. 3d 22; 664 N.E.2d 164; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 237; 215 Ill. Dec. 767



March 29, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE MICHAEL J. POPE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), which denied his motion to dismiss an indictment charging him with arson and felony murder.


OVERVIEW: The state brought charges of arson and felony murder against defendant and received a conviction that was later affirmed on appeal. However, the state's highest court then ruled that the arson statute was unconstitutional. Defendant successfully filed a petition for habeas corpus, which the trial court granted. On the same day, the state charged defendant by indictment with non-aggravated arson and felony murder. These charges were not brought in the original indictment. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the indictment, but the trial court denied the motion. The court affirmed. Under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. § 5/3-4(d)(2) the state was allowed to reprosecute if subsequent proceedings resulted in the invalidation, setting aside, reversal, or vacating of the conviction, unless defendant thereby was adjudged not guilty. Contrary to defendant's assertion, the writ of habeas corpus was not the functional equivalent of an acquittal. Additionally, the fact that the prior judgment was vacated due to the unconstitutionality of the statute was not an acquittal absent some suggestion that the evidence was insufficient to convict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that denied defendant's motion to dismiss an indictment charging him with arson and felony murder.

Department of Corrections ex rel. State v. Adams


NO. 4-94-1050


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


278 Ill. App. 3d 803; 663 N.E.2d 1145; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 285; 215 Ill. Dec. 631


September 11, 1995, SUBMITTED  
March 26, 1996, FILED; April 23, 1996, NUNC PRO TUNC


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rule 23 Order Redesignated Opinion and Ordered Published April 23, 1996. Released for Publication April 23, 1996. As Corrected August 28, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Logan County. No. 92L42. Honorable Gerald G. Dehner, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment in favor of plaintiff state in an action to recover costs of incarceration pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-7-6 (1992) in the Circuit Court of Logan County (Illinois). Defendant complained that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The state filed an action against defendant to recover the costs of incarceration pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-7-6. At trial, defendant presented no evidence, and the state prevailed. Defendant appealed, asserting that the statute was unconstitutional as violative of the ex post facto clause, constituted cruel and unusual punishment under the Eighth Amendment, was a due process violation, and that the state did not prove his ability to pay. The court affirmed and found that the ex post facto clause only applied to penal statutes and that the statute at issue was not penal in nature. Using the same analysis, the statute was not cruel and unusual punishment, either. As to the due process allegation, the court held that the statute was not void for vagueness and it clearly informed defendant of the elements of the statute. Further, as the statute was compensatory and not penal, the vagueness analysis was not applicable. Finally, the court found that defendant was required to show his inability to pay in order for that issue to be considered. As defendant did not make that showing, it was not considered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding of the trial court in favor of the state.

People v. Bryant

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION

Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by People v. Bryant, 394 Ill. App. 3d 1101, 985 N.E.2d 1078, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 5407, 369 Ill. Dec. 92 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2009)

Straub v. Zollar


No. 1-94-2367


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


278 Ill. App. 3d 556; 663 N.E.2d 80; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 146; 215 Ill. Dec. 330



March 20, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Edwin M. Berman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff dentist challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County dismissing his complaint for administrative review of a decision by the department of professional regulation (department) suspending his license to practice dentistry.


OVERVIEW: The dentist was under a consent order to complete continuing education classes after it was found that he furnished inferior services. When he failed to comply with the order, the department filed a complaint with the Board of Dentistry (board) seeking to revoke or suspend his license. The board recommended to the director of the department that the dentist's license be suspended until he completed the courses. The director suspended the dentist's license. The dentist then filed a complaint for administrative review, naming the director as the sole defendant. The trial court dismissed the complaint with prejudice as being noncompliant with the Administrative Review Law, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-107. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that because both the director and the department were parties to the proceedings, the clear and unambiguous language of § 3-107 required that they both be named and served. In addition, the court refused to retroactively apply the amendment to § 3-107, which would have provided the dentist with time to correct the defect, finding the amendment to be substantive rather than procedural, thus necessitating prospective not retroactive application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the dentist's complaint for review of a decision by the department to suspend his license to practice dentistry, finding that the dentist failed to comply with the Administrative Review Law.

Village of Schaumburg v. Doyle


No. 1-94-0460


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


277 Ill. App. 3d 832; 661 N.E.2d 496; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 54; 214 Ill. Dec. 642



February 5, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE LESTER D. FOREMAN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a village and its manager, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motion to dismiss filed by defendant Department of Agriculture of Illinois in the village's declaratory judgment action regarding the constitutionality of an amendment to the Pesticide Act.


OVERVIEW: The village brought a declaratory judgment action against the Department of Agriculture (department) and sought to have an amendment to the Pesticide Act declared unconstitutional. The trial court granted the department's motion to dismiss and the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the village was not a "person" as that term was embraced by the equal protection provisions U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1, and Ill. Const. art. II, § 2 (1970). The court held that the village had no standing to pursue its due process and equal protection challenges to P.A. 88-345. The court held that the rational basis test applied and that such test did not require the legislature to explain why it drew the line at 2 million people. The court held that mathematical precision in creating a classification was not required. The court held that the village had not established in its pleadings that the general assembly failed the rational basis test. The court held that it was not unreasonable to presume that large population centers would have the resources, expertise, and will to deal with the regulation of pesticides. The court found that the amendment was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that granted the department of agriculture's motion to dismiss for failure to state a cause of action in the village's declaratory judgment action regarding the constitutionality of an amendment to the Pesticide Act.

People v. Parker


NO. 4-94-0402


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


277 Ill. App. 3d 585; 660 N.E.2d 1296; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 20; 214 Ill. Dec. 347


September 11, 1995, SUBMITTED  
January 25, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 1, 1996. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied April 3, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Adams County. No. 93CF302. Honorable Dennis K. Cashman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Adams County (Illinois), which convicted him of unlawful possession of a controlled substance, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/402 (1992), and permitting the unlawful use of a building, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/406.1 (1992). The trial court sentenced him to four years' imprisonment on each count, with the sentences to run concurrently.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for permitting the unlawful use of a building, arguing the statute was unconstitutional and he was not proved guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the language of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570-406.1(a) was not so vague that persons of common intelligence could not assess its meaning or application. Because 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570-406.1(a) contained a criminal knowledge element, the statute was not overly broad and did not penalize innocent behavior. The court rejected defendant's argument that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570-406.1(a) and 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/37-1 prohibited the same acts and imposed different penalties. While an individual charged with permitting an unlawful use of a building could also be charged with maintaining a public nuisance, the opposite was not always true. Accordingly, the statutes were not identical and did not violate the constitutional prohibition against disproportionate penalties. From the evidence, any rational trier of fact could conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant exerted control over the residence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and defendant's convictions for unlawful possession of a controlled substance and permitting the unlawful use of a building.
