People v. Potts


No. 3-94-0781


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


277 Ill. App. 3d 567; 660 N.E.2d 560; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 11; 214 Ill. Dec. 115



January 12, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County, Illinois. No. 94-CF-509. Honorable John Michela, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from the judgment of the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County (Illinois), which convicted him in a bench trial of possession of explosive or incendiary devices and sentenced him to a six-year term of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was denied the right of a jury trial because he did not make a written waiver of a jury trial as required under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115-1 (1994). The State contended the issue was not reviewable because defendant failed to raise the issue with the trial court, that a written jury waiver was not required, that the statute requiring written waivers was unconstitutional, and that any error was harmless. The court reversed, holding that defendant was entitled to a new trial because 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115-1 (1994), requiring all criminal trials to be tried before a jury unless defendant waived the jury trial in writing, was constitutional and mandatory. The failure to hold a jury trial absent defendant's written waiver constituted plain error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the matter for a new trial.

 

678 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Cavarretta v. Department of Children & Family Servs.


No. 2-95-0462


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


277 Ill. App. 3d 16; 660 N.E.2d 250; 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 6; 214 Ill. Dec. 59


December 5, 1995, SUBMITTED  
January 5, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 94-MR-226. Honorable Bernard E. Drew, Jr., Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, accused abuser (accused), filed an action against defendants, Department of Children and Family Services and its officials (collectively Department), under 325 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7.16 of the Abused and Neglected Child Reporting Act, 325 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/21 et seq. (1994), to expunge his name from the state register of child molesters. The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) ruled for the accused. The Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The accused's hearing to expunge his name from the state register of child molesters was held 299 days after his request. The Department's denial was 581 days after his request. The court affirmed the decision to expunge his name. The accused had a protected liberty interest in not having been listed on the register because the listing endangered his employment as a teacher and endangered his teaching certificate under 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/21-23(b) (1994) and his ability to obtain certain employment under 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/8(9) (1994). Thus, the listing affected more than his reputation. The Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, 325 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7.16 (1994), and Ill. Admin. Code tit. 89, § 336.110(d)(1) (1994) entitled the accused to a timely hearing to expunge his name. The court held that the delay violated this right, he did not waive the argument, and he did not have to proceed in mandamus to correct the delay. The credible evidence standard of Ill. Admin. Code tit. 89, § 336.130(b)(14) violated the accused's due process rights because the standard of proof should have been preponderance of the evidence, which was not met.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision for the accused against the Department in his action to expunge his name from the state register of child molesters.

 

679 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Wells v. Industrial Comm'n


No. 1-95-1133WC


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, INDUSTRIAL COMMISSION DIVISION


277 Ill. App. 3d 379; 660 N.E.2d 229; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 977; 214 Ill. Dec. 38



December 29, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 94 L 50100. Honorable Alexander White, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant longshoreman filed claims for workers' compensation coverage under the Illinois Workers' Compensation Act and under the Longshore and Harbor Workers' Compensation Act (LHWCA), 33 U.S.C.S. § 901 et seq. Appellee Illinois Industrial Commission (commission) awarded benefits. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) upheld the award in part. The longshoreman and appellee stevedore company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The stevedore company argued that the commission lacked subject matter jurisdiction to consider the longshoreman's application for benefits. It contended that at the time of the injury, the longshoreman was injured while performing his duties over navigable waters of the United States; that injuries sustained by the longshoreman were within the exclusive jurisdiction of the LHWCA; and that the longshoreman could only be compensated under the provisions of the LHWCA. The court agreed, holding that the commission lacked subject matter jurisdiction to consider the longshoreman's application for benefits and to award benefits because his claim for compensation for his injury fell within exclusive federal jurisdiction. Under the Jensen doctrine, states could not constitutionally apply their workers' compensation statutory schemes to maritime employees who were performing traditional maritime functions and were injured over navigable waters. Working as a longshoreman was clearly a traditional maritime activity. Moreover, longshoremen injured over navigable waters fell outside the concurrent jurisdiction of the Davis "twilight zone."


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court upholding in part the commission's award of benefits to the longshoreman under the Illinois Workers' Compensation Act.

 

680 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Jenkins v. Leininger


1-93-1456


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


277 Ill. App. 3d 313; 659 N.E.2d 1366; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 956; 213 Ill. Dec. 719



December 22, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE AARON JAFFE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, parents of and low-income students, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed plaintiffs' complaint with prejudice, finding that they failed to state a cause of action regarding an alleged violation of Ill. Const. art. X, § 1, which guaranteed an efficient and high-quality education. Plaintiffs alleged deprivation of parental rights to control the education of their children.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, parents of and low-income students, filed a claim against defendants, superintendent and state and city boards of education, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief, alleging deprivation of parental rights to control and influence the education of their children. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's dismissal in favor of defendants. The court found that the parents had not alleged actionable conduct that was arbitrary, unreasonable, or capricious, and their complaint failed to state a cause of action under Ill. Const. art. X. The court concluded that the right to a high quality education was not a "fundamental right" for purposes of an equal protection claim. The court found that the parents' complaint had failed to set forth factual allegations of disparate treatment that was not rationally related to a governmental purpose. The court reasoned that the state's reliance on residence for school assignment determinations was rationally related to the purpose of providing an educational system to all residents. The court concluded that the equal protection claim had been properly dismissed because the parents had failed to allege facts of unequal treatment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court, holding that plaintiffs', parents of and low-income students, complaint failed to state a cause of action under the state constitution.

 

681 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Soto


No. 1-93-1934


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


277 Ill. App. 3d 433; 660 N.E.2d 990; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 952; 214 Ill. Dec. 283



December 21, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing January 25, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Richard E. Neville, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated stalking in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-7.4(a)(3) (1992).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of aggravated stalking, arguing that the Illinois stalking and aggravated stalking statutes, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-7.3 and 5/12-7.4 (1992), were unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the matter for resentencing, holding that the statutes were constitutional. However, the order of protection entered into evidence by the state did not state the reason that it was issued. The state presented no testimony concerning the circumstances leading up to the issuance of the order. Defendant argued that the state failed to establish the predicate threat beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that the standard of proof which had to have been met at an order of protection hearing was only a preponderance of the evidence. That burden did not satisfy the quantum of proof required to sustain a criminal conviction. Thus, standing alone, the order of protection did not constitute sufficient evidence that defendant threatened the victim. Nothing in the record showed that defendant expressed an intent to harm the victim. Therefore, there was no proof beyond a reasonable doubt of a predicate threat.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which convicted defendant for aggravated stalking. The court remanded the matter for resentencing.

 

682 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


City of Chicago v. Youkhana


1-93-3909


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


277 Ill. App. 3d 101; 660 N.E.2d 34; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 934; 213 Ill. Dec. 777



December 18, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Thaddeus L. Kowalski, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed the grant to defendants of their motion to dismiss their convictions under the city's gang-loitering ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Code § 8-4-015 (1992), by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). The city argued that § 8-4-015 was a valid exercise of its police power and that it did not violate the U.S. or Illinois Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were arrested for loitering and charged with violating the ordinance in the city that was aimed at curbing street gangs. During their prosecution, defendants filed a motion to dismiss, arguing that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The trial court granted the motion, and the city appealed. The court affirmed. The court held that the ordinance violated defendants' freedoms of association, assembly, and expression secured by the First Amendment and Ill. Const. art. I, § 5. It had a chilling effect on those rights. It was unconstitutionally vague, so it violated defendants' due process rights. The ordinance unconstitutionally criminalized status by prohibiting gang members from loitering because they were gang members, not because they were loitering. It was the status, not the conduct that triggered the ordinance. Criminal penalties could be imposed only if there was a criminal act. The ordinance allowed arrests without probable cause in violation of the Fourth Amendment. In fact, the ordinance appeared to be a transparent attempt to avoid the probable cause requirement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of defendants' motion to dismiss their loitering convictions. The city's gang ordinance was not enforced because it violated the U.S. and Illinois Constitutions.

People v. Webb


No. 3-94-0844


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


276 Ill. App. 3d 570; 658 N.E.2d 852; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 928; 213 Ill. Dec. 103



December 7, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 10, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 13th Judicial Circuit, LaSalle County, Illinois. No. 94-CF-138. Honorable H. Chris Ryan, Jr., Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; order vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of the 13th Judicial Circuit, LaSalle County (Illinois), which ordered that her bond money, which was posted by her boyfriend, be used to reimburse the county for the services of the public defender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with unlawful delivery of a controlled substance. Bail was set and a warrant for defendant's arrest was issued. Upon her arrest, defendant filed an affidavit of assets and liabilities showing no income, assets, liabilities, or resources. The trial court found defendant indigent and appointed a public defender to represent her. Defendant pleaded not guilty and moved for a reduction of bail, which was denied. The matter was tried by a jury and resulted in an acquittal. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the trial court's order requiring defendant to reimburse the county for the public defender's services was contrary to the manifest weight of the evidence and an abuse of discretion. There was no evidence that defendant had any funds or any foreseeable ability to pay attorney fees. The court rejected the State's suggestion that the hearing passed constitutional due process muster because the boyfriend never testified that any recoupment would result in a financial burden to him. The court found that defendant complied with the conditions and there was no reasonable notice that the public defender's services were to be paid for out of the bond deposit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order of reimbursement for services of the public defender provided to defendant.

Westshire Retirement & Healthcare Ctr. v. Department of Pub. Aid


NO. 1-93-3885


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


276 Ill. App. 3d 514; 658 N.E.2d 1286; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 897; 213 Ill. Dec. 265



December 4, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied April 3, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE MARY JANE THEIS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both plaintiff Medicaid facility and defendants, Illinois Department of Public Aid (IDPA) and director, appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, on cross-motions for summary judgment, held that the 1985 regulation was arbitrary and capricious and violated Illinois statutory law, but ruled that the Medicaid facility had failed to prove any damages and denied its motions to amend its complaint and for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: The Medicaid facility challenged the validity and legality of a regulation, Ill. Admin. Code tit. 89, § 140.571(e), promulgated by IDPA. The circuit court granted the Medicaid facility summary judgment on its claims that the 1985 amendments were invalidated and violated part of the Medical Assistance Act, 305 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-1 et seq. (1992), but it ruled against the Medicaid facility otherwise. The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to the Medicaid facility due to lack of subject matter jurisdiction. Sovereign immunity mandated that the state or a department of the state could not be a defendant in an action brought directly in the circuit court, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 505/1 et seq. (1992). Where a judgment for the Medicaid facility would operate to control IDPA action or subject it to damage liability, the action was effectively against the state and was barred. Where the IDPA and its director were named as defendants and no writ of mandamus was sought against the relevant state officer, the circuit court lacked jurisdiction. Also, it was not error to deny the Medicaid facility leave to amend because its amendment did not go to the jurisdictional question.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's grant of summary judgment to the Medicaid facility on two counts and remanded for further proceedings consistent with the opinion and with directions to dismiss both counts for lack of jurisdiction.

Miller v. Department of Professional Regulation


No. 2-95-0259


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


276 Ill. App. 3d 133; 658 N.E.2d 523; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 892; 213 Ill. Dec. 53



December 1, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 4, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 93-MR-56. Honorable James C. Franz, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the department of professional regulation and its director, challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois), which vacated the department's cease and desist order directing appellee, a consultant, to refrain from violating the Professional Engineering Practice Act of 1989, 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 325/1 et seq. (1992). The engineer had filed an action seeking administrative review and a reversal of the order.


OVERVIEW: The consultant had a degree in electrical/electronic engineering but was not a licensed professional engineer. In his investigative engineering practice, he testified as an expert and used the term "Engineer." The department alleged that he violated the Professional Engineering Practice Act of 1989 (1989 Act), 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 325/1 et seq. (1992), by engaging in the unlicensed practice of professional engineering and issued a cease and desist order. The circuit court vacated the order. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and held that: (1) prior to the 1989 Act, which replaced the Professional Engineering Act of 1945 (1945 Act), the consultant did not have to be licensed as a professional engineer because investigative engineering was not within the purview of the 1945 Act; (2) he did not have a right to be "grandfathered" in because due process did not exempt him from the licensing requirements of the 1989 Act or require the department to issue him a license, but it required that he had a fair opportunity to take the professional competency examination; and (3) there was a rational basis for requiring professional engineers to pass an examination for licensure.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment, which vacated the department's cease and desist order directing the consultant to refrain from violating the Professional Engineering Practice Act of 1989 in his action against the department and the director seeking reversal of the cease and desist order. The court reinstated the order.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his sentence for and conviction of aggravated sexual assault and armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault and armed robbery for his participation in a robbery and sexual assault with several other perpetrators. Defendant contended that the evidence did not support a guilty verdict, and that consecutive sentences were inappropriate. Village of Riverwoods v. BG Ltd. Partnership


Nos. 1-93-1964 & 1-94-0463 Consolidated


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


276 Ill. App. 3d 720; 658 N.E.2d 1261; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 894; 213 Ill. Dec. 240



December 1, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE THOMAS O'BRIEN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff village filed a suit against defendant department of transportation (department) and construction company (company) alleging trespass. The department filed a motion to dismiss, and the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the motion. The company then filed a motion to dismiss, claiming that the department was a necessary party to the action. The trial court granted the motion, and the village appealed both orders.


OVERVIEW: The village's suit was based on the department's and company's construction work on land allegedly owned by the village. The trial court held that because of sovereign immunity of the department, it lacked jurisdiction of the subject matter of the action pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-619(a)(1). The court held that the trial court did not have subject matter jurisdiction to resolve the property dispute in this matter because the Court of Claims had exclusive jurisdiction over all claims against the state founded upon any law in Illinois. The court held further that even if the village had no remedy available in the Court of Claims, codification of public policy was for the legislature, and the lack of a remedy could not grant jurisdiction to a circuit court over subject matter which was specifically barred by statute. In addition, in regard to the company's claim that the department was a necessary party, the court held that because the village failed to cite any authority to support its claim that the department was not a necessary party, the village waived this argument in its appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of attempted first degree murder, aggravated battery with a firearm, and aggravated battery after he shot his former girlfriend. Defendant argued that 720 Ill. People v. Sandham


NO. 4-94-0212


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


276 Ill. App. 3d 86; 657 N.E.2d 719; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 824; 212 Ill. Dec. 518


September 19, 1995, ORAL ARGUMENT HELD  
November 7, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 11, 1995. As Corrected January 9, 1996. Petition for Leave to Appeal Allowed January 31, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Livingston County. No. 93CF59. Honorable Charles H. Frank, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted after a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois) of aggravated criminal sexual abuse under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-16(c)(1)(i) (1992). Defendant appealed, challenging the sufficiency of the evidence, the waiver of his right to a jury trial, and the failure of the trial court to have ordered sua sponte a fitness hearing.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The findings of a physical examination of the two-year-old victim were consistent with sexual abuse. In open court, defense counsel, after admonishment by the trial court, stated that defendant waived his right to a jury trial. Before trial, defense counsel asked to employ a psychiatrist to determine defendant's fitness, but no motion was filed. The presentence report stated that defendant received psychiatric treatment and suffered a chemical imbalance. The court held that under the circumstances, the waiver was knowingly made. Failure to obtain a written waiver did not always require reversal. In defendant's case, the error was harmless. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by not ordering sua sponte a fitness hearing prior to trial or sentencing under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/104-11(a) (1992). There was no evidence as to the nature of the treatment that defendant received. Defendant's conduct at trial showed that he understood the proceedings. The trial court properly allowed defendant to introduce trial testimony of his reputation for good moral character but not testimony of specific acts or personal opinion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated criminal sexual abuse.

People v. Sowewimo


1-93-2771


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


276 Ill. App. 3d 330; 657 N.E.2d 1047; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 808; 212 Ill. Dec. 702



October 27, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 12, 1995. Released for Publication December 21, 1995. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied April 3, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE DANIEL J. KELLEY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of two counts of aggravated sexual assault, aggravated unlawful restraint, stalking, aggravated stalking, attempted first-degree murder, and aggravated discharge of a weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of aggravated sexual assault, aggravated unlawful restraint, stalking, aggravated stalking, attempted first-degree murder, and aggravated discharge of a weapon. The court affirmed in part and vacated in part. The court held that defendant was not denied his constitution right to testify on his own behalf because the trial court's admonitions, which allegedly caused defendant to forego testifying, were not improper. The court found that the trial court's comments were not intimidating or threatening, instead the admonishments were given in a proper manner, and the court did not depart from its neutral judicial role. The court found that defendant's conviction for aggravated discharge of a firearm could not stand because the attempted murder count was based on the same act by defendant, thus the greater offense of attempted murder was affirmed, and the conviction for aggravated discharge of a firearm was vacated. Similarly, because stalking was a lesser-included offense of aggravated stalking, defendant's stalking conviction was also vacated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment that convicted defendant of aggravated sexual assault, aggravated unlawful restraint, aggravated stalking and attempted murder. The court vacated the conviction of aggravated discharge of a firearm because it was a lessor-included offense of attempted murder as it was based on the same act by defendant; the court vacated the stalking conviction as a lesser-included offense of aggravated stalking.

People v. Moss


No. 1-92-3988


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


275 Ill. App. 3d 748; 656 N.E.2d 193; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 755; 212 Ill. Dec. 40



September 29, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 3, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable James M. Schreier, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault and sentenced him to an extended prison term.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for the aggravated criminal sexual assault of his girlfriend's daughter and challenged: (1) the constitutionality of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-10 under the confrontation clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, § 8; (2) the reliability of statements made by an unavailable declarant which were admitted the challenged statute; (3) whether such testimony was cumulative; (4) the court's refusal to instruct the jury on the offense of aggravated criminal sexual abuse, and (5) whether the trial court properly sentenced him. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held the challenged statute did not violate the Illinois Constitution, that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding that certain hearsay testimony of the deceased victim given by her brother had the sufficient indicia of reliability, and that such testimony was not cumulative. The court also concluded that the trial court did not err in refusing defendant's instruction on aggravated criminal sexual abuse. Finally, the court did not err in sentencing defendant to an extended term because of his prior criminal record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of aggravated criminal sexual assault and his extended prison term sentence.

 

694 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Chicago Title & Trust Co. v. Village of Greenwood (In re Petition to Incorporate Village of Greenwood)


No. 2-95-0034 & 2-95-0053 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


275 Ill. App. 3d 465; 655 N.E.2d 1196; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 734; 211 Ill. Dec. 813



September 22, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 23, 1995. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 6, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 94-MC-5. Honorable Haskell M. Pitluck, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A petition was filed pursuant to § 2-3-5 of the Illinois Municipal Code (65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-3-5 (1994)) in the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois), which sought to incorporate certain territory as a village. Objectors, municipality and trust company (collectively objectors), contended that § 2-3-5 was unconstitutional and appealed an order overruling the objections and calling for an election.


OVERVIEW: The petition to incorporate a village pursuant to § 2-3-5 of the Municipal Code (65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-3-5 (1994)) was filed and objections to the petition were filed. The objections were overruled and an election was ordered. In dismissing the objectors' appeal the court held that the order directing that an election be held did not finally determine the rights of the parties and was not final and appealable. A final order under § 5/28-4 imposed procedural requirements and was final only as to those requirements. It did not confer jurisdiction on the appellate court, even if the trial court stated that it was appealable. The trial court's role did not end when the election was ordered, but when the election results were declared and entered.


OUTCOME: The court found that the order directing that an election be held was not a final order and dismissed the objectors' appeal for lack of jurisdiction.

 

695 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Thompson


No. 1-93-1487


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


275 Ill. App. 3d 725; 656 N.E.2d 77; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 728; 211 Ill. Dec. 885



September 20, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 3, 1995. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied January 31, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Loretta Morgan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) after he was convicted following a bench trial of aggravated home repair fraud in violation of 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. 515/3, 515/5 (1992) and theft in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/16-1(A)(1)(A) (1992).


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that (1) the Home Repair Fraud Act (Act), 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. 515/1 et. seq. (1992), violated state and federal due process of law in that it did not require a culpable mental state; (2) the Act's penalty provisions violated state and federal due process of law and equal protection because the class of penalty was increased on the basis of the contract's amount instead of the value of the actual loss or harm caused; and (3) his sentence violated due process of law and the constitutional assurances of proportionate penalties. The court held that the Act: (1) criminalized conduct based on fraud or deceptive practices used in the field of home repairs and did not include potentially innocent conduct within its scope; (2) was rationally related to the legislature's goal in enacting it; (3) was a reasonable means of achieving the legislative goal because it operated to criminalize precisely the type of conduct that the legislature sought to prevent by its enactment; and (4) was constitutional on its face. The court ruled that there was no equal protection violation in the imposition of defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for aggravated home repair fraud and theft.

 

696 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Reuben H. Donnelley Corp. v. Brauer


1-93-0710


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


275 Ill. App. 3d 300; 655 N.E.2d 1162; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 719; 211 Ill. Dec. 779



September 15, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 13, 1995. As Corrected October 10, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE WILLIAM J. LASSERS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant attorney appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed with prejudice several counts of his counterclaim to plaintiff publisher's cause of action for breach of contract due to the attorney's alleged failure to pay for charges associated with classified advertisements in a telephone directory. The counts in question alleged a violation of the attorney's civil rights and the commission of a tort.


OVERVIEW: The attorney defended against the publisher's breach of contract action by contending that the publisher violated his civil rights in causing the sheriff to attempt service at his business office on 12 occasions while knowing that the attorney would not be present and that the publisher thereafter obtained and published in the complaint his private residential address and telephone number. The court rejected all of the attorney's claims and concluded that the publisher's actions of misusing process service procedures, as alleged by the attorney, could not be attributed to state policy and thus did not state a cause of action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. In addition, the allegations were insufficient to establish the requisite color of law because there was no allegation of joint participation between the private party and state officials. The sheriff's serving process was, therefore, mere ministerial action which was insufficient for state participation because it was not wrongful in and of itself. Finally, the obtaining of the attorney's address was not tortious conduct but breach of contract, and the attorney should have sued on a tortious interference with a contract claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that dismissed those counts of the attorney's counterclaim alleging violation of civil rights and commission of a tort.

Communications & Cable of Chicago v. Department of Revenue


No. 1-94-2040


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION

September 7, 1995, FILED

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE EARL ARKISS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff cable companies (companies) sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissing their complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief against defendants, Department of Revenue of the City of Chicago and the Director of Revenue of the City of Chicago (city).


OVERVIEW: The companies brought an action in equity seeking declaratory and injunctive relief against the city alleging that, pursuant to Chicago Municipal Code § 3-32-010 et seq. (1992), it assessed an unauthorized transaction against them. The companies appealed the trial court order dismissing the action for lack of equity jurisdiction. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in part and reversed in part. The court held that although equity is generally not available to provide tax relief where an adequate remedy at law is available, it is permitted where a tax is alleged to be unauthorized by law. The court further held that the complaint sufficiently alleged that the transaction tax imposed on the companies amounted to an occupation tax that is unauthorized within the meaning of Ill. Const. 1970, art. VII, § 6(e)(2)). However, the court also held that the companies' estoppel claim was properly dismissed because they failed to show the requisite special circumstances to justify permitting assertion of estoppel against the government.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in part and reversed it in part and remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Keener


No. 2-93-1081


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


275 Ill. App. 3d 1; 655 N.E.2d 294; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 691; 211 Ill. Dec. 391



September 6, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 11, 1995. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 6, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 90-CF-2434. Honorable Raymond J. McKoski, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which dismissed his post conviction petition based upon ineffective assistance of counsel at trial. The court had already affirmed defendant's convictions for home invasion, armed robbery, and residential burglary as well as the trial court's order that denied defendant's post trial motion filed under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1401 (1992).


OVERVIEW: The victim, who identified defendant at two photo show ups and at trial, initially identified another person in a photo show up. At trial, defense counsel had not objected to admission of the identifications of defendant or cross examined the victim as to her testimony that indicated that police might have tainted the show ups in which she had identified defendant. Defendant had not raised the issue of ineffective assistance of counsel in his post trial motion or the appeal of his conviction and the trial court's denial of the motion. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order that denied defendant's post conviction petition, finding first that defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim was not waived by failure to raise it in the post trial motion because trial counsel still represented defendant at that point and raising the issue would have caused a conflict of interest. However, since the original appellate record had been sufficient to support an argument that trial counsel may have been ineffective in handling the victim's identification and testimony, the court held that defendant had waived his right to raise the issue in his post conviction petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that dismissed defendant's post conviction petition that alleged ineffective assistance of counsel.

Town of Northville v. Village of Sheridan


No. 3-95-0086


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT

July 18, 1995, SUBMITTED  
August 31, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 4, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 13th Judicial Circuit La Salle County, Illinois. No. 94 MC 2. Honorable Robert L. Carter Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, township and citizens, sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for the 13th Judicial Circuit La Salle County (Illinois), which granted defendant municipality's motions to dismiss. The township and the citizens alleged that the municipality's exercise of its extraterritorial zoning authority violated their constitutional voting rights.


OVERVIEW: The township and the citizens filed a complaint against the municipality, alleging that the municipality's exercise of its extraterritorial zoning authority violated their constitutional voting rights and that the statutory ranking of the zoning power of municipalities versus townships was an unreasonable classification. The trial court dismissed the township's claims for lack of standing and further held that the citizens' voting rights had not been violated. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the statute allowing the municipality to exercise extraterritorial zoning did not violate the citizens voting rights because they were not allowed to vote for the officials who adopt, amend, and administer the municipality's zoning ordinance. The court held that the trial court properly determined that the township lacked standing to bring a claim challenging the classification of zoning authority. The court held that the township also lacked standing to contest the constitutionality of the statutory ranking of the zoning authority because it did not have any constitutional right, which would be protected through its challenge to the legislative classification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the township and the citizens' complaint.

Adcock v. Montgomery Elevator Co.


NO. 1-93-3378


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


274 Ill. App. 3d 519; 654 N.E.2d 631; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 638; 211 Ill. Dec. 169; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P14,390



August 21, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 14, 1995. Released for Publication September 25, 1995. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 6, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE WILLIAM J. LASSERS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, granted summary judgment in favor of defendant escalator manufacturer in plaintiff injured party's action for negligence for injuries the injured party received on an escalator. The injured party appealed.


OVERVIEW: The injured party was riding on an escalator manufactured by the escalator manufacturer (manufacturer) when the escalator stopped abruptly, the injured party was thrown forward and down the escalator. The injured party contended that Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-214(b) did not bar his claim because the manufacturer was not within the class of persons the legislature intended to protect. The court held that the plain language of § 13-214(b) showed that one was protected not based upon his profession, but upon his performance of the activities enumerated and held that, applying the activity analysis to the case, it was clear that the manufacturer was protected under § 13-214(b). Finally, the court held that § 13-214(b) did not violate the open courts provision of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, § 12 because it merely modified the common law to provide that there was no cause of action against architects, contractors, engineers, and manufacturers involved in the construction of an improvement to real property after 10 years following the completion of construction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Rogers v. Desiderio


NO. 3-95-0169


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


274 Ill. App. 3d 446; 655 N.E.2d 930; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 622; 211 Ill. Dec. 547


July 19, 1995, SUBMITTED  
August 8, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified On Denial of Rehearing September 14, 1995. Released for Publication September 14, 1995. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 6, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. No. 94-MR-3275. Honorable Martin C. Rudman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, individuals and a high school board, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois, which affirmed the decision of defendant regional board of school trustees approving a petition filed under § 7-2b of the School Code, 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-2b (Supp. 1995), for the annexation of territory from plaintiffs' high school district to defendant high school board's district.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs first argued that the regional board's approval of the 1993 petition was void because, under the "first in time" principle, the 1993 petition should have been held in abeyance pending the outcome of the appeal regarding the 1992 petition. However, application of the "first in time" principle would not serve the ends of justice. The only justification for applying that principle would be to deter regional boards and school superintendents from considering § 7-2b petitions in future cases where to do so would risk invalidation of a petition under 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-8 (Supp. 1995). Section 7-8 had been amended to exclude 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-2b (Supp. 1005) petitions from its purview. As a result, the risk taken by the regional board would not arise in the future. The court declined to invalidate the 1993 petition. Also, § 7-2b was not a delegation of legislative power to private individuals in violation of Article IV, section 1 of the Illinois Constitution. The provision granted a privilege of organizing school districts subject to specific rules and conditions, and was not an unconstitutional delegation of lawmaking authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

Wollan v. Jacoby

People v. Smith


1-92-0133


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


274 Ill. App. 3d 84; 653 N.E.2d 944; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 568; 210 Ill. Dec. 749



July 24, 1995, Decided

Denied December 6, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable John Morrissey, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of two counts of armed robbery. Defendant contended that the admission of pretrial identification evidence denied him due process and that the trial court erred in refusing to give a lesser-included offense instruction, in allowing the state to elicit a prior consistent statement, and in its entry of judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of armed robbery, was found guilty, but was granted a new trial based on the unconstitutionality of a statute that allowed the state to demand a jury trial. During a second trial, and a mistrial was declared after the jury was unable to return a verdict. Defendant was tried for a third time and was convicted. Prior to the first trial, defendant's motion to suppress his pretrial identification was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed, in part, and held that the showup was proper because the facts demonstrated that the witnesses saw defendant in good light, had ample opportunity to view him, and did so with attention. The court found that there was no evidence in the record to support the lesser-included offense charge and that no jury could have rationally found defendant guilty of theft. The court held that the defendant never objected to the prior consistent statement testimony but that, regardless, the statement fell within an exception to the hearsay rule. Defendant was improperly convicted of two counts of armed robbery based on a single act, and the court remanded the case with directions to reflect only one conviction for armed robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, in part, but remanded the case to correct the judgment to reflect only one conviction for armed robbery and to vacate the other conviction for armed robbery.

The court held that accountability and the doctrine of transferred intent were inapplicable.

People v. Folks


NOS. 4-93-1045, 4-93-1046 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


273 Ill. App. 3d 126; 652 N.E.2d 378; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 434; 209 Ill. Dec. 838


May 12, 1995, SUBMITTED  
June 21, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 18, 1995. Released for Publication August 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Macon County. No. 93CF366. Honorable John K. Greanias, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 4-93-1045: Affirmed. No. 4-93-1046: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, first defendant and second defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which convicted them of three counts of attempted first degree murder and one count of aggravated discharge of a firearm, and two counts of attempted first degree murder and two counts of aggravated discharge of a firearm, respectively.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, first defendant argued that the trial court erred in admitting evidence of his nickname, and second defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to convict him of attempted first degree murder. Both defendants contended that they were denied effective assistance of counsel and that the statutory provisions creating the offense of aggravated unlawful discharge of a firearm were unconstitutional. Upon review, the appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The trial was heard at bench, and nothing in the record indicated that the trial court gave any substantial consideration to the evidence of first defendant's nickname. Even if second defendant was surprised the first time first defendant shot, the evidence fully supported a determination that he thereafter cooperated with the intent of aiding first defendant in shooting at the victims. In addition, both defendants received effective assistance of counsel. Under the statute concerning the unlawful discharge of a firearm, every one of the circumstances covered involved the firing of a firearm under circumstances that were extremely dangerous. That, of itself, was enough to justify the statute.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and held that the trial court properly convicted first and second defendant of the multiple offenses of attempted first degree murder and aggravated unlawful discharge of a firearm.

Rockford Memorial Hosp. v. Department of Human Rights


No. 2-94-0812


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


272 Ill. App. 3d 751; 651 N.E.2d 649; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 394; 209 Ill. Dec. 471



May 31, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 11, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 94-MR-4. Honorable Alford R. Penniman, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor physician filed a charge with appellant department of human rights (department), alleging that appellee hospital discriminated against him in violation of the Illinois Human Rights Act, 775 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1-101 et seq. (1992). The Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) enjoined the department from taking any action to investigate the physician's charges. The department appealed the decision.


OVERVIEW: The department argued that the trial court's decision to grant summary judgment and enjoin the department's investigation should be reversed because the trial court erred in finding that the Illinois Hospital Licensing Act, codified at 210 Ill. Comp. Stat. 85/10.2 (1992), conferred absolute immunity from discrimination claims arising from decisions made by peer review committees. The court held that the trial court misinterpreted the grant of absolute immunity from civil damages provided in the Human Rights Act § 10.2, codified at 775 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/8A-104 (1992), as a grant of absolute immunity from all legal liability. The court reversed the trial court's judgment. Section 10.2 was merely a restriction on the remedies available to physicians aggrieved by a hospital's peer review process, but according to the plain language of the statute it did not confer absolute immunity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision in favor of the hospital and remanded the case.

 

709 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Guerrero v. Ryan


1-93-4047


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


272 Ill. App. 3d 945; 651 N.E.2d 586; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 369; 209 Ill. Dec. 408



May 23, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 10, 1995. Certiorari Denied March 18, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 1890.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Lester D. Foreman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that granted a motion of defendant Secretary of State for judgment on the pleadings in this action, wherein the secretary suspended the drivers license of the driver pursuant to the Illinois Safety Responsibility Law (Safety Law), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95-1/2, para. 7-100 (1987) (now 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-100 et seq. (West 1992).


OVERVIEW: The driver was involved in an automobile accident involving injury in excess of $ 500. The driver failed to show proof of insurance as required by the Safety Law. Pursuant to the Safety Law, the secretary mailed the driver a hearing date. When the driver failed to appear at the hearing date or post bond pursuant to the Safety Law, his license was suspended. The driver commenced suit in the circuit court to reinstate his driving privileges. The secretary filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings. The circuit court granted the motion. The driver sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that (1) the Safety Law offered procedural due process protection to drivers who were unable to post security; (2) the secretary followed the Safety Act in mailing the hearing notice to the driver and the mailing was reasonably calculated to provide actual notice; (3) the driver had the obligation to instruct the secretary that he had moved; and (4) the Safety Law did not violate the driver's equal protection rights because it the purpose of the statute had a rational relationship to a legitimate government purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court that dismissed the driver's cause of action against the secretary and upheld the secretary's suspension of the drivers license of the driver.

 

710 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Martini v. Netsch


No. 1-92-3995


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


272 Ill. App. 3d 693; 650 N.E.2d 668; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 363; 208 Ill. Dec. 974



May 19, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 23, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Arthur L. Dunne, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied plaintiff taxpayer leave to file her suit against defendant, county board president. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer argued that an executive order issued by the county board president, which reinstated elective abortions at the county hospital, was unconstitutional and void, and that the trial court erred in finding that she lacked standing to pursue her action. The court held that the taxpayer had standing to pursue her claim but that the complaint failed to state a claim as a matter of law. A plaintiff who suffered injury in fact to a legally recognized interest had standing. The taxpayer presented a challenge to the use of public resources, which was sufficient to confer standing. However, the taxpayer did not assert that any state tax funds had been appropriated for use in performing the abortion procedures. The complaint was insufficient because it did not contain any factual allegations that the taxpayer's tax obligation to the state had or would be affected by the reinstatement of the procedures.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed in part because the taxpayer had standing to pursue her claim. The court affirmed in part because the complaint failed to state a claim against the county board president.

 

711 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Anderson


1-93-4153


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


272 Ill. App. 3d 537; 650 N.E.2d 648; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 347; 208 Ill. Dec. 954



May 16, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 23, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Michael B. Getty, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of attempted vehicular invasion, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-11.1 (1992).


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of attempted vehicular invasion, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-11.1 (1992), and sentenced defendant to six years imprisonment as a Class X offender based upon two prior Class two felony convictions. The defendant appealed, questioning whether 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-11.1 (1992) was constitutional, whether defendant was entitled to notice of the state's intention to seek an enhanced sentence, pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/111-3(c) (1992), and whether the mittimus issued required correction. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the designation of vehicular invasion a Class 1 felony was not so wholly disproportionate as to shock the community's moral sense, that the mittimus properly noted that defendant was sentenced to a six year prison term followed by three years of mandatory supervised release, and that the gravity of conduct offensive to the public safety and welfare, authorizing Class X sentencing, justifiably required lengthier watchfulness after prison release than violations of a less serious nature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of attempted vehicular invasion.

 

712 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Shepard v. Pollution Control Bd.


No. 2-94-0864


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


272 Ill. App. 3d 764; 651 N.E.2d 555; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 319; 209 Ill. Dec. 377



May 4, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied and Released for Publication July 11, 1995. Petition for
Leave to Appeal Denied December 6, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Review of the Order of the Pollution Control Board. PCB No. 94-2. Chairman Claire A. Manning.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner residents sought review of an order of respondent Pollution Control Board (Illinois), dismissing their complaint against respondent sports club and village, which alleged that the sports club's shooting activities caused noise pollution in violation of the Environmental Protection Act, 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/23, 5/24 (1992) and Ill. Admin. Code tit. 35, §§ 900.102, 901.102(a), 901.104 (1991).


OVERVIEW: On review, the court affirmed, finding that the sports club was exempt from the noise standards pursuant to 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/25 (1992) as an organized amateur sporting activity and that 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24 (1992) did not provide a general cause of action. No cause of action existed pursuant to Ill. Admin. Code tit. 35, § 900.102 (1991), which was subject to the exemption of 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/25, 5/3.25 (1992). The club's shifting of locations did not affect the exemption because it had been continuously involved in skeet and trap shooting since it was founded in 1944. The exemption extended to the village, which had no ownership interest in the club, and the fact that the village assisted the club in the setting up its facilities did not establish that it was responsible for the noise resulting from the use of those facilities. The board applied all of the necessary criteria in determining that the club was exempted under the Act. Although the club's articles of incorporation failed to include a reference to shooting activities, that did not render the exemption inapplicable. Finally, the court concluded that §§ 5/25, 5/3.25 were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board's order dismissing the residents' complaint against the sports club and village.

 

713 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Calahan


No. 1-93-1326


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


272 Ill. App. 3d 293; 649 N.E.2d 588; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 284; 208 Ill. Dec. 532



April 24, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 15, 1995. Released for Publication May 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE CHRISTY S. BERKOS, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-14(a)(1)(1992). Defendant was sentenced to a 16-year term of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal assault for inappropriately touching the minor child of his girlfriend. On appeal, defendant argued that his sentence was excessive, that § 5-4-3 of the Unified Code of Corrections (Code), 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-4-3 (1992), was unconstitutional, and that he was improperly certified as a child sex offender under the Child Offender Act (Act), 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/1 et seq. (1992). The court affirmed the conviction. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant because the sentence was within the guidelines and the fact that defendant acted as father figure to a very young victim justified his sentence. The court held that § 5-4-3 of the Code, which required those convicted of sexual offenses to submit blood samples, did not violate U.S. Const. amend. IV because the governmental interest in having a permanent identification record from a prisoner outweighed the minor intrusion. The statute was not unreasonable under the state constitution. Defendant was not improperly certified as a sex offender under the Act because he was convicted after the effective date of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault on a minor child.

 

714 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Holt


No. 3-94-0566


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


271 Ill. App. 3d 1016; 649 N.E.2d 571; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 283; 208 Ill. Dec. 515


February 16, 1995, SUBMITTED  
April 21, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 23, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit Peoria County, Illinois. No. 93-CF-961. Honorable Robert E. Manning Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit Peoria County, Illinois, which convicted him of stalking, in violation of Ill. Crim. Code. § 5/12-7.3(a)(2) (1961), 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-7.3(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for stalking his ex-girlfriend. He appealed the conviction and his sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the "remaining present outside" language in the stalking statute required judicial construction because its application was not clear and unambiguous. The court found that the statute encompassed the surveillance of a person from a place within the same primary structure but distinct from the "other place occupied by" the person. The court also found that, combined with defendant's prior conduct, the evidence was sufficient to find a "substantial probability" that defendant knew his behavior placed the victim in reasonable apprehension of harm. Additionally, the court rejected defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of the statute. It found that the statute contained sufficiently objective standards of conduct and knowledge to allow its valid application. The court also noted that although the statute was relatively broad, it did not substantially infringe upon constitutionally protected behavior or expression either generally or as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of stalking was affirmed.

 

715 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Tampam Farms v. Supervisor of Assessments


No. 2-94-0761


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


271 Ill. App. 3d 798; 649 N.E.2d 87; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 272; 208 Ill. Dec. 255



April 20, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 15, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ogle County. Nos. 88-TX-1; 90-TX-39; 91-TX-46. Honorable John L. Moore and Dennis J. Riley, Judges, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Ogle County (Illinois) in favor of defendants, tax assessor, treasurer, and county, under the Civil Rights Act of 1871, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Plaintiff also challenged the decertification of a class of taxpayers of which plaintiff was a member.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayer challenged the trial court's dismissal of its claims against defendants, tax assessor, treasurer, and county, under the Civil Rights Act of 1871, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983; and the trial court's decertification of a class of taxpayers that plaintiff asserted had been fraudulently over-assessed for property taxes on farmland containing public roads and highways within their boundaries. Plaintiff sought administrative rather than judicial review of his civil rights claim. On appeal, the court held that the doctrine of constructive fraud did not apply in § 1983 cases and that plaintiff failed to pursue an administrative review in which constructive fraud was cognizable. The court found that although defendant assessor had made some honest mistakes in assessing plaintiff's property, he did not harbor a discriminatory purpose toward plaintiff. The decertification of plaintiff's class was proper because the proposed members of the class had different parcels of land and different tax interests. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decisions dismissing plaintiff's taxpayer's claim against defendants, tax assessor, treasurer, and county, and decertifying the class of taxpayers of which plaintiff was a member.

 

716 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Ogle County Bd. ex rel. County of Ogle v. Pollution Control Bd.


No. 2-94-0074


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


272 Ill. App. 3d 184; 649 N.E.2d 545; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 268; 208 Ill. Dec. 489



April 20, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 23, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Pollution Control Board. PCB 93-114.



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons, the decision of the PCB is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the grant of site location approval for appellant landfill operator by appellant county board, appellee business owner filed an appeal with appellee, Pollution Control Board (PCB) (Illinois), which reversed the county board's decision on the notice issue. Appellants sought a review of the PCB's decision.


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued that the business owner failed to properly plead and prove that he was so located as to be affected by the proposed facility under 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/40.1(b) (1992) of the Environmental Protection Act. In affirming the PCB's decision, the court held that the business owner had standing to challenge the county board's approval of the proposed landfill site. The court held that compliance with the individual notice requirements of 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/39.2(b) (1993) was a jurisdictional prerequisite to the county board's authority to act over a given landfill proposal. Any order entered in the absence of such compliance was void in that the county board entering the order would lack the inherent power to enter the particular order involved. The landfill operator's alleged failure to comply with § 39.2(b) rendered the county board's approval void and left the order subject to attack at any time or in any court. Furthermore, the business owner's standing as a person who was affected by the proposed facility pursuant to 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/40.1(b) (1992) was sufficient to give him standing to challenge the validity of the county board's approval.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the PCB, which reversed the county board's approval of a proposed landfill site for the landfill operator.

 

717 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Terry v. Metropolitan Pier & Exposition Auth.


No. 1-93-2881


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


271 Ill. App. 3d 446; 648 N.E.2d 1047; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 238; 208 Ill. Dec. 125



March 31, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 9, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Earl Arkiss, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, vehicle operators and passengers, challenged an order dismissing their class action complaint challenging the constitutionality of the Airport Departure Tax Ordinance, Metropolitan Pier and Exposition Authority, Ill., Airport Departure Tax Ordinance § 1-3 (1992), by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: The Airport Departure Tax Ordinance, Metropolitan Pier and Exposition Authority, Ill., Airport Departure Tax Ordinance § 1-3 (1992), imposed an occupation tax on all commercial vehicle operators departing from a metropolitan airport. The tax was to assist in financing an expansion project. The operators and passengers challenged the constitutionality of the ordinance. The trial court dismissed the complaint and the court affirmed. Although the burden of the tax was passed on to the passengers, the court held that their claim failed because the incidence of the tax rested on the operators. The court held that the ordinance did not violate the operators' due process, equal protection, or uniformity clause rights. The court noted that the operators benefited directly from the project and that they failed to establish a distinction between classes of operators who were taxed and those who were not. The scheme was found to be a workable method to tax those who would benefit directly from the project and reasonably related to its goal. The ordinance did not violate the commerce clause of U.S. Const. art. I, § 8 because it was imposed only on operators doing business within the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the class action complaint of the operators and passengers and found the Airport Departure Tax Ordinance to be constitutional.

People v. Cross


1-93-0353, 1-93-4516


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


272 Ill. App. 3d 354; 650 N.E.2d 1047; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 175; 209 Ill. Dec. 74



March 21, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing May 23, 1995. Rehearing Denied May 10, 1995. Released for Publication May 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable John W. Crilly, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed, vacated and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted and sentenced him for the offense of second degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed a man. He claimed self-defense. Defendant contended on appeal that the trial court erred in sustaining objections to questions concerning threats made against him and his state of mind, that he was denied a fair trial by the failure to give the jury a general "not guilty" verdict form, that the second degree murder statute violated due process,that the prosecutor made improper comments in closing argument, and that the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing him. The court reversed, vacated, and remanded for new trial. The court concluded that defendant's excluded testimony might have affected the outcome of the case, and that the exclusion was plain error, requiring reversal of the conviction. The court determined that the omission of the not guilty verdict form constituted plain error and denied defendant a fair trial. The court noted that the constitutionality of the statute had been upheld by the supreme court. The court determined that several of the prosecutor's comments were improper. The court did not find an abuse of discretion in the length of the sentence imposed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated defendant's conviction and sentence, and remanded the cause for a new trial.

 

719 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jones


NO. 4-93-0523


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


271 Ill. App. 3d 264; 647 N.E.2d 598; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 130; 207 Ill. Dec. 367


November 22, 1994, SUBMITTED  
March 10, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 10, 1995.
As Corrected March 31, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Vermilion County. No. 91CF309. Honorable Rita B. Garman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois), which vacated consecutive 25-year terms for armed robbery, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 18-2(a) (1991), and attempted first-degree murder, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 8-4, 9-1(a) (1991), and resentenced him to 30 years for the attempted murder. He sought vacation of the sentence under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615(b)(4), 36 Ill. 2d R. 615(b)(4).


OVERVIEW: The sentencing range for attempted first degree murder was 6 months to 30 years under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-1(a)(3) (1992). Defendant contended that his sentence was improperly increased and excessive given his potential for rehabilitation, the influence of drugs upon him during the offense, and the suggestions by others that he commit the crime. The trial court denied his supplemental motion to reconsider the sentence. He sought vacation of the sentence and a minimum or lesser term. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615(b)(4) did not permit it as a reviewing court to reduce the sentence unless it constituted an abuse of discretion. There was no abuse of discretion in resentencing when the sentence was significantly reduced by 20 years. The court held that Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615(b)(4) did not permit a reviewing court to reduce any sentence that conformed to the law, absent an abuse of discretion, or to select a lesser sentence to impose. 36 Ill. 2d R. 615(b)(4). The 30-year sentence fell within the statutory guidelines and the trial court had considered aggravating and mitigating factors the three times it addressed the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that resentenced defendant.
