People v. Cooks


1-92-3579


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


271 Ill. App. 3d 25; 648 N.E.2d 190; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 117; 207 Ill. Dec. 734



February 28, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 13, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Daniel J. Kelly, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him for two counts of murder and sentenced him to a mandatory term of imprisonment for life.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a 14 year old, was charged with the murders of two individuals and transferred from the juvenile court, indicted, and prosecuted as an adult. Defendant was found guilty of both murders and given the mandatory life sentence of imprisonment. Defendant appealed, challenging his transfer from juvenile court an the constitutionality of imprisonment of the mandatory life sentence. Defendant contended that the juvenile court failed to consider whether or not it was in defendant's best interest or the best interests of society that defendant be imprisoned for life. The court held that a single mention of the life sentence awaiting defendant without any other consideration in the record of the potential penalty was sufficiently explicit for meaningful review. The court also determined that defendant failed to demonstrate that the mandatory life imprisonment statute was unconstitutional on its face or as applied to him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting and sentencing defendant for two counts of murder.

 

721 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jackson


No. 1-93-1185


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


269 Ill. App. 3d 851; 646 N.E.2d 1299; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 51; 207 Ill. Dec. 212



February 3, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 21, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. No. 92 CR 25581. THE HONORABLE MATTHEW MORAN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to bar introduction of his prior felony conviction based on § 111-3(c) of the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/111-3(c) (1992).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with unlawful use of weapons and ammunition by a felon in violation of § 24.1.1 of the Criminal Code of 1961, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24-1.1 (1992). The trial court granted defendant's motion to bar introduction of his felony conviction. The trial court precluded the information that defendant was convicted of possession of a stolen vehicle and allowed defendant to stipulate that he was convicted of a felony The court reversed and remanded. The court allowed jurisdiction for the appeal and held that the prosecution was impaired in the case because it had the burden of presenting evidence for conviction. Section 111-3(c) was not applicable to § 24-1.1 because the state was not seeking an enhanced sentence and the crime of unlawful use of weapons and ammunition was a separate offense. The court held that § 24-1.1 did not deprive defendant of equal protection because the statute bore a rational relationship to the legitimate state purpose of keeping firearms out of the possession of convicted felons.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which granted defendant's motion to exclude evidence of his prior felony conviction.

 

722 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lewis


NO. 4-94-0045


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


269 Ill. App. 3d 523; 646 N.E.2d 305; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 57; 206 Ill. Dec. 938


December 14, 1994, ORAL ARGUMENT HELD  
February 3, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing March 8, 1995. Released for Publication March 8, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 92CF905. Honorable Ronald C. Dozier, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which convicted him of official misconduct. Defendant objected to the denial by the trial court of his motions to suppress and for a mistrial and to its refusal to sever and order separate trials on the various charges against him. Defendant also argued that the evidence against him was insufficient.


OVERVIEW: Various female probationers accused defendant, who was a probation officer, of engaging in sexual improprieties with them in his office. At trial, a police veteran testified that one of the victims agreed to take a polygraph examination. The court held that the trial court abused its discretion in denying defendant's motion for a mistrial. The court noted the substantial conflict in the testimony of defendant and his victims and reasoned that the improper polygraph reference could have substantially enhanced the credibility of the one particular victim in the eyes of the jury. Reference to probation department personnel policies was not required to establish defendant's guilt because his sexual acts with probationers during the course of official duties clearly exceeded the scope of his lawful authority. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by not ordering separate trials because defendant's other crimes would have been admissible as modus operandi. Finally, the trial court did not err by refusing to suppress defendant's statement to investigators because he was not physically restrained and therefore was not in custody for Miranda purposes when he have his statement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for official misconduct because of the mistrial that occurred when an investigator testified that one of defendant's victims agreed to take a polygraph examination. The court remanded the case for a new trial.

 

723 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Witt v. Jones & Jones Law Offices, P.C.


NO. 4-94-0156


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


269 Ill. App. 3d 540; 646 N.E.2d 23; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 55; 206 Ill. Dec. 891


August 23, 1994, ORAL ARGUMENT HELD  
February 3, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 3, 1995. Released for Publication March 3, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Edgar County. No. 93L25. Honorable Richard E. Scott, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff beneficiaries filed a legal malpractice action against defendant attorneys for damages that allegedly resulted from the drafting of a will. The Circuit Court of Edgar County (Illinois) granted the attorneys' motion to dismiss because the beneficiaries' claim was barred by the statute of limitations under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-214.3(d) (1992).


OVERVIEW: The decedent left a will that was drafted by the attorneys and the beneficiaries were appointed as executors. One of them filed a declination of office as executor and a petition for probate of the will and letters of testamentary were filed with copies being sent to all of the heirs and legatees. The note stated that they and 42 days to file a petition with the court. One of the heirs filed a petition and stated that she had knowledge that the beneficiary who declined to serve as executor was going to protest the will, which the lower court denied. After distribution of the estate, the beneficiaries filed their complaint against the attorneys who drafted the will under a breach of contract and negligence theory. The court determined that the beneficiaries were required to file their action one year prior to when they did and it was therefore barred by the statute of limitations. The court stated that the beneficiaries had actual notice of any alleged defects within the period of the statute of limitations and it did not matter whether the attorneys were the source of that actual knowledge. The court held that the beneficiaries' claim was barred under § 13-214.3(d).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment that dismissed the beneficiaries' claim because it was time-barred.

 

724 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Rollin Foods v. Village of Glendale Heights


No. 2-93-1251


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


269 Ill. App. 3d 351; 646 N.E.2d 12; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 49; 206 Ill. Dec. 880



February 1, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 2, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 92-CH-820. Honorable John S. Teschner, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, village and Illinois Liquor Control Commission, challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which found in favor of appellee general partner in its action for a declaratory judgment that the "happy hours prohibited" statute, § 6-28 of the Liquor Control Act of 1934, 235 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/6-28 (1992), did not prohibit the general partner from conducting a ladies' buffet night in its restaurant and bar.


OVERVIEW: A restaurant offered a ladies' buffet night at which women paid the cover charge and received a buffet dinner with unlimited alcoholic drinks. Women who chose not to pay the cover charge could not partake of the buffet and were not entitled to free drinks. Men were required to pay the cover charge, could not partake of the buffet, and were required to pay the regular price for drinks. Restaurant employees were arrested for violating the "happy hours prohibited" statute. The general partner of the partnership that owned the restaurant sought a declaratory judgment that the statute did not prohibit the restaurant from conducting the ladies' buffet night. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the general partner and the court reversed. It found that the statute prohibited the selling of alcoholic liquor on any one date at a reduced priced other than that charged other purchasers of drinks on that day where such reduced price is a promotion to encourage consumption of alcoholic liquor and that the exception allowing the inclusion of drinks of alcoholic liquor as part of a meal package was not intended to be an exception to the prohibition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which granted a declaratory judgment in favor of the general partner holding that the ladies' night buffet did not violate the "happy hours prohibited" statute.

 

725 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


McGee v. La Salle Nat'l Bank (In re Estate of Rollins)

OVERVIEW: The sister, a licensed nurse, provided nursing care, room, and board for her ailing brother for 11 years. After the decedent's death, she filed a claim against his estate, claiming that she was entitled to compensation for services she rendered to the decedent and for personal funds she expended for his care. The trial judge substantially limited the testimony of the sister's witnesses pursuant to respondent estate administrator's objections under the Dead Man's Act (Act), 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/8-201. After the sister's claims were denied, she contended on appeal that the trial court erred when it refused to allow her testimony as to the physical and mental condition of her brother and as to the care she provided for him. The court held that the trial court's denial of her claims was proper because the sister failed to establish her right to recovery under an implied contract theory. The court found no evidence that the decedent expected to compensate the sister beyond the payments she received as his appointed guardian.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was affirmed.

People v. Kang


NO. 4-94-0223


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


269 Ill. App. 3d 546; 646 N.E.2d 279; 1995 Ill. App. LEXIS 34; 206 Ill. Dec. 912


October 18, 1994, ORAL ARGUMENT HELD  
January 20, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 20, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 93CF765. Honorable William T. Caisley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of perjury and sentenced defendant to five years imprisonment to be served consecutively to a sentence he was serving when the perjury was committed.


OVERVIEW: As part of a plea agreement, defendant testified before a grand jury regarding a codefendant's role in a criminal drug conspiracy. Defendant testified that he was a friend of the codefendant and had arranged with him to sell cocaine. When called to testify at the codefendant's trial, defendant attempted to avoid answering questions regarding the codefendant. The trial court ruled that by virtue of defendant's guilty plea, the privilege against self-incrimination was not available to him and ordered defendant to answer some nonincriminating questions. Defendant testified that he did not recall specific events that he had testified to before the grand jury nor specific answers he had given in his grand jury testimony. The trial court found defendant guilty of perjury. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that defendant was not deprived of his right against self-incrimination as there were no criminal proceedings pending against him at the time of his trial testimony. Further, his plea agreement resulted in waiver of his right against self-incrimination. Finally, the evidence was sufficient for a jury to have found that defendant's memory was selective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for perjury where he was not deprived of his rights against self-incrimination and it was shown that defendant's memory regarding his testimony before a grand jury was selective.

 

727 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wickland


No. 2-93-1321


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


268 Ill. App. 3d 758; 644 N.E.2d 799; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1525; 206 Ill. Dec. 31



December 27, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 93-TR-12376. Honorable John G. Radosevich, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which found him guilty of driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI), sentenced him to one year of conditional discharge, and levied a fine under the provisions of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-6-1(d) (1993).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of DUI and given a fine and a one-year conditional discharge. He challenged the decision and argued that he was entitled to supervision because the amendment to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-6-1(d) (1993) enlarging the time limit for the consideration of past violations from 5 years to 10 years was unconstitutional. Specifically, he asserted that the statute was in conflict with 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-500 (1992), which limited supervision in summary suspension cases to offenders who had not had a violation within the past 5 years. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that no conflict existed because the summary suspension statute and the DUI statute addressed different problems. The summary suspension statute was civil in nature and not part of the punishment for DUI. Rather, it was designed to restrict limited driving privileges available to repeat offenders. The DUI statute was designed to punish violations of the law and the establishment of a longer period to preclude first offender status was appropriate. Defendant's argument that he did not have fair warning of the passage of the new amendment was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for DUI.

People v. Robinson


1-92-1479


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


268 Ill. App. 3d 1019; 645 N.E.2d 437; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1514; 206 Ill. Dec. 432



December 22, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 8, 1995. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied
December 6, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE FRED G. SURIA, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found him guilty of armed robbery and, pursuant to the Habitual Criminal Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33B-1 et seq. (1989), now 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/33B-1 et seq. (1992), sentenced him to a term of natural life without the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with armed robbery. The state sought to admit evidence of other crimes from two prior victims; however, the trial court allowed the testimony of only one prior victim to show a common scheme and design. Defendant was convicted and sentenced, and the court affirmed. It found that "other crimes" evidence was properly admitted based on the similarities between the two crimes, coupled with the corroborative fact that defendant's fingerprint was found on the current victim's car. Further, the state proved defendant was guilty of armed robbery beyond a reasonable doubt based on the similarities of the current attack with the prior attack, which established modus operandi and defendant's identity as the attacker, together with evidence of defendant's fingerprints found on the victim's car. Finally, the certified records of defendant's prior convictions for armed robberies were sufficient to support the adjudication of the trial court under the Habitual Criminal Act as defendant offered no evidence other than his bare contention that he was not convicted of an armed robbery to rebut evidence of his prior conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for armed robbery and his adjudication as a habitual offender for sentencing purposes.

People v. Jennings


No. 3-93-0256


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


268 Ill. App. 3d 439; 644 N.E.2d 1199; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1523; 206 Ill. Dec. 146



December 22, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied and Released for Publication February 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County, Illinois. No. 92-CF-418. Honorable Daniel Gould Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions entered in the Circuit Court of Kankakee County (Illinois) for first-degree murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1 and of aggravated battery with a firearm in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-4.2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and aggravated battery with a firearm. On appeal, defendant maintained that the shooting death of the victim was accidental or at worst the product of a mere reckless act. Defendant also contended that his actions were justified on the basis of self-defense or were the result of an unreasonable belief in the need for self-defense. Finally, defendant argued that he was entitled to a new trial because he did not waive his right to a jury trial in writing as required by § 115-1 of the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-1. The court found that although defendant knowingly waived his right to a jury in open court, defendant's convictions required reversal because no written waiver of a jury trial was obtained as required by para. 115-1. Further, para. 115-1 did not violate the Separation of Powers Clause of the Illinois Constitution, and defendant did not waive the issue by failing to properly preserve it for appeal because the right to a jury trial involved substantial rights. For purposes of retrial, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions of first-degree murder and aggravated battery with a firearm and remanded for a new trial.

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtor sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which denied his motion to quash the garnishment of a mutual fund by appellee creditor and denied his motion to quash and restrain the sale of his home.


OVERVIEW: A judgment was entered in favor of the creditor against the debtor. Comp. Stat. 1005/1c (1992).

West v. Granny's Rocker Niteclub


No. 5-93-0375


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


268 Ill. App. 3d 207; 643 N.E.2d 850; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1450; 205 Ill. Dec. 559



December 1, 1994, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 91-L-1706. Honorable Philip J. Kardis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administrator filed a wrongful death action against defendants, nightclub and its owner (collectively nightclub), towing company, and city, to recover for the decedent's death following a motorcycle accident. The Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) dismissed the complaint as to the nightclub, and entered summary judgment in favor of the towing company and the city. The administrator appealed.


OVERVIEW: The administrator claimed that as a patron of the nightclub the decedent became intoxicated. As a result of his intoxicated state, he collided head-on with another vehicle and died from his injuries. The administrator argued that the nightclub's promotion was a willful and wanton violation of the Liquor Control Act (Act), 235 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/6-28(b) (1992), which prohibits happy hours. On appeal, the court determined that the only remedy available to the administrator under the Act was provided for in 235 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/6-21 (1992). The court held that no common law cause of action existed against the nightclub for willful and wanton violation of the statutory prohibition against happy hours. As to the grant of summary judgment in favor of the towing company, the court held that material issues of fact existed as to whether the motorcycle was entrusted to the decedent and if so, if the towing company's owner knew or should have known that the decedent was intoxicated. Finally, the city could not be held liable on a theory of respondeat superior for the actions of the towing company because it was an independent contractor over which the city had not control.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal for the company against the nightclub because the administrator failed to state an actionable cause of action against the nightclub. The court also affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the city; however, the court reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the towing company because material issues of fact existed.

 

733 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. McGee


No. 2-93-0718


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


268 Ill. App. 3d 32; 644 N.E.2d 439; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1449; 205 Ill. Dec. 883


August 9, 1994, ASSIGNED; October 27, 1994, SUBMITTED  
November 30, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 10, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 92-DT-1203. Honorable Hollis L. Webster, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to suppress the results of a blood-alcohol test taken at the scene of an accident pursuant to § 11-501.6(a) of the Illinois Vehicle Code, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501.6(a) (1991) (now 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501.6(a) (1992)), where defendant was charged with driving under the influence of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: The statute that authorized the blood test had been declared facially unconstitutional, and the State argued against suppression because the officer relied in "good faith" on the validity of the statute at the time he requested the test. The court affirmed the order of suppression, and initially noted that the Illinois Constitution afforded greater protection than the Federal Constitution. Although the United States Supreme Court recognized a limited "good faith" exception for a warrantless administrative search where a statute was later found to be unconstitutional, Illinois' Constitution recognized no such exception. Illinois courts have consistently refused to apply the good-faith exception in cases where no warrant was present, and a warrantless search or seizure was deemed unreasonable per se unless it came within a specific, well-delineated exceptions to the warrant requirement. In the absence of probable cause, a "good faith" reliance on a facially invalid statute could not legitimize an unconstitutional search. Absent probable cause, the invasion of the physical integrity of a person constituted an unreasonable invasion of privacy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that suppressed the evidence.

Jacobson v. Department of Pub. Aid


No. 2-93-1275


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


269 Ill. App. 3d 359; 646 N.E.2d 949; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1430; 207 Ill. Dec. 115


July 25, 1994, Assigned  
November 22, 1994, FILED

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 92-MR-89. Honorable Alford R. Penniman, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants department of public aid challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), court reversing the administrative decision of the director of the department that plaintiffs parents were required to reimburse the department as responsible relatives for their 19-year-old daughter who was receiving aid to families with dependent children (AFDC).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued that the distinction in 305 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/10-2 between parents whose 18- to 21-year-old children lived at home and those whose children did not violated the equal protection clauses of both the United States and Illinois Constitutions. The department argued that the parents of AFDC recipients who allowed their 18- to 21-year-old children to reside at home were not similarly situated to those who did not allow their AFDC recipient children in the same age group to live in the parental home. The court held that 10-2 did not directly and substantially interfere with a family's fundamental right to live in the type of family unit that it chose. In light of the stated purposes of the statute the court however found no rational basis for distinguishing between parents whose 18- to 21-year-oldchildren lived with them and those whose children did not, in the determination of support liability. The court finally found that the invalid provision of 10-2 could not be severed from the remainder of the section under 305 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-4, as the legislative history showed that it was enacted to include the exception at issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

International Ins. Co. v. City of Chicago Heights


No. 1-92-1493


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


268 Ill. App. 3d 289; 643 N.E.2d 1305; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1417; 205 Ill. Dec. 698



November 18, 1994, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1]  UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23 ORDER.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 13, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE ALBERT GREEN, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and Reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurer appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant city's motion for summary judgment and awarded damages and legal fees in the insurer's declaratory judgment action seeking a determination of its liability to indemnify the city under a public officials and employees liability policy issued to the city for legal fees resulting from seven lawsuits filed against it.


OVERVIEW: An insurer issued a public officials and employees liability policy to the city which contained exclusions for claims based on property damage and for claims based on wrongful entry or eviction. Seven lawsuits were brought against the city for engaging in a conspiracy to force minorities from the city. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the city, awarded attorneys' fees on the underlying suit, damages, and attorneys' fees on the declaratory judgment action. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court affirmed all but one of the underlying cases. Only one plaintiff had a claim for eviction, which did not have civil rights violations attached. The court reversed the award of attorneys' fees on the declaratory action, holding that there was no proof the insurer acted vexatiously in bringing the suit.


OUTCOME: The decision granting summary judgment in favor of the city was reversed with respect to the award of attorneys' fees incurred by the city in one underlying case and with respect to the amount awarded to the city for attorneys' fees incurred in coverage litigation. The award in favor of the city was affirmed with respect to the remainder of the judgment.

People v. Ross


No. 3-94-0143


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


267 Ill. App. 3d 711; 642 N.E.2d 914; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1424; 205 Ill. Dec. 49


September 8, 1994, Submitted  
November 18, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 22, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 9th Judicial Circuit Warren County, Illinois, No. 93-CF-42. Honorable Scott I. Klukos Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of the Ninth Judicial Circuit Warren County, Illinois, which granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence obtained from defendant's residence under an anticipatory search warrant and ruled that the search warrant was invalid under state law. Defendant alleged that the warrant violated the requirements in 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/108-3(a) (1993).


OVERVIEW: The U.S. postal service contacted police when they mistakenly opened a package addressed to defendant and discovered a substance that they believed was cocaine. The substance was cocaine. Based on the police's belief that probable cause would exist after the delivery of the letter, the police obtained a search warrant for defendant's home for a time shortly after the package was to be delivered. The affidavit in support of the search warrant stated that "once the contents of the letter" was delivered probable cause would exist. The court affirmed the trial court's suppression of the evidence and its ruling that the warrant was invalid. The court held that anticipatory search warrants were impermissible under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/108-3(a) (1993) because that law required a prior crime for the issuance of a warrant. Moreover, the contingency for execution of the warrant was not noted in the affidavit in support of the warrant with sufficient specificity as it was not explicit, clear, and narrowly drawn so as to avoid misunderstanding or manipulation. Indeed, the affidavit was silent on the role the police would play in the actual delivery of the letter and its search operations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of defendant's motion to suppress evidence and its ruling that the anticipatory search warrant was invalid under Illinois law.

Halfway House v. City of Waukegan


No. 2-93-1233


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


267 Ill. App. 3d 112; 641 N.E.2d 1005; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1372; 204 Ill. Dec. 575


July 21, 1994, Assigned  
November 1, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 92-CH-196. Honorable Peter M. Trobe, Judge, Presiding.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of September 29, 1994, Previously Reported at: 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1281.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) declaring invalid certain conditions which the city attached to a conditional use permit granted to plaintiff halfway house for the construction and operation of a residential rehabilitation center.


OVERVIEW: The halfway house applied for a conditional use permit for the construction and operation of a residential rehabilitation center. The city denied the request, and on appeal, the trial court determined that the zoning ordinance was unreasonable and that the proposed use was reasonable. Further hearings were conducted, and the city granted the conditional use permit subject to 14 conditions. The halfway house objected to five of the conditions, and the trial court declared all but one of them invalid. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The court held that the trial court should not have automatically declared invalid the 32-person restriction because it conflicted with a prior court order without determining whether the restriction was otherwise unreasonable, and therefore, remand on that issue was necessary. The court found that the condition prohibiting the halfway house from accepting residents who had been convicted of sexual offenses was void for vagueness because it did not set forth the standards for making that determination. Finally, the 14-day notice requirement was also invalid because there was no evidence that it was necessary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the trial court's order findings that the 14-day notice period was unreasonable and that the condition prohibiting the halfway house from accepting residents who had been convicted of offenses that were of a sexual nature was vague and unenforceable. The court reversed the portion of the order invalidating the 32-person restriction and remanded for further hearings on whether the restriction was reasonable.

People v. Cunningham


1-92-4391, 1-93-0495 (Cons.)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


267 Ill. App. 3d 1009; 642 N.E.2d 781; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1356; 204 Ill. Dec. 880



October 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 29, 1994. Released for Publication December 16, 1994. Petition for Rehearing Denied January 23, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE MATTHEW J. MORAN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the dismissal by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of his motion for post-conviction relief filed in accordance with 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 et seq. with respect to his convictions for murder, attempted murder, and attempted armed robbery and the sentences associated therewith.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of murder, attempted murder, and attempted armed robbery and was sentenced to 70, 30, 15 years' respectively. He filed a motion for post-conviction relief pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 et seq. The trial court dismissed his motion and he appealed. Petitioner contended that his constitutional rights were violated during his direct appeal because the wrong constitutional standard was used in denying admittance of an extrajudicial third party confession, he was denied effective assistance of trial counsel and denied effective assistance of appellate counsel. The court affirmed the dismissal. First, the court held the petitioner's constitutional rights were not violated because the trial court applied the applicable standard at the time with respect to the inadmissibility of an untrustworthy extrajudicial third party confession. Secondly, the court held that dismissal was proper based upon the affidavit asserting that new evidence was discovered following the trial because the statement was not obtained with diligence. Thirdly, the court although petitioner's trial and appellate counsel were not ineffective, the issue was barred by res judicata.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of petitioner's motion for post-conviction relief with respect to his murder, attempted murder, and attempted armed robbery convictions. The court held that dismissal was proper where the standard used to preclude admissibility of an extrajudicial statement was proper, where the affidavit purporting that new evidence was discovered was not diligent, and where his counsel was not ineffective.

Greco v. McHenry County Sheriff's Dep't Merit Comm'n


No. 2-93-1221


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


267 Ill. App. 3d 303; 642 N.E.2d 177; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1360; 204 Ill. Dec. 715


July 21, 1994, Assigned  
October 26, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 30, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 90-MR-184. Honorable William D. Block, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employees challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois), which dismissed their complaint against defendants, county and sheriff's department, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief based on their claim that they were improperly barred from promotion within the sheriff's department.


OVERVIEW: In their complaint, the employees alleged that portions of a collective-bargaining agreement (FOP contract) between defendant county and their union, and the bylaws of the merit commission violated the Sheriff's Merit System Law (Merit System Law), 55 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-8001 et seq. Moreover, the employees sought an order enjoining the sheriff's department from hiring new officers to the rank of deputy sheriff or, alternatively, an order directing the department to pay the employees at the rate earned by the deputy sheriffs. In its motion to dismiss, the county argued that the employees waived their right to contest them merit commission's promotion system by virtue of their participation in the FOP contract, which acknowledged that the merit commission had sole authority over promotions. The court held that the merit commission could not maintain, either by rule or practice, a dual entry level. Therefore, the court reversed and remanded the trial court's decision to dismiss the employees' action holding that the employees pleaded sufficient facts to indicate that they had been systematically denied rights available to others within the merit system.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's decision which dismissed the employees' complaint against the county and sheriff's department, which sought injunctive relief based on their claim that they were improperly barred from promotion within the sheriff department.

 

741 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Lee v. Pucinski


No. 1-93-0472


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


267 Ill. App. 3d 489; 642 N.E.2d 769; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1381; 204 Ill. Dec. 868



October 26, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 16, 1994. As Corrected December 13, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Richard Curry, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff litigants appealed a ruling of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their class action against defendant clerk that sought a declaration that § 27.2a(k)(5) of the Clerks of Court Act (Act), 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 105/27.2a(k)(5) was unconstitutional, to recover fees paid under the Act, and a temporary restraining order.


OVERVIEW: The litigants complained that the required fees for reproduction of documents by the clerk as mandated by the Act were unconstitutional because it violated the free access to justice clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. 1970, art. I, § 12 and the due process clause of the United States Constitution, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1. The litigants initially applied for a temporary restraining order to enjoin the clerk from charging the fees, which was denied, so they filed an amended class action complaint, which the circuit court dismissed pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-615. The court affirmed on appeal. The court rejected the litigants' assertion that 105/27.2a(k)(5) imposed a duty upon the clerk to provide the reproduction services, thus the clerk was properly following the costs laid out in the statute. The fees were only charged to those who requested the specific service of reproduction, rather than to raise general revenue, thus, there was not a chilling effect on those who sought access to the courts, and the fees were not in violation of the free access to justice clause of the Illinois Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the litigants' class action against the clerk, which sought a declaration that a provision of the Clerks of Court Act was unconstitutional and a temporary restraining order.

 

742 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


In re J.S.


No. 2-94-0216


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


267 Ill. App. 3d 145; 640 N.E.2d 1379; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1321; 204 Ill. Dec. 30


May 11, 1994, Assigned; September 13, 1994, Submitted  
October 12, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 10, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied February 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 93-J-179. Honorable Roger W. Eichmeier, Richard D. Larson, Judges, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought interlocutory review of an order from the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), seeking to vacate a gag order which prohibited the mother, her attorneys, appellee father, and his attorneys from discussing the facts in the underlying child neglect proceeding with members of the news media.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the mother asserted that the gag order (1) violated her constitutional right to free speech, (2) was an unnecessary injunctive restraint on speech in that less-restrictive alternatives existed, and (3) was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague. Finding no merit in any of the assignments of error, the court affirmed. While there was a strong presumption against the validity of prior restraints upon free speech, the danger of public disclosure and probability of irreparable adverse effects upon the child constituted a compelling state interest against such disclosure. The record indicated that the child had suffered emotional trauma because of the strife between the parents; airing that strife in the media only would have exacerbated the problem and would have constituted an egregious invasion of the child's privacy. Such interests outweighed the mother's right to take her case to the press. The court concluded by rejecting the notion that the gag order failed constitutional overbreadth and vagueness standards, particularly where a person of ordinary intelligence could read the gag order to forbid exactly what the mother wanted to do.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's gag order concerning the underlying child neglect proceeding.

People v. Feld


No. 2-93-0448


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


267 Ill. App. 3d 56; 641 N.E.2d 924; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1318; 204 Ill. Dec. 494


May 11, 1994, Assigned; September 13, 1994, Submitted  
October 11, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. Nos. 91-CM-2236, 91-CM-2237. Honorable Timothy Q. Sheldon, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which convicted them of violating the Drug Paraphernalia Control Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 2101 (1991) et seq.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were the production manager and the general manager of a company that manufactured a variety of wood products. Pursuant to a warrant, police officers seized various items alleged to be drug paraphernalia, including empty wooden boxes with sliding tops and small wooden pipes from the manufacturer's premises. Defendants were convicted of violating the Drug Paraphernalia Control Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 2101 (1991). The court reversed on the ground that the state did not prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendants possessed the requisite state of mind to market for use drug paraphernalia. Given the lack of defendants' state of mind, and the express direction of para. 2106 that all reasonable inferences be drawn in favor of the legitimacy of an item alleged to be drug paraphernalia, defendants were not proved guilty beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' convictions for violating the drug paraphernalia law.

President Lincoln Hotel Venture v. Bank One


1-92-2380, 1-92-2668 Cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


271 Ill. App. 3d 1048; 649 N.E.2d 432; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1300; 208 Ill. Dec. 376



October 3, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 5, 1995. Released for Publication May 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable MONICA REYNOLDS, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff partnerships challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their action for injunctive relief against defendants, state treasurer and banks, on the grounds that it was barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The partnerships also challenged the order disqualifying their attorneys on the grounds that they had previously represented a party related to the defendants.


OVERVIEW: The partnerships borrowed money from the state through a special mortgage program. The state treasurer appointed the bank to be the trustee and loan administrator. Defendants then required the partnerships to submit reliance letters in order to continue their loan agreements. After the partnerships, through their accountants, submitted multiple reliance letters that were rejected due to allegedly improper form, defendants pledged to declare the loans in default. The partnerships sought injunctive relief. On appeal of the lower court's dismissal of the action, the court found that the action, although seeking injunctive relief, was based on contract and, thus, was barred by 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 505/8(b) (1992), which required such claims to be brought in the court of claims. The court ruled that the partnerships' use of words such as "wrongful" were mere conclusions that could not place what was otherwise a contract action against the state within an exception to the bar of sovereign immunity. The court did find that the disqualification of the partnerships' counsel was erroneous because the attorneys' prior representation was not "substantially related" to the litigation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's dismissal of the partnerships' action in the circuit court, but the court reversed the disqualification of the partnerships' attorneys.

Miller v. Pollution Control Bd.


Nos. 4-93-0047, 4-93-0585 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


267 Ill. App. 3d 160; 642 N.E.2d 475; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1293; 204 Ill. Dec. 774


March 22, 1994, Oral Argument Held  
September 30, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 22, 1994. Petition for Rehearing Denied and Released for Publication October 27, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied February 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Administrative Review of Illinois Pollution Control Board. No. AC92-37



DISPOSITION: No. 4-93-0047, Affirmed. No. 4-93-0585, Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county initiated two administrative citation procedures with the Illinois Pollution Control Board (board) against defendant property owner. The board found that the property owner used his property as an open dump resulting in the occurrence of litter, and imposed a $ 500 penalty and ordered him to pay the costs of the hearing process which, by separate order, were assessed at $ 952.25. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: A county health inspector filed an administrative citation, alleging that the property owner caused or allowed open dumping on his property, resulting in the occurrence of litter. The property owner contested the citation, and a hearing was held. The board entered an order bifurcating the proceedings, assigning a portion of the proceedings to "Docket A" and another portion to "Docket B." The board found that the property owner committed the violation, assessed a $ 500 penalty, and ordered him to pay the hearing costs which would later be assessed in the "Docket B" proceedings. The board contended that the court did not have jurisdiction to consider the arguments raised by the property owner's first appeal as the notice of appeal was not timely filed. The court found that the appeal was actually premature because the first order was not final. The court held that the board did not have the authority, on bifurcating the administrative citation proceedings, to purport to make the first (as well as the second) order "final" for purposes of appeal. The court held, however, that the improper bifurcation of the proceedings did not render the order assessing costs void.


OUTCOME: The court found that the property owner did violate the Act, but that the board abused its discretion in assessing costs of $ 952.25. The court affirmed the violation, but reversed and remanded the order requiring the property owner to pay costs of $ 952.25.

Maher & Assocs. v. Quality Cabinets


No. 2-93-0700


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


267 Ill. App. 3d 69; 640 N.E.2d 1000; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1280; 203 Ill. Dec. 850


April 3, 1994, Assigned; September 7, 1994, Submitted  
September 29, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 2, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied February 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 91-L-0878. Honorable John S. Teschner, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant cabinet manufacturer appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which entered summary judgment in favor of plaintiff cabinet retailer and awarded compensatory damages, punitive damages, and attorney's fees in the retailer's action against the manufacturer for commissions earned after a unilateral termination of the sales contract between the parties by the manufacturer.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturer terminated the sales agreement with the retailer when the retailer began to carry the goods of another manufacturer. The manufacturer perceived the second manufacturer to be a competitor, and that the retailer's sale of the second manufacturer's products was in violation of the contract. According to the retailer's interpretation, the second manufacturer was not a competitor under the contract because of the price differences between the products. The court held that the choice of forum clause in the contract, requiring an action to be brought in Texas, was void against the public policy of the state to protect sales representatives. The choice of law forum was also voided to avoid the absurd result of applying Texas state law after the determination that Illinois policy required the dispute to be litigated in Illinois. The court held that the issue of whether the second manufacturer was a competitor of defendant manufacturer was a genuine issue of fact needed to be resolved at trial; therefore, the trial court erred in granting summary judgment in favor of the retailer. Accordingly, the award of punitive damages and attorney's fees was also error.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and the cause was remanded for further proceedings in accordance with the court's opinion.

Committee for Educ. Rights v. Edgar


No. 1-92-2379


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


267 Ill. App. 3d 18; 641 N.E.2d 602; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1286; 204 Ill. Dec. 378



September 29, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 2, 1994. Released for Publication November 10, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Thomas J. O'Brien, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, 37 school districts, 11 parents, 11 students, and an interest group, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their action against defendants, governor, board of education, and education superintendent, seeking a declaratory judgment that the Illinois School Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 1-1 et seq. (1989), violated the Illinois Constitution of 1970.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' challenged the way public education was financed in Illinois. The trial court dismissed their complaint for failure to state a cause of action. On appeal, plaintiffs argued that Illinois' statutory scheme for financing public education violated Ill. Const. art. X, § 1 (1970), the education article, and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 (1970), the equal protection clause. Plaintiffs also challenged the constitutionality of the statutory scheme applied to economically disadvantaged students. Upon review, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. Plaintiffs failed to state a cause of action that the method chosen by the legislature to finance public schools violated the education article of the Illinois Constitution. The allegation that certain educational resources were unavailable in poorer school districts, or inferior to those in wealthier districts, did not compel the conclusion that the funding provided by Illinois' financing system was insufficient to provide an adequate education. Illinois' school financing scheme was rationally related to the goal of local control, which was a legitimate state purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and held that plaintiffs failed to state a cause of action that the method chosen by the legislature to finance public schools violated the education article or equal protection clause of the Illinois Constitution.

Des Plaines Firemen's Ass'n v. City of Des Plaines


1-93-3206, 1-93-3241, consolidated


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


267 Ill. App. 3d 920; 642 N.E.2d 732; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1282; 204 Ill. Dec. 831



September 27, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified On Denial of Rehearing November 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Arthur Dunne, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant municipalities sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which rendered summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs, fireman's association and treasurer, in plaintiffs' action seeking a declaration that the municipalities were in violation of 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-10-1 (1992).


OVERVIEW: 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-10-1 (1992) granted the municipalities the authority to impose a tax on certain fire insurance policies on property located within the municipality. A prior version of the statute gave the municipalities the option of distributing the money to the local fire department or donating it to a qualified fireman's pension fund. The statute was amended to remove the latter option. Plaintiffs alleged that the municipalities were continuing to deposit the money collected in the pension funds. The municipalities argued that the amendment was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the trial court decision in favor of plaintiffs. The court found that the restrictions placed on the municipalities by the amendment did not violate home rule. Home rule municipalities had no authority to levy taxes against insurance companies. Section 5/11-10 was therefore an exceptional grant of power that could be limited as the legislature saw fit. The court also found that the amendment was not unconstitutional merely because it exempted Chicago from the statute because population classifications distinguishing Chicago from the rest of the state had long been presumed valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs in their action against the municipalities over the distribution of certain tax revenue.

People v. Martin


NO. 4-93-0278


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


266 Ill. App. 3d 369; 640 N.E.2d 638; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1235; 203 Ill. Dec. 718


August 16, 1994, Oral Argument Held  
September 15, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23 ORDER.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 29, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied February 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 93CF27. Honorable Stuart H. Shiffman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgments of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which entered the jury's convictions of three counts of reckless homicide and one count of leaving the scene of an accident. The jury had convicted defendant of three counts of reckless homicide, two counts of misdemeanor driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI), and one count of leaving the scene of an accident.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving his truck when he struck and killed three pedestrians who were walking on the wrong side of a road at night. When the state originally charged defendant with three counts of reckless homicide, three misdemeanor traffic citations were dismissed. The trial court granted the state a nol-pros. The state refiled the homicide counts and the three original citations for DUI and leaving the scene of an accident after the misdemeanor statute of limitations had expired. The trial court entered the jury's convictions for three reckless homicides and leaving the scene of an accident, but not the DUI convictions. On appeal, the court affirmed. The traffic offenses were properly charged and presented to the jury because the misdemeanor statute of limitations was tolled during the pendency of the homicide cases, the charges arose out of the same conduct alleged in the homicide cases, and the amendments did not change the substance of the original charges. The trial court properly granted the state's unopposed motion to nol-pros. The court concluded that defendant failed to show how he was prejudiced by the DUI jury instruction that included the term "proximate cause."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting and sentencing defendant on three counts of reckless homicide and one count of leaving the scene of an accident.

ILLINOIS MASONIC MED. CTR. v. A C & S


No. 1-93-2578


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


266 Ill. App. 3d 631; 640 N.E.2d 31; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1221; 203 Ill. Dec. 604



September 7, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 14, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Dean M. Trafelet, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant manufacturers filed an interlocutory appeal in plaintiff medical center's action for property damage after the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) certified the question of whether the Illinois Code of Civil Procedure, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-214(b), applied to an action against an entity, which designed and/or manufactured, but did not install, a material or product, which was used in a building during construction.


OVERVIEW: The medical center filed an action against the manufacturers alleging property damage from the integration of the manufactures' asbestos-containing products into its medical buildings. The manufacturers filed a motion to dismiss the complaint interposing a defense under § 13-214(b) of the Illinois Code of Civil Procedure, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-214(b), which the trial court granted and then reversed. Subsequently, the court granted manufacturers' motion for interlocutory appeal certifying the question of whether § 13-214(b) applied to an action against an entity which designed and/or manufactured, but did not install, a material or product which was used in a building during construction. The court held that in order to be afforded the benefit of § 13-214(b), a manufacturer must have performed some role related to the construction beyond furnishing standard products generally available to the public and not custom designed for the project.


OUTCOME: The court answered the question in the negative and remanded the case with instructions for the trial court to examine the relationship between the manufacturers' products and the construction to determine whether their products were generic or mass-produced for public consumption. If the manufacturers' products were for public consumption, they would have been outside the protection of section 13-214(b), 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-214(b).

Shelton v. Industrial Comm'n (Inland Steel Coal Co.)


NO. 5-93-0358WC


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


267 Ill. App. 3d 211; 641 N.E.2d 1216; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1217; 204 Ill. Dec. 597



September 2, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Franklin County. No. 92-MR-37. Honorable Terry H. Gamber, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured employee challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Franklin County (Illinois), which affirmed a decision of the Illinois Industrial Commission awarding him permanent loss of use of the man as a whole to the extent of 17.5 percent, pursuant to the Workers' Compensation Act (Act), 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. 310/6(c) (1992), for employee's pulmonary impairment from coal mining or comparable work with appellee employer.


OVERVIEW: The employer cross-appealed seeking dismissal of the claim for workers' compensation benefits on constitutional and statutory grounds. The court affirmed and held that the award of permanent partial disability was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court ruled that the employee's claim was not barred under § 6(c) of the Act because the employee's coal workers' pneumoconiosis (CWP) was governed by the five-year statute of limitations which was obviously intended to supplant the three-year filing requirement preceding it in section 6(c) of the Act. The court found that the amendment in § 6(c) of the Act included a special filing time for CWP based on the date of the last exposure. The court also upheld the constitutionality of the Act. The court concluded that the commission's decision was not against the manifest weight of the evidence because it was reasonably inferred from the record that employee's present state of health would not have totally prevented him from seeking other employment upon his retirement and that given his education and previous work experience there would have been a reasonably stable market for his services.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commission's decision in favor of the employer in the employee's action for workers' compensation benefits.

Villegas v. Board of Fire & Police Comm'rs


No. 2-93-0588

August 30, 1994, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Board of Fire and Police Commissioners (Board) challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which found Downers Grove, Ill., Municipal Code § 17-33(b)(1990) unconstitutional, reversed the decision of the Board discharging plaintiff fireman, and ordered the fireman reinstated with back pay and lost benefits.


OVERVIEW: The fireman was terminated for rules violations after an informal hearing. The fireman brought an action seeking reinstatement on grounds that he was entitled to a formal hearing with an opportunity to present evidence. Obasi v. Department of Professional Regulation


1-92-1430


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


266 Ill. App. 3d 693; 639 N.E.2d 1318; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1165; 203 Ill. Dec. 499



August 19, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 6, 1994. Released for Publication October 14, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE LESTER FOREMAN, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the circuit court is affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff physician appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed the revocation of the physician's medical license by defendants, the Illinois Department of Professional Regulation and its director, without opportunity to apply for reinstatement for five years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant the Illinois Department of Professional Regulation (department) revoked the medical license of plaintiff physician after finding the physician guilty of patient abandonment, gross negligence, and a pattern of practice which demonstrated incapacity or incompetence to practice medicine in violation of the Medical Practice Act of 1987 (Act). The physician filed a complaint for administrative review. The court reversed the revocation in part, holding that the abandonment charge was not supported by sufficient evidence in that no expert testimony was presented to support the charge. The court affirmed the revocation in part, holding that the findings regarding the remaining charges were correct; the Act did not violate the separation of powers or due process provisions of the Illinois Constitution; the presence of television cameras during the administrative hearing did not deprive the physician of due process; and the trial court correctly ruled that it did not have the power to reduce the sanction imposed. The court remanded the case to the department to determine whether the same or a reduced sanction should be imposed in light of the reversal of the abandonment charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part , the lower court's affirmance of the revocation of plaintiff physician's medical license and remanded to defendant the Illinois Department of Professional Regulation for further proceedings.

 

755 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Wright v. Chicago Mun. Employees' Credit Union


No. 1-92-4436


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


265 Ill. App. 3d 1110; 639 N.E.2d 203; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1166; 203 Ill. Dec. 164



August 19, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Name of this Case has been Corrected August 29, 1994. Released for Publication September 27, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Thomas J. O'Brien Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city employee appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which entered summary judgment in favor of defendants, credit union, retirement fund, and fund's trustees, in the employee's action concerning a deduction from his retirement fund account.


OVERVIEW: The city employee borrowed money from the credit union and executed a power of attorney permitting the credit union to collect any balance due from amounts to be refunded to him at the time of his separation from the city. When he left city employment a few years later, the retirement fund deducted money from the employee's account and paid it to the credit union to pay off the remaining balance. The employee filed suit alleging that the credit union's and retirement fund's actions were contrary to § 8-244 of the Illinois Pension Code. The trial court entered summary judgment for the credit union, retirement fund, and the fund's trustees. On appeal, the court affirmed. A prior case interpreting § 8-244 did not collaterally estop the court from independently interpreting the section because in the prior case the judge decided an unmixed question of law. The court affirmed the trial court's determination that § 8-244, even before its 1991 amendment, permitted assignments of refunds. The legislature did not use "refund" in the section as it did in other sections.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting the credit union, retirement fund, and fund's trustees summary judgment was affirmed, in the employee's action concerning a deduction from his retirement fund account.

People v. Almendarez


Nos. 1-90-1863, 1-91-0171 Consolidated


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


266 Ill. App. 3d 639; 639 N.E.2d 619; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1163; 203 Ill. Dec. 299



August 18, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 21, 1994. Released for Publication September 27, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 6, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied February 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Shelvin Singer, Judge Presiding.
People v. Galvan, 244 Ill. App. 3d 298, 614 N.E.2d 391, 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 442, 185 Ill. Dec. 257 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 1993)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions for aggravated arson and the murder of two people who died in the fire as well as their life sentences in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). Defendants alleged various errors by the trial court that deprived them of a fair trial and also argued that their sentences were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants and his accomplice were gang members. They burned down a rival gang member's house, which resulted in the deaths of two people. The accomplice then confessed. Defendants were convicted of aggravated arson and murder, and sentenced to life without parole. On consolidated appeal, the court affirmed. The court held as to one defendant that he was not arrested without probable cause because he was implicated by the accomplice, who described defendant's actions and was found to be reliable. The court held as to the other defendant that while a witness' prior inconsistent statement was erroneously admitted as substantive rather than impeaching evidence, such error was harmless in light of the ample evidence of defendant's guilt. As to both defendants, the court held that witness testimony that defendants were gang members was admissible because it provided a motive for an otherwise inexplicable act. In addition, § 5-8-1(a)(1)(c) of the Unif. Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 105-8-1(a)(1)(c) (1990), under which defendants were sentenced to mandatory life imprisonment without parole, was held to be constitutional based on state precedent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for aggravated arson and murder and their life sentences without parole.

People v. Robinson


1-92-3704


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


267 Ill. App. 3d 900; 642 N.E.2d 1317; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1151; 205 Ill. Dec. 200



August 16, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing November 29, 1994. As Corrected September 15, 1994. Rehearing Denied November 16, 1994. Released for Publication December 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Thomas P. Durkin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court rejected defendant's argument that the bodily injury the victim suffered was inherent in offense of criminal sexual assault and should not have served as an aggravating factor of bodily harm. The court reasoned that there was sufficient evidence presented at trial that enabled the trial court to conclude that the victim suffered bodily harm other than that inherent in the offense. The evidence included the victim's testimony that it hurt when defendant's penis touched her vagina, and the medical evidence indicating a perforated hymen, absent hymenal ring, and "old" blood in the vagina, and ecchymotic or dark purple in two areas of the vagina. The court held that the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing defendant to concurrent rather than the consecutive terms of imprisonment required under Ill. Code Civ. P., 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4(a). The court affirmed the sentencing however, holding that ordering the trial court to impose consecutive sentences might have been a prohibited expansion of the State's limited right to appeal in a criminal case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault and remanded the cause for sentencing on the third count of the offense.

Sharma v. Zollar


1-91-3834


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


265 Ill. App. 3d 1022; 638 N.E.2d 736; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1133; 202 Ill. Dec. 868



August 5, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 13, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE JOHN HOURIHANE, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff physician brought an administrative review action against defendant Illinois Department of Professional Regulation (department) to contest the denial of his request for subpoenas pursuant to Ill. Admin. Code tit. 68, § 1110.140 (Supp. 1988). The physician sought a declaratory judgment that the provision was void on its face and as applied. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the department's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The physician was charged with violating the Medical Practice Act of 1987 (Medical Malpractice Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 4400-1 et seq. (1987). The physician sought a declaratory judgment against the department that Ill. Admin. Code tit. 68, 1110.140 (Supp. 1988) was void on its face and as applied. The physician also sought a writ of mandamus ordering the director of the department to issue the requested subpoenas. On appeal, the court held that the physician's need for the requested subpoenas was eliminated and his right to them became moot when the department adopted the medical disciplinary board's finding that the department had failed to prove the physician's violation of the Medical Practice Act. The court held that the physician did not meet the public interest exception to the mootness doctrine because the exception was invoked only in cases involving an extraordinary degree of public concern and only where the public interest was very clear.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment rendered in favor of the department.
