Luperini v. County of Du Page


No. 2-93-0438


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


265 Ill. App. 3d 84; 637 N.E.2d 1264; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1104; 202 Ill. Dec. 528


June 1, 1994, Submitted  
July 22, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 22, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 91-MR-657. Honorable John S. Teschner, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) that denied the landowner's petition for a writ of mandamus against defendants, county, county environmental agency, and highway commission (county), to compel the county to award damages for a taking. The trial court granted the county's motion for summary judgment to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: Landowners filed a complaint for a writ of mandamus and sought to compel the institution of condemnation proceedings after the county had installed a storm sewer on an adjoining parcel of land that caused a diversion of runoff water onto their property. Both the landowners and the county moved for summary judgment. The court denied the landowners' motion and granted the county's motion. The landowners sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that: (1) the landowners' use of the term "continuous" to describe the state of flooding on their property was arguably imprecise and misleading; (2) there was no evidence that the flooding caused a permanent accumulation of water on the landowners' property; (3) the landowners showed no actual physical invasion of their property, which deprived them of the use of the land; (4) there was no evidence that the property was a "retention site" because the water was not permanent; and (5) the undisputed facts showed that no taking occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that denied the landowners' petition for a writ of mandamus against the county and granted the county's motion for summary judgment to dismiss the complaint.

 

760 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Waller v. 1992 Oldsmobile Station Wagon


No. 2-93-0485


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


265 Ill. App. 3d 93; 638 N.E.2d 373; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1100; 202 Ill. Dec. 727


July 8, 1994, Submitted  
July 20, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 25, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 92-MR-610. Honorable Raymond J. McKoski, Judge, Presiding



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) of possession with the intent to offer for sale untaxed cigarettes, Ill. Rev. State. Ch. 120, para. 453.24 (1991). The trial court ordered forfeiture of defendant's automobile under § 36-1 of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 36-1 (1991) (current version at 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/36-1 (1992)). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police stopped defendant's car and recovered from the vehicle 40 cartons of cigarettes, none of which contained tax stamps. Section 36-1 allowed for forfeiture of any vehicle a defendant knowingly used in the commission of any offense prohibited by the Cigarette Tax Act. Defendant argued that the forfeiture was an excessive fine in violation of the Eighth Amendment. The court reversed the trial court's ruling, which ordered the forfeiture of defendant's car. The court noted that in rem civil forfeiture was punishment for purposes of the Eighth Amendment. Some degree of nexus between the property and the commission of the offense was required to permit forfeiture. The court remanded the case to the trial court for the trial court to consider various factors such as the extent to which the car facilitated the offenses, examination of the value of the property, and examination of the relative seriousness of the offense. The fact that defendant was 69 years old and cared for his retarded son were additional factors to consider.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the ruling of the trial court, which ordered forfeiture of defendant's car pursuant to his conviction for possession with intent to offer for sale untaxed cigarettes. The court remanded for further proceedings.

 

761 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Roberts


No. 1-91-4003


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


265 Ill. App. 3d 400; 638 N.E.2d 359; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1097; 202 Ill. Dec. 713



July 20, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 25, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE MARY MAXWELL THOMAS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated battery with a firearm, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-4.2 (1991).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated battery with a firearm and he appealed. The court reversed and remanded. The court held that the failure of the trial court to give a jury instruction concerning the lesser-included offense of reckless conduct was reversible error. Where there was even slight evidence in the record that, if believed by the jury, would have reduced a crime to a lesser-included offense, an instruction defining the lesser-included offense should have been given. Where such evidence existed, the trial court could not weigh the evidence in deciding whether an issue had been raised entitling defendant to the instruction. In addition, the aggravated battery statute was not unconstitutional when the legislature mandated a harsher sentence to those who used forearms in the commission of a crime because the frequency of a crime and the high risk of bodily harm associated with a crime could also be considered in determining the seriousness of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for aggravated battery with a firearm and remanded.

Village of Vernon Hills v. Vernon Fire Protection Dist. (In re Village of Vernon Hills)


No. 2-93-0162


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


265 Ill. App. 3d 46; 637 N.E.2d 1240; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1102; 202 Ill. Dec. 504


June 8, 1994, Submitted  
July 20, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 22, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Allowed December 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 92-MC-15. Honorable Jack Hoogasian Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Objector fire district appealed from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) judgment in favor of petitioner village to transfer a portion of its fire protection area to respondent fire district under § 14.14 of the Fire Protection District Act (Act), 70 Ill. Comp. Stat. 705/14.14, following denial of its post-judgment motion, arguing that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The non-home-rule village sought to disconnect certain territory of the objecting fire district and transfer it to respondent district, relying on the disconnection provisions of § 14.4 of the Act. The objecting district argued that the Act was unconstitutional as a special or local law applying only to a county with a population of half to three-quarters of a million. It tried unsuccessfully to have the petition dismissed under § 2-619(a)(9) of the Code of Civil Procedure, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-619(a)(9). The circuit court concluded the statute was constitutional and the objector's arguments were moot. It granted the petition. The district argued the classification limiting application based on population was arbitrary and did not bear a rational and proper relation to the evil to be remedied. The court reversed, holding § 14.4 unconstitutional, agreeing with the objecting district that the Act was special legislation and the limiting classification was arbitrary. There was no relationship between county population and the need for municipalities to consolidate fire protection districts or any indication that one county was distinct from any other for purposes of the Act.


OUTCOME: The judgment for the village, transferring fire district territory to another district, was reversed and remanded with directions, because the relevant statutory section violated the state constitution. The circuit court was ordered to restore the parties to their status quo ante.

Dodt v. Roy (In re Estate of Roy)


No. 3-93-0657


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


265 Ill. App. 3d 99; 637 N.E.2d 1228; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1094; 202 Ill. Dec. 492


February 9, 1994, Submitted  
July 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 22, 1994. As Corrected August 30, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County, Illinois. No. 93-P-49. Honorable Sheldon Reagan Judge, Presiding



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a petition to adjudicate a wife as disabled was filed, the disabled person filed a petition to appoint her husband as guardian. Appellant husband sought review of the order of the Circuit Court Kankakee County (Illinois) dismissing the wife's petition pursuant to 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11a-5(a) (1992), which precluded convicted felons from acting as guardians, and appointing appellee daughter as guardian.


OVERVIEW: The wife filed a petition to have her husband appointed as her guardian, but the petition was denied due to the husband's felony conviction. The court held that the motivation of the General Assembly in enacting 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11a-5(a) (1992) was to protect the vulnerable. This was in accord with the paramount concern surrounding the selection of a guardian which was in the best interest and well-being of the incompetent. The bill of attainder clause was not violated and the court found no ex post facto violation. However, the court found that § 5/11a-5(a), although constitutional, could have been unconstitutionally applied to the husband. It could have been found that there was no rational basis for treating a person with a 36-year old felony conviction differently from any other husband of 43 years who sought to be appointed as his wife's guardian upon her becoming disabled. The court held that if on remand the husband proved by a preponderance of the evidence that he was fit and that his appointment would have served the wife's best interests, it would find that the law was unconstitutionally applied and would give due consideration to the wife's choice of a guardian.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment dismissing the wife's petition to have her husband appointed as her guardian and remanded the cause for a hearing to determine if the husband's appointment would serve the best interests and welfare of the wife.

Richardson v. Mulcahey


No. 3-93-0976


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


265 Ill. App. 3d 123; 637 N.E.2d 1217; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1085; 202 Ill. Dec. 481



July 15, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 22, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County. No. 93-MR-182. Honorable Jay M. Hanson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervening plaintiff candidate appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois), which held that 55 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-5005(b) (1992), under which a referendum was held, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: A county held a referendum asking voters to determine whether to adopt the county executive form of government and elect not to become a home rule unit. The voters approved the referendum and an election was scheduled to elect the county's chief executive. The candidate challenged the constitutionality of 55 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-5005(b) (1992), which provided the model language for the referendum. The trial court ruled that the challenged statute was constitutional. On appeal, the court granted expedited consideration and held that § 2-5005(b) was a valid method of allowing counties to choose an executive form of government and opt out of home-rule status as permitted by Ill. Const. art. VII, §§ 6(a), 6(b). The court held that the state constitution did not require the decision to choose a county executive form of government and the decision to opt out of home-rule status in separate elections. The court held that Ill. Const. art. III, § 3 allowed the two issues to be joined in one referendum because they were reasonably related to a common objective in a workable manner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision finding that a statute under which a referendum was held was constitutional.

OVERVIEW: Defendant set the victims' house on fire while they were in the house, killing them. Defendant later came back to the house and stole items. CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the State's petition to revoke defendant's probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to burglary and violation of bail bond. He was sentenced to one years' probation and six months' imprisonment. During the probationary term, the State filed a petition to revoke defendant's probation for failure to report to his probation officer. Several months later, a hearing was conducted on the petition, and defendant was sentenced to 30 days' imprisonment. A few weeks later, defendant was arrested for participation in a robbery. After defendant's probationary term expired, the State filed a second petition for revocation of defendant's probation based on the arrest. On appeal, the court held that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to rule on the State's petition because it was filed after the expiration of defendant's probationary term. The court also held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-6-4(a)(3) (1991) did not extend defendant's probationary term by the amount of the period tolled for the first revocation proceeding, which was commenced and completed within the probationary term.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's judgment.

People v. Weatherspoon


No. 1-91-2406


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


265 Ill. App. 3d 386; 637 N.E.2d 651; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1002; 202 Ill. Dec. 112



June 29, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 12, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Marcia Orr, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the rulings of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of criminal sexual assault, robbery, and unlawful restraint. The trial court held that the rape shield statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-7 (1991), did not allow defendant to present evidence of the victim's alleged history of trading sexual favors for drugs.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that defendant had not shown the extraordinary circumstances needed to meet the "prior pattern exception" to the rape shield statute because there was no showing of distinctive characteristics or a modus operandi, and defendant was allowed to present his theory of defense by other means. The court held that defendant's right of confrontation was not violated by restrictions on his cross-examination of the victim because the entire record showed that the jury was made aware of many factors concerning relevant areas of impeachment through testimony as to her history of drugs and alcohol and testimony related to possible consent. The court also found that an acquittal of aggravated criminal sexual assault was not an inconsistent verdict because the evidence showed a time lag between the sexual assault and the taking of jewelry. The court found that a prosecutor's comments were based on the evidence, not personal opinion, and that any possible error from a reference to another case was cured by the prompt ruling of the trial court and an admonition to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of criminal sexual assault, robbery, and unlawful restraint.

La Salle Nat'l Trust, N.A. v. Village of Westmont


Nos. 2-93-0804, 2-93-1070, 2-93-1107 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


264 Ill. App. 3d 43; 636 N.E.2d 1157; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1026; 201 Ill. Dec. 725


May 24, 1994, Submitted  
June 29, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 3, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 92-CH-509. Honorable Bonnie M. Wheaton, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 2-93-0804, Affirmed. No. 2-93-1107, Reversed and remanded. No. 2-93-1070, Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sought injunctive and declaratory relief against defendants, a village, a landowner and a bank, alleging, inter alia, the invalidity of the rezoning granted to the land owner by the village. The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) found the rezoning unconstitutional, but found for the village and the landowner in all other respects. The village and the landowner appealed and the property owners cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The village rezoned a parcel purchased from the bank by the landowner to a residential development, despite the property owner's opposition, whose hotel and golf course were adjacent to the parcel. The trial court found the rezoning unconstitutional because combining the proposed residential use with the hotel and golf course would have a negative effect on public health, safety, and welfare, but granted summary judgment to the landowner on the property owners' claim for sum owed on an easement. The trial court also dismissed the bank's counterclaim that alleged that the rezoning was valid. The village and the landowner argued that the trial court erred in finding the rezoning unconstitutional by not looking beyond the hotel and the golf course. The property owners argued that the trial court misconstrued the easement agreement. The bank argued that it had standing to bring its counterclaim. The court held that there was sufficient evidence for the trial court's finding that the rezoning was unconstitutional and that the trial court incorrectly found that the property owners had no lien pursuant to the easement agreement. The dismissal of the bank's counterclaim was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in all respects the trial court's decision, which declared the rezoning unconstitutional, but reversed the order that granted summary judgment to the landowner on the reimbursement due to plaintiffs and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings. The court further affirmed the trial court's order, which dismissed the bank's counterclaim.

Ligon ex rel. Williams v. Williams


1-94-0445


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


264 Ill. App. 3d 701; 637 N.E.2d 633; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 996; 202 Ill. Dec. 94



June 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 12, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE SAUL A. PERDOMO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Custody order vacated; custody reinstated in plaintiff.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother filed two complaints that requested the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) to find a parent-child relationship between her child and defendant father and to order the father to pay child support. The court held a hearing in which the mother was absent, found that a parent-child relationship existed, and awarded custody to the father. The trial court denied the mother's petition to return custody. She appealed.


OVERVIEW: Three attempts to effect service of process upon the father resulted in the sheriff's return of "not found." He was finally served with summons and a hearing was set. The state's attorney sent notice of the hearing to the mother, but she contended that she never received it. The father admitted paternity asked for custody of the child. The mother argued that the trial court's ruling awarding custody to the father was void because the issue of custody was not properly before the court. The parentage petition was not directed at custody. The court held that the trial court erred when it entered the custody order because its authority to decide the custody issue was not activated through the proper procedural mechanism. The only justiciable questions raised by the petition were the establishment of a parent/child relationship between the child and the father and his support obligation.


OUTCOME: The court ordered a return to the status quo ante by vacation of the custody order and reinstatement of custody of the child with the mother.

 

771 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Garrett


No. 1-93-1168


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


264 Ill. App. 3d 1089; 637 N.E.2d 615; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 969; 202 Ill. Dec. 76



June 24, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 12, 1994.
As Corrected August 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE RICHARD LaCIEN, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found defendant guilty of criminal sexual assault and aggravated criminal sexual abuse of a fourteen year old girl in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-13, 12-16 (1991). Defendant argued that the trial court violated his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to a public trial by excluding his parents from the courtroom while the girl testified.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of criminal sexual assault and aggravated criminal sexual abuse. The court reversed the conviction and remanded, holding that the trial court committed reversible error in ordering the removal of defendant's parents during his alleged victim's testimony without first determining whether closure of the trial was justified. The court held that the presumption of openness was not overcome and defendant was denied his constitutional right to a public trial where the trial court failed to determine whether the "overriding interest" advanced by the state was legitimate. The court found that the trial court did not give due consideration to the girl's maturity and understanding, notwithstanding a showing by defendant that she possessed a level of sophistication exceeding that of others her age, did not inquire as to why or to what degree the complainant felt uncomfortable in the presence of defendant's parents, and failed to consider whether reasonable alternatives to closure were available.


OUTCOME: On appeal, the court reversed defendant's convictions for criminal sexual assault and aggravated criminal sexual abuse and remanded.

 

772 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Segarra v. Chicago Transit Auth.


No. 1-92-3674


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


265 Ill. App. 3d 480; 637 N.E.2d 572; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 978; 202 Ill. Dec. 33



June 23, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 12, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable John J. Crown, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff passenger appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the passenger's personal injury action because the passenger had failed to give the six month notice required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 341 (1985) to defendants, bus driver and transit authority.


OVERVIEW: The passenger alleged that the bus driver's negligence injured her as she stepped off a moving bus. Her action was filed one year after the injury, and the passenger claimed to have notified the transit authority's general attorney within six months after the accident. The lower court dismissed the passenger's action because she failed to comply with § 341, and the court affirmed. The court held that § 341 was to be strictly construed and that it required that notice be given to both the transit authority's general attorney and its secretary. Because the passenger failed to notify the secretary, her action against it failed. The court ruled that even though the six month notice requirement of § 341 was shorter than the one year notification requirement contained in the Tort Immunity Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1991, ch. 85, para. 8-101 (1991), the six-month notification requirement did not violate the passenger's equal protection rights because the transit authority was so large that it performed unique functions which justified differences between its liability and the liability imposed on other entities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, which dismissed the passenger's personal injury action against the transit authority and the bus driver.

People v. Latona


No. 2-92-1014


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


268 Ill. App. 3d 718; 644 N.E.2d 424; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1120; 205 Ill. Dec. 868


June 3, 1994, Submitted  
June 21, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rule 23 Order Redesignated Opinion and Ordered Published. Petitions for Rehearing Denied July 29, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lee County. No. 89-CF-114. Honorable Thomas E. Hornsby, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Lee County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of solicitation of murder and imposed an extended-term sentence of 40 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: While in prison, defendant sought out the services of a fellow inmate's gang buddies to arrange the murder of his daughter's boyfriend. The inmate informed police who sent an undercover cop to arrange the details of the hit with defendant. Defendant at first requested only that the boyfriend be injured, but after repeated prodding by the undercover officer, admitted he wouldn't mind if the boyfriend were killed. Defendant was convicted of solicitation of murder. The court found that there was sufficient evidence for the trial court to find that defendant was predisposed to commit the offence of solicitation of murder rather than solicitation of aggravated battery and that defendant was not entrapped. The court also found that the mere fact that the crime of solicitation of murder carried a harsher penalty than other felonies in the same class did not mean that defendant could not be sentenced to an extended prison term under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-1. Finally, the court found that the trial court erred in considering the threat of serious harm as an aggravating factor in sentencing because that factor was part of the crime charged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for solicitation of murder but vacated his sentence and remanded for resentencing.

People v. Emmett


No. 1-92-3427


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


264 Ill. App. 3d 296; 636 N.E.2d 1035; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 888; 201 Ill. Dec. 603



June 10, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Leo Holt, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), defendant was convicted of counterfeiting a temporary vehicle permit, in violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/4-105 (1992). Defendant appealed, claiming the Anti-Theft Laws of the vehicle code, of which § 4-105 was a part, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after a police officer encountered the vehicle he was riding in, which had a counterfeit temporary registration permit in its back window. When questioned about the counterfeit permit, defendant told the officer that he made it. At trial, the parties stipulated that the records of the Illinois Secretary of State showed that the vehicle in question was registered to a codefendant. On appeal, defendant claimed that he owned the vehicle and based on precedent of the Illinois Supreme Court, that his conviction violated due process. Though the court rejected the State's claim that the issue was waived because it was not raised at trial, emphasizing that constitutional challenges to legislation could be raised at any time, it affirmed the judgment. In doing so, the court ruled that because the parties had stipulated at trial that a codefendant owned the vehicle, no evidence on the issue of ownership was presented. Given that, the record was not sufficiently developed to rule on the question of ownership, and because defendant's ownership of the car was an essential element to the success of his appeal, it necessarily failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of counterfeiting a temporary vehicle permit, in violation of Illinois law.

North Pole Corp. v. Village of E. Dundee


No. 2-93-0655


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


263 Ill. App. 3d 327; 635 N.E.2d 1060; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 911; 200 Ill. Dec. 721


May 25, 1994, Submitted  
June 10, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 19, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 93-CH-0185. Honorable R. Peter Grometer, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant non-profit corporation, which owned and operated an amusement park within the corporate limits of appellee village, filed suit for a declaratory judgment that an amusement tax enacted by the village was unconstitutional and void. The non-profit corporation challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) denying its request for a preliminary injunction that would prevent the enforcement or collection of the tax.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented on appeal was whether the non-profit corporation raised a fair question of whether the amusement tax violated equal protection, the requirement of uniformity of taxation, Ill. Const. art. IX, § 265 (1970), or the prohibition on impermissible special assessments, 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-2-45. The court held that the trial court's denial of the requested relief was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The trial court had sufficient grounds to conclude that non-profit corporation had not demonstrated likelihood of success on the merits. The court found that the amusement tax offended neither uniformity nor equal protection as it was directed against customers rather than against the non-profit corporation. In rejecting the non-profit corporation's argument that the burden of the tax was disproportionate to the benefit it received, the court also found that the ordinance imposed a general revenue tax for the benefit of the village as a whole. The court concluded that the amusement ordinance could not be considered a special assessment because it was never designed to exact a charge in return for a particular benefit to a specific property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying the non-profit corporation its prayer for preliminary injunctive relief.

People v. Lukach


No. 2-93-0627


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


263 Ill. App. 3d 318; 635 N.E.2d 1053; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 903; 200 Ill. Dec. 714


May 13, 1994, Submitted  
June 8, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 19, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 91-CF-1291. Honorable Thomas E. Hogan and James T. Doyle, Judges, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: People challenged the order upon reconsideration of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence of a blood-alcohol concentration test.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for the offense of reckless homicide. He was involved in a single-car accident in which his passenger was fatally injured. Later, at the hospital, police requested that defendant submit to a blood-alcohol concentration test under 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 11-501.6 (1992). Defendant agreed and when blood was taken he was not under arrest. The trial court allowed defendant's motion to suppress on the basis that the statute had been declared unconstitutional. The state contended, on appeal, that probable cause existed to conduct a warrantless and nonconsensual search or test of defendant independent of the statute, regardless of the officer's belief that there was no probable cause to test the defendant. The court held that there had to be particularized probable cause to believe defendant was driving under the influence of alcohol or a drug before he could be tested without violating the constitutional prohibition against unreasonable searches and seizures. Here, the officer's testimony showed that defendant was not intoxicated at the time of the accident. Defendant had none of the customary indicia of intoxication and was not arrested at the time of the accident.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

People v. Murphy


No. 2-92-1249


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


261 Ill. App. 3d 1019; 635 N.E.2d 110; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 843; 200 Ill. Dec. 9


May 11, 1994, Submitted  
June 1, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of De Kalb County. No. 91-CF-352. Honorable Philip L. DiMarzio, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part as modified; vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of De Kalb County (Illinois) that convicted him of armed violence, aggravated unlawful restraint, unlawful possession of a firearm by a felon, aggravated assault, and unlawful violation of an order of protection.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed violence, aggravated unlawful restraint, unlawful possession of a firearm by a felon, aggravated assault, and unlawful violation of an order of protection after he forced his way into his ex-wife's car while holding a sawed off shotgun and forced her to driven them to a park. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed in part and vacated in part. Defendant contended that the armed violence charge and the aggravated unlawful restraint charge were identical offenses and disproportionate. The court disagreed. A person could commit aggravated unlawful restraint by using a deadly weapon rather than a dangerous weapon and not simultaneously commit armed violent. Thus, allowing unlawful restraint to be used as the predicate offense for armed violence did not nullify the aggravated unlawful restraint charge. The court found that the charge for aggravated assault arose out of the same single physical act as the aggravated unlawful restraint and therefore was an improper multiple conviction. The court therefore vacated the aggravated assault charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and vacated in part the judgment convicting defendant of armed violence, aggravated unlawful restraint, unlawful possession of a firearm by a felon, aggravated assault, and unlawful violation of an order of protection.

Hewette v. Carbondale Zoning Bd. of Appeals


No. 5-93-0255


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


261 Ill. App. 3d 803; 634 N.E.2d 1223; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 827; 199 Ill. Dec. 869



May 27, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County. No. 92-MR-3. Honorable E. Dan Kimmel, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which affirmed a decision of defendant, the Carbondale Zoning Board of Appeals, and denied the property owner a zoning variance.


OVERVIEW: The property owner's building and original porch did not meet the setback requirement of § 15-2-30(J) of the Carbondale zoning ordinances, Carbondale, Ill., Revised Code § 15-2-30(J) (1990), but they were classified as nonconforming structures. The property owner built a new porch that encroached on the minimum setback, and the Board denied a variance. The property owner argued that the variance would keep much of the snow and ice from falling on the sidewalks used by his tenants. The Board found that there were no special conditions or circumstances peculiar to the building and that the property owner would not be deprived of rights enjoyed by other property owners if the variance was denied. The court concluded that the Board's decision was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court held that the language of Carbondale, Ill., Revised Code § 15-2-102 (1990) was not unconstitutionally vague because § 15-2-102(B) served as a sufficient guide to ascertaining whether a variance could be granted. The property owner failed to show by clear and convincing evidence that the denial of the variance was unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

People v. Williams


No. 1-92-3752


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


263 Ill. App. 3d 1098; 638 N.E.2d 207; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 826; 202 Ill. Dec. 561



May 27, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 19, 1994. As Modified July 29, 1994. Released for Publication August 2, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Thomas P. Cawley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting him of four counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault and two counts of aggravated kidnapping, and sentencing him to a prison term of eight years for each of the of four counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault and four years for each of the two counts of aggravated kidnapping, all of which ran consecutively for a total sentence of 40 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant forced the complainants into his vehicle at gunpoint and drove them to an alley where he forced them to engage in oral sex and sexual intercourse with him. Defendant was convicted and sentenced. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded. The court held that defendant's consecutive sentences for aggravated criminal sexual assault under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4(a) did not violate the due process or equal protection clauses of the United State Constitution because there was a reasonable basis for denying those guilty of sexual assault the benefits of concurrent sentencing under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4(b) (1992). Further, § 5/5-8-4(a) did not violate the due process or disproportionate penalty clauses of the Illinois Constitution of 1970. Defendant committed four distinct acts of aggravated criminal sexual assault on the complainants, and thus, his sentence was proportionate to his acts. However, while 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 5/5-8-4 was not unconstitutionally vague, it contained ambiguities when applied to certain factual settings because it did not expressly indicated which sentences were required to run consecutively.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for aggravated criminal sexual assault and aggravated kidnapping. The court vacated one of defendant's two sentences for aggravated kidnapping and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) convicted defendant of stalking in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-7.3(a)(2) (1992) and sentenced defendant to 30 months probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant threatened to hurt or kill his wife if she went through with a pending divorce and was found on the wife's property on more than one occasion, twice with a video camera which he used to tape the house, even going inside and taping his wife and a male companion in the bedroom on one of those occasions. These were the facts upon which the trial court based defendant's stalking conviction and, on appeal, the court affirmed. The court also found that the taping of the house and the cars near the house could be considered surveillance as the stalking statute used that term.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction after finding defendant threatened his wife and subjected her to his surveillance on two separate occasions.

People v. Szudy


1-91-3950


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


262 Ill. App. 3d 695; 635 N.E.2d 801; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 770; 200 Ill. Dec. 462



May 16, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 14, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable JOHN MORAN, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of first-degree murder and concealment of a homicidal death. The trial court sentenced defendant to a sentence of natural life imprisonment to be served consecutively with a five-year sentence of imprisonment for concealment of the death, pursuant to the habitual criminal statute, Ill. Comp. Stat. ch. 720, para. 5/33B-1 (1992).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and concealment of a homicidal death. Pursuant to the habitual criminal statute, Ill. Comp. Stat. ch. 720, para. 5/33B-1 (1992), the trial court sentenced defendant to a sentence of natural life imprisonment to be served consecutively with a five-year sentence of imprisonment for concealment of the death, and defendant sought review. The court held that threats made by defendant against the victim prior to a criminal act against that victim were admissible to show malice and criminal intent. The court held that the trial court had the primary responsibility of conducting the voir dire examination and that the scope and manner of such questioning was within its broad discretion. The court held that photographs of the deceased victim were admissible if they tended to establish any fact in issue or any element of the crime charged in spite of the fact that they could have been of a gruesome or disgusting nature. The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of first-degree murder and concealment of a homicidal death and sentenced him pursuant to the habitual criminal statute. The court held that threats made by defendant against the victim prior to a criminal act against that victim were admissible to show malice and criminal intent. Photographs of deceased victim were admissible to establish any element of charged crime.

Granny's Rocker, Inc. v. Illinois Liquor Control Comm'n


No. 5-92-0861


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 779



May 16, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. Nos. 91-MR-291 & 91-MR-341. Honorable Lola P. Maddox, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court reversed; suspension vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff licensee appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which affirmed a ruling of defendant Illinois Liquor Control Commission finding the licensee violated §§ 6-28 and 10-1 of the Liquor Control Act of 1934 (Act) by promoting games or contests involving the drinking of alcoholic beverages. The licensee appealed on the grounds including that § 6-28 was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The violations stemmed from promotions in which women received unlimited alcoholic beverages at a nominal price, and patrons were encouraged to sit in a barber chair, receive multiple shots of liquor, and received a T-shirt. The circuit court affirmed the commission's decision suspending the licensee's liquor license for 30 days. On appeal, the court held that the licensee met its burden of demonstrating the invalidity of § 6-28 of the Act, 235 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 5/6-28(b)(5) (1992). The statute prohibited retail licensees from encouraging or permitting any "game or contest" that involved drinking alcoholic liquor. The court held that § 6-28 of the Act was vague and uncertain and was unconstitutional in that it violated the due process rights of those it is intended to regulate. Persons of ordinary intelligence, upon reading the statute, would not know what they could or could not do to avoid violating its provisions. The court noted that the broad interpretation of the Act as advocated on behalf of the commission would preclude taverns from permitting patrons to watch the Super Bowl on television or allow customers to play foosball.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment and vacated the 30-day suspension of the licensee's liquor license.

People v. Dukes

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, who were brothers, sought review of a judgment by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted one defendant of first degree murder and attempted first degree murder and the other defendant of first degree murder on a theory of accountability.


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed that the second degree murder statute was unconstitutional in that it deprived a defendant of being able to prove self-defense, the evidence was insufficient to prove that accountability of defendant for first degree murder as an accomplice, and the prosecution's closing argument was error. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendants of first degree murder, attempted first degree murder, and first degree murder on a theory of accountability, holding that the second degree murder statute did not deprive defendants of the right to prove self-defense and the evidence failed to show that defendants acted in self-defense, which was based on the killing of one person and the wounding of another in a gang related home invasion that was in retaliation for a person being ejected from a party. The court further held that the prosecution's argument, which may have been inappropriate, was cured by defendants' immediate objection and the trial court's jury instruction to disregard the argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted one defendant of first degree murder and attempted first degree murder and convicted another defendant of first degree murder.

Moushon v. AAA Amusement


NO. 4-93-0971


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


267 Ill. App. 3d 187; 641 N.E.2d 1201; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 619; 204 Ill. Dec. 582


April 12, 1994, Oral Argument Held  
April 29, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 23, 1994. As Modified on Denial of Rehearing November 3, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 92L0045. Honorable Richard J. Cadagin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tavern owners appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which awarded plaintiff patrons damages for losses the patrons suffered while using illegal gambling machines at the tavern.


OVERVIEW: The tavern owners contended that the statute allowing for treble damages, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/28-8 (1992), violated federal and state constitutional provisions, that the evidence did not support the verdict, that the trial court improperly instructed the jury, and that the patrons perpetrated a fraud on the tavern owners and the trial court. The court held that that statute did not violate equal protection or Ill. Const. art. IV, §13 and that there was a rational basis for exempting repayment of certain gambling losses but not other types. The court also held that there was sufficient proof to support the verdict, including the testimony of a tavern patron estimating her losses. The court determined that the trial court did not err in instructing the jury and by communicating with the jury because the instructions were proper, and the judge's communication with the jury was neutral and non-prejudicial. Finally, the court held that the patrons did not perpetrate a fraud on the tavern owners or the trial court. According to the court, there was sufficient evidence upon which the jury could have found that the patrons did not commit fraud and the court affirmed the decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which awarded the patrons damages for losses the patrons suffered while using the tavern owners' illegal gambling machines.

 

787 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lann


1-90-2966


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


261 Ill. App. 3d 456; 633 N.E.2d 938; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 588; 199 Ill. Dec. 142



April 19, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 7, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JOHN M. MANNION, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of armed robbery, kidnapping, aggravated kidnapping, and aggravated battery. On a prior appeal, the court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence but remanded the case for a Batson hearing. Defendant appealed the trial court's determination that he did not make out a prima facie case of racial discrimination under Batson.


OVERVIEW: Six of the seven potential jurors excused by the state were African-Americans, and six of the seven were women. The court affirmed the trial court's finding that defendant failed to make out a prima facie case of racial discrimination under Batson. The court held that: 1) six of nine African-American venirepersons did not constitute a pattern of strikes; 2) the prosecutor's statements did not evidence an intent to discriminate; 3) the excluded venire members shared a common characteristic, being unmarried, besides being of the same race; 4) the percentage difference in the level of African-American representation in the venire as compared to the jury was only slight evidence of discriminatory intent; and 5) because both the victim and defendant were black, their racial characteristics did not warrant an inference of discrimination. Although defendant had waived his claim of gender-based discrimination in the use of peremptory challenges, the issue was reviewable under the plain error rule. The court held that Batson applied to gender-based discrimination under both Batson and the Illinois Constitution. Thus, the court remanded the action for a Batson hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's determination that defendant failed to present a prima facie case of racial discrimination under Batson. However, the court remanded the cause to the trial court to conduct a Batson hearing in order to determine whether the state improperly exercised its peremptory challenges to exclude women from the petit jury.

 

788 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Fisher


No. 5-92-0403


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


259 Ill. App. 3d 445; 632 N.E.2d 689; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 534; 198 Ill. Dec. 359



April 15, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Pope County. No. 90-CF-10. Honorable Rodney C. Clutts, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Pope County (Illinois), which dismissed a charge of armed violence against defendant after a jury found him guilty of aggravated battery. A mistrial was declared concerning the armed violence and attempted first-degree murder charges. The court's dismissal of the armed violence charge was based on its reasoning that aggravated battery was a lesser included offense of armed violence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot a man and was charged with armed violence and aggravated battery. The jury was instructed that defendant could be found guilty of either, and the court later clarified that if the jury found defendant guilty only of aggravated battery, it should select only that form and sign it. The jury found defendant guilty of aggravated battery. The court declared a mistrial concerning the armed violence charge. Defendant filed a motion to have the court dismiss the latter charge. At first, the court denied the motion, and then dismissed the charge for armed violence reasoning that jeopardy had attached. The court affirmed holding that the double jeopardy clauses of the United States Constitution and Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. 1970, art. I, § 10, provided that no person could be twice put in jeopardy for the same offense. The court ruled that there was an implied acquittal of an offense where there was a guilty verdict on a lesser offense and silence as to the charged offense. The court concluded that aggravated battery was a lesser-included offense of armed violence, and therefore affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which dismissed the armed violence charge against defendant.

 

789 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Doe (In re Doe)


1-93-4322


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


260 Ill. App. 3d 392; 632 N.E.2d 326; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 501; 198 Ill. Dec. 267



April 5, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 5, 1994. The Name of this Case has been Corrected by the Court June 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Gary L. Brownfield, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee mother was 35 weeks pregnant. Medical doctors determined that the fetus was not receiving an adequate amount of oxygen. After the mother refused to undergo a cesarean section or to have labor induced, the state filed a petition for adjudication of wardship of the fetus, seeking to invoke jurisdiction of the Juvenile Court Act, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/1-1 et seq. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied the petition.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issue was whether an Illinois court could balance whatever rights a fetus may have had against the rights of a competent woman to refuse medical advice to obtain a cesarean section for the supposed benefit of her fetus. The state argued that the circuit court should have balanced the rights of the unborn, but viable fetus which was nearly at full term and which, if the uncontradicted expert testimony of the physicians had been accurate, would have been born dead or severely retarded if the mother delivered vaginally, against the right of the competent women to choose the type of medical care she deemed appropriate, based in part on personal religious considerations. After consideration, this court held that no such balancing should have been employed, and that a woman's competent choice to refuse medical treatment as invasive as a cesarean section during pregnancy had to be honored, even in circumstances where the choice could have been harmful to her fetus.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

People v. Thomas


1-89-1804


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


261 Ill. App. 3d 366; 633 N.E.2d 839; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 442; 199 Ill. Dec. 43



March 31, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 18, 1994. Released for Publication June 7, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable William Cousins, Jr. Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION REDUCED, SENTENCE VACATED, AND CAUSE REMANDED FOR A NEW SENTENCING HEARING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), for possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. Defendant argued that the state failed to prove his intent to deliver, that the circuit court erroneously failed to provide the jury with a transcript of defendant's testimony, and that he was denied a fair trial by the prosecutor's actions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested when an officer chased a fleeing suspect into a room where defendant was filling packets with cocaine. Defendant was indicted. Over contradictory testimony, defendant testified that he did not have a shotgun next to him when the police arrived. A jury convicted defendant of unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. Defendant appealed, and the court held that the state failed to prove the element of intent to deliver, but it did prove all the elements of unlawful possession. Accordingly, the court reduced defendant's conviction to unlawful possession of a controlled substance and vacated defendant's sentence, remanding for a new sentencing hearing. Evidence of intent to deliver was not proved. Defendant was not found possessing a combination of narcotics or any significant amount of money that could lead to an inference of such intent. No scales for weighing the narcotics were found. An amount of 5.5 grams of cocaine, by itself, did not give rise to an inference of intent to deliver. Questioning on the shotgun was irrelevant and inadmissible, but the error was not prejudicial, so defendant was not denied a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court reduced defendant's conviction from possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver to unlawful possession of a controlled substance, and it vacated and remanded defendant's sentence for a new sentencing hearing.

Hyde Park Medical Lab. v. Court of Claims


1-91-3886


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


259 Ill. App. 3d 889; 632 N.E.2d 307; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 493; 198 Ill. Dec. 248



March 31, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 5, 1994. Petition for Rehearing Denied June 14, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1159.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE ARTHUR L. DUNNE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff medical laboratory appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied a motion for reconsideration after the trial court held it had no power to review a decision of the court of claims and held in favor of defendants, the court of claims, the Department of Public Aid, and the Director of the Department of Public Aid.


OVERVIEW: The laboratory brought suit against defendants for unpaid invoices and instituted the action in the court of claims, which had exclusive jurisdiction of all claims against the state. The court of claims ordered payment of the invoices, but denied motions by the laboratory for pre-award interest and attorneys fees. The laboratory then filed a complaint in the trial court seeking a declaratory judgment, a writ of mandamus, and a writ of certiorari to compel the defendants, including the court of claims, to order payment of the interest and fees under the Prompt Payment Act, 30 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 540/1 et seq. (1992). On appeal, the court held that sovereign immunity barred the action against the defendants outside the court of claims because the laboratory failed to prove that the state's actions were in violation of statutory law since the provisions relied on by the laboratory were not retroactive. Thus, since the laboratory failed to show a clear right to relief, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in not issuing a writ of mandamus. Likewise, a writ of certiorari was inappropriate where the trial court lacked jurisdiction to review decisions of the court of claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the action because it was without jurisdiction to review the merits of a court of claims decision denying an award of interest and fees on a judgment in favor of the laboratory.

People v. Parker


No. 1-90-1239


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


260 Ill. App. 3d 942; 632 N.E.2d 214; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 455; 198 Ill. Dec. 155



March 30, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 5, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Christy Berkos, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, after a jury trial, convicted him of first-degree murder in the stabbing death of his son.


OVERVIEW: Defendant believed his son was involved in the drug trade. Earlier, defendant took cocaine belonging to his son, for which he was shot and wounded by his son. Later, his son, and the son's partners, confronted defendant regarding the son's beeper, which was allegedly stolen by defendant. A heated argument ensued. According to defendant, his son pulled a gun on him. At that moment, defendant stabbed his son. When the ambulance picked-up the son's body, more than one hour later, no gun was found. The court reversed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder, holding that the failure of defendant's counsel to request a jury instruction on provocation was erroneous. In so ruling, the court stated that, had such an instruction been given, the verdict would have been different. In remanding, the court stated that because the evidence was sufficient to support a first-degree murder conviction, a new trial was not violative of defendant's right against double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder and remanded the matter for a new trial.

People v. Heineman


No. 1-92-3424


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


260 Ill. App. 3d 476; 632 N.E.2d 270; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 480; 198 Ill. Dec. 211



March 30, 1994, Decided


NOTICE:

 [***1] Released for Publication May 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Paul J. Nealis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him, after his guilty plea, of reckless homicide and driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI). The trial court imposed a 10-year sentence for reckless homicide and a concurrent 3-year term for DUI.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's truck struck another vehicle, killing the sole occupant who was a wife and mother of three children. Defendant smelled of alcohol, his speech was unintelligible, and he failed sobriety tests. Defendant challenged his 10-year sentence for reckless homicide. He contended that the sentence constituted an impermissible double enhancement and resulted from the trial court's consideration of improper factors and bias. On appeal, the court affirmed his sentence. The statutorily mandated sentence for reckless homicide committed while under the influence of alcohol did not constitute impermissible double enhancement. The court concluded that the trial court properly considered appropriate factors in mitigation and aggravation. While the trial court noted the type and size of the vehicles, it did not appear to give undue weight to these factors. The trial court also recognized defendant's prior convictions for DUI and his problems with alcohol abuse. This was not improper and was not to be interpreted as bias since a defendant's demonstrated history of alcoholism was a factor to be considered in the sentencing determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence for reckless homicide.

Trombello v. United Airlines (In re Air Crash Disaster at Sioux City)


1-93-0241


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


259 Ill. App. 3d 231; 631 N.E.2d 1302; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 426; 197 Ill. Dec. 843



March 29, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 5, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Donald J. O'Brien, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, an airline and associated entities, sought review of an order entered in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granting plaintiffs' motion for voluntary dismissal of 23 consolidated cases arising from the crash of an aircraft.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, an airline and associated entities, challenged the trial court's order granting a motion for voluntary dismissal of 23 consolidated cases arising from the crash of an aircraft filed by plaintiffs to avoid discovery deadlines and cut-offs. The court ruled that plaintiffs had a right to voluntary dismiss the cases pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1009(a) (1992), as neither the supreme court nor legislature had identified discovery abuse as a basis for restricting the right to nonsuit. The court also ruled that the separation-of-powers clause of Ill. Const. art. II, § 1 was not violated because the voluntary dismissal statute, as applied, did not conflict with the supervisory authority of the supreme court, and ruled that plaintiffs were neither estopped from seeking, nor did they waive their right to seek, voluntary dismissal based on a statement of their lead counsel that they would not dismiss the case. The court determined that the trial court erred in refusing to hear and decide two motions for summary judgment filed prior to the motion for voluntary dismissal because it had discretion to hear dispositive motions that did not affect all parties and claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting the motion for voluntary dismissal of 23 consolidated cases arising from the crash of an aircraft, except with respect to two defendants who had filed motions for summary judgment prior to the filing of the motion for voluntary dismissal. The court reversed the order as to those two defendants and remanded with directions to the trial court to consider the summary judgment motions.

Purlee v. Liberty Mut. Fire Ins. Co.


NO. 5-92-0065 CONSOLIDATED


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


260 Ill. App. 3d 11; 631 N.E.2d 433; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 449; 197 Ill. Dec. 430



March 29, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 90-L-1712. Honorable P.J. O'Neill, Judge Presiding.

Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 90-L-1713. Honorable A. A. Matoesian, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 90-L-1712, Affirmed. No. 90-L-1713, Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured claimants sought review of orders of the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment to defendant insurer in plaintiffs' actions for breach of contract for refusing to make payment upon plaintiffs' underinsured motorist coverage claims.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff insured claimants filed actions against defendant insurer for breach of contract for refusing to make payment upon plaintiffs' underinsured motorist coverage claims. The trial court granted summary judgment to defendant on both claims, and the court affirmed the orders. The court held that the underinsured motorist coverage statute provided for reduction-type coverage, which put plaintiffs in the same position they would have occupied had the tortfeasor's liability insurance limits been the same as the underinsured motorist coverage limits purchased by plaintiffs. The court held that because the tortfeasor's liability insurance limits exceeded the underinsured motorist coverage limits the underinsured motorist coverage was inapplicable. The court held that the test for the equal protection violation was not whether plaintiffs suffered a hardship, but whether the statute treated similarly situated groups of persons equally, which the court found that it did. The court held that the statute did not violate due process or equal protection under the law. The court held plaintiffs had no viable claim for improper claims practice or breach of any duty to deal in good faith.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders granting summary judgment to defendant insurer in plaintiff insured claimants' actions for breach of contract for refusing to make payment upon plaintiffs' underinsured motorist coverage claims. The court held that the vehicle was not underinsured because the total sum available to cover liability of the tortfeasor was not less than the limits of the underinsured motorist policy.

People ex rel. Ryan v. Lujack Schierbrock Chevrolet Co.


No. 3-93-0362 (Consolidated with 3-93-0364)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


259 Ill. App. 3d 581; 630 N.E.2d 1346; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 395; 197 Ill. Dec. 222


December 8, 1993, Submitted  
March 25, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 25, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County, Illinois. No. 91 CH 43 (Consolidated with 91 MR 186). Honorable John M. Telleen Judge, Presiding



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, state and Illinois auto dealers, appealed from a summary judgment entered by the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois), which was in favor of defendant Iowa auto dealership. Plaintiffs alleged that the dealership's display at the airport violated the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 1-100 et seq. (1991); and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 5-102.1 (1991).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed complaints against the dealership alleging that its automobile display at the airport, which was located in Illinois, violated the Illinois Vehicle Code Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 1-100 et seq. (1991), because the dealership was not licensed as a new car dealer in Illinois. The dealership was located and incorporated in Iowa. The complaint also alleged violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 5-102.1 (1991), required Illinois licensed dealers to obtain a permit in order to participate in a trade show or exhibition. Summary judgment was entered in favor of the dealership, and the court affirmed on appeal. The dealership was not "selling" or "dealing" in new cars in Illinois. The display was simply an advertisement, and therefore, the dealership was not required to obtain a license of permit. Nor was the display an "exhibition" as part of a trade show or event.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment, which was entered in favor of the dealership. The court held that the dealership's display was an advertisement and not subject to permit and licensing requirements.

People v. Studley


NO. 4-93-0771


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


259 Ill. App. 3d 556; 631 N.E.2d 839; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 381; 197 Ill. Dec. 617



March 25, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 2, 1994. Petition for Appeal as a Matter of Right or Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 92T22835. Honorable Jeffrey B. Ford, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment on a jury verdict of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) that convicted him of a violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-505 (1991), which outlawed screeching of tires. Defendant contended that the trial court erred when it applied the statute to a nonmoving vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stopped his car in traffic and made the rear tires screech, while a state trooper watched. Defendant said his foot slipped off the clutch. Defendant claimed that the language of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-505 (1991), prohibiting squealing and screeching of tires, pertained only to a moving vehicle. He based this conclusion on the section's placement within the Vehicle Code following the offenses of reckless driving and drag racing and preceding the general speed restrictions, which he argued showed a legislative intent to prohibit hazardous speeds and movement of vehicles, rather than merely noise. He also claimed that rapid acceleration or excessive speed around corners referred only to a moving vehicle. In response to defendant's motion for a directed verdict, the trial court concluded that the language "rapid acceleration" applied to acceleration of the engine and the tires, as well as the vehicle. The court concluded that rapid acceleration that caused squealing or screeching of tires did not require any movement of the vehicle.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for screeching of tires was affirmed.

 

798 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wilkenson


No. 1-92-3177


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


262 Ill. App. 3d 869; 635 N.E.2d 463; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 373; 200 Ill. Dec. 124



March 23, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 14, 1994. Released for Publication July 14, 1994. Second Corrected August 3, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable William P. O'Malley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decisions from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of endangering the life or health of a child pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/4 (1992) and denied defendant's motions to dismiss the complaint and for arrest of judgment. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statute and the sufficiency of the evidence, and she contended that the complaint was insufficiently drafted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after she was found holding a knife to her baby's throat, screaming that she had to kill the baby. The baby was unharmed. The appellate court affirmed. The sufficiency of a complaint was judged according to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 5/111-3 (1992). Mere technical violations were disregarded. The complaint was judged according to its plain and ordinary meaning. The complaint was sufficiently drafted to apprise defendant of the conduct and charges for which she could prepare a defense. Evidence of the child's age and the fact that defendant had her care was admitted. Actual physical harm was not required for a conviction under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 150/4 (1992). Endangering a child meant placing her in danger of probable harm. Any contradictions in the police officers' testimony went to credibility, which was for the trier of fact. Section 150/4 was not void for vagueness. The fact that there could have been borderline cases where a person was convicted for disciplining a child harshly did not render the statute unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for endangering the life or health of a child and the denial of motions to dismiss and for arrest of judgment were affirmed.
