McMichael v. Michael Reese Health Plan Found.


No. 1-92-3898


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


259 Ill. App. 3d 113; 631 N.E.2d 317; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 315; 197 Ill. Dec. 314



March 11, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 19, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE JOSEPH N. CASCIATO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: DISMISSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an interlocutory appeal, defendant health plan foundation challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied the foundation's motion to dismiss plaintiff estate administrator's complaint alleging medical malpractice. The foundation based its motion on the Voluntary Health Services Plans Act (VHSPA), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 32, para. 620 (1987).


OVERVIEW: The administrator brought a medical malpractice action against the foundation on behalf of the estate of the deceased. The foundation sought to dismiss the complaint on the ground that it was immune from liability under § 26 of the VHSPA. When the motion was denied, the foundation was allowed an interlocutory appeal to determine whether a 1988 amendment to § 26, which revoked the immunity previously granted to all VHSPA corporations except one, was unconstitutional because it constituted special legislation. The court dismissed the appeal, holding that the resolution of that question would not affect the foundation's interests in any way and therefore would not materially advance the litigation in the case. In amending the VHSPA, the legislature intended that no health maintenance organization (HMO) be entitled to immunity. A single exception was made for one HMO because it was the only health service plan that the legislature felt still conformed to the original concept of the VHSPA. In light of this, the foundation's premise that it was entitled to the same protection as the exempted HMO because it was the same type of organization was flawed.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the foundation's interlocutory appeal from the order denying its motion to dismiss the administrator's medical malpractice complaint.

 

800 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wenger


1-92-4322


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


258 Ill. App. 3d 561; 631 N.E.2d 277; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 288; 197 Ill. Dec. 274



March 8, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 19, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Ronald J.P. Banks, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of child abduction in violation of § 10-5(b)(10) of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-5(b)(10) (1991) (now 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/10-5(b)(10) (1992)).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with child abduction for allegedly attempting to lure a child under the age of 16 into his vehicle without parental consent for other than a lawful purpose. On appeal of his conviction, the court reversed. The court found that the evidence did not establish that defendant was following the child. The only evidence that went to the element of attempted luring was the child's testimony that defendant waved to her to come toward him from his parked vehicle. According to the child, defendant never said anything to her. The child testified that after defendant waved to her she turned her bicycle and rode away. The court held that without some affirmative conduct evidencing an intent to lure the child into defendant's vehicle, the innocuous gesture of waving was insufficient to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was attempting to lure the child into his vehicle.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment convicting defendant of child abduction.
